\begin{document}

\maketitle

\begin{abstract}
For \(X=K3\times E\) the theorem-level physical input used here is the
protected index.  Right-moving localization in the K3 Ramond sector gives
\[
Z_{\mathrm{K3}}=2\phi_{0,1},\qquad
\phi_{0,1}=\sum f(n,l)q^nr^l.
\]
Replacing the protected K3 index by its Borcherds half produces only a
virtual \(K_0\)-determinant package.  It does not produce a microscopic
Hilbert space.  Unitarity is used to localize the right-moving K3
supertrace before the index is taken; the index itself is a charge-graded
virtual object that no longer requires Hilbert positivity.  For virtual super vector spaces
\(\mathbb U_{n,l}\) with \(\sdim\mathbb U_{n,l}=f(n,l)\), set
\(\mathcal V_{(n,l,m)}=\mathbb U_{nm,l}\).  In the Borcherds cusp
chamber the determinant is
\[
\mathcal D_X(Z)
=64q^{1/2}r^{1/2}s^{1/2}
\prod_{(n,l,m)\in\Gamma_{\mathrm{eff}}}
(1-q^nr^ls^m)^{f(nm,l)}
=\Delta_5(Z).
\]
The constant \(64\) is the theta-constant normalization
\([q^{1/2}r^{1/2}s^{1/2}]\Delta_5=64\); hence the monic Borcherds
product is \(D_5=64^{-1}\Delta_5\).

The same coefficients are the signed root supermultiplicities in the
Gritsenko--Nikulin Borcherds--Kac--Moody denominator algebra.  Under
\[
\alpha(n,l,m)=2nf_2-lf_3+2mf_{-2}
\]
one has
\[
\operatorname{den}(\mathfrak g_{\Delta_5})
=64^{-1}\Delta_5(2Z),\qquad
\smult\mathfrak g_{\Delta_5,\alpha(n,l,m)}=f(nm,l)
\]
on the active support.  Thus the denominator algebra supplies the
algebraic square root target and its target-internal Borcherds bracket.
It does not supply a compact BPS Hilbert space, compact Hall
correspondences, an orientation, or a BPS operator product/local
collision map.

The square root in the title is meant in Dirac's sense.  The scalar
OP/DT branch \(Z^X_{\mathrm{OP/DT}}=-4096\,\Delta_5^{-2}\) is
orientation-forgetful: the sign character is squared away.  The
recognition target is a first-order protected operator/algebra
\(\mathfrak D_X\) with protected Pfaffian
\(\mathrm{Pf}_{\mathrm{prot}}(\mathfrak D_X)=\Delta_5\) and scalar trace
\(\operatorname{Tr}_{\mathrm{prot}}((-1)^F\mathfrak D_X^{-2})
=-4096\,\Delta_5^{-2}\); the orientation/Pfaffian datum is the
algebraic input that distinguishes \(\Delta_5\) from \(-\Delta_5\) and
that the squared scalar cannot recover.  Constructing
\(\mathfrak D_X\) is the open recognition problem; this paper formulates
the target and the orientation-character constraint
\(\varepsilon_o=\nu_{\Delta_5}\) on
\(W^{(2)}(\Lambda_{II}^{2,1})\).

The scalar Behrend-weighted branch is imported from
Oberdieck--Pixton, Oberdieck--Pandharipande, and Oberdieck.  In OP's
normalization \(\chi_{10}^{\mathrm{OP}}=D_5^2\), so
\[
\chi_{10}^{\mathrm{OP}}=(64^{-1}\Delta_5)^2
=4096^{-1}\Delta_5^2,\qquad
Z^X_{\mathrm{DT}}=Z^X_{\mathrm{OP}}
=-\left(\chi_{10}^{\mathrm{OP}}\right)^{-1}
=-4096\,\Delta_5^{-2}.
\]
The factor \(4096=64^2\) is a normalization conversion; the minus sign is
the OP scalar convention.  Neither fixes the automorphic reflection
character or the compact orientation monodromy.

A compact realization would have to begin with an additive physical
charge lattice \(\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}\), the Gram map
\(\Pi_X:\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}\to\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}}\), and a
holomorphic \(E_3\)-factorization algebra on \(K3\times E\), with a
specified formality point, \(S^3\)-framing, quantum master equation,
anomaly control, descent, and finite-first HN completion.  It would then
specialize along the K3 direction to a chiral object on
\(\operatorname{Ran}(E)\), solve the
\(\operatorname{Ran}(E)\)-support-locality obstruction in the
K3-integrated chiral shadow by mixed local/wrapped correspondences, and
identify the Gram-descended protected primitive bracket with
\(\mathfrak g_{\Delta_5}\).  This paper proves the virtual
determinant, records the imported scalar and denominator theorems, and
formulates that compact Hall/factorization realization as an open
recognition problem.  The final part records the eight Clery--Gritsenko
diagonal-divisor rows and the certificate required before any boundary
row becomes a physical host.
\end{abstract}

\bigskip
\tableofcontents

\section{Introduction and claim strength}
\label{sec:introduction-claim-strength}

The local object comes first.  A compact BPS theory on
\(X=K3\times E\), if it exists in the form needed here, should produce
protected local observables before any trace is taken.  After twisting
and passing to the protected index, the positive Hilbert space has
collapsed to a charge-graded virtual object, but locality has not
disappeared: disjoint insertions must still factorize and collisions
must remember extensions.

Thus the natural order is
\[
\begin{gathered}
\hbox{protected locality}
\longrightarrow
\hbox{compact/hybrid factorization}
\longrightarrow
\hbox{primitive recognition}
\\
\longrightarrow
\hbox{Borcherds denominator}
\longrightarrow
\hbox{OP scalar square}
\longrightarrow
\hbox{eight-row host certificates}.
\end{gathered}
\]
\paragraph{Protected locality.}
The protected index is theorem-level.  Right-moving localization of the
unitary K3 sigma model gives
\[
Z_{\mathrm{K3}}=2\phi_{0,1},\qquad
\phi_{0,1}=\sum f(n,l)q^nr^l.
\]
The half-index used by the Borcherds lift is represented only in
\(K_0(\mathrm{sVect}_{\mathrm{fd}})\).  Its coefficients are signed
superdimensions, not dimensions of a constructed compact D-brane Hilbert
space.

\paragraph{Compact and hybrid factorization.}
A compact realization would first supply the additive physical charge
lattice \(\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}\), the non-additive Gram map
\(\Pi_X:\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}\to\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}}\), and a
charge-completed holomorphic \(E_3\)-factorization algebra
\[
\mathcal A^{E_3}_X,\qquad X=K3\times E,
\]
then a chain-level K3-to-\(E\) specialization
\[
\mathcal F_X\simeq
\mathrm{Sp}^{\mathrm{ch}}_{K3,E}(\mathcal A^{E_3}_X)
\in\mathrm{Fact}(\operatorname{Ran}(E)).
\]
This is not reconstructed from the scalar partition function or from the
Borcherds product.  There is also a geometric obstruction: a
one-dimensional subscheme with positive elliptic degree projects onto
all of \(E\).  Hence a naive support-local object on
\(\operatorname{Ran}(E)\) sees only projection-finite sectors.  The full
Igusa \(s\)-direction requires hybrid local/global factorization for
wrapped \(E\)-sectors.  A separate global Hecke/Fock mode is only a
determinant-level repair unless it is coupled to the projection-finite
sector by mixed Hall actions and then tested at the primitive bracket
level.  This is open.

\paragraph{Primitive recognition.}
The microscopic algebra sought from such a compact realization is first
the upstairs protected primitive bracket
\[
[\ ,\ ]:\Prim_{c}^{\mathrm{prot}}(\mathcal F_X)
\otimes
\Prim_{c'}^{\mathrm{prot}}(\mathcal F_X)
\longrightarrow
\Prim_{c+c'}^{\mathrm{prot}}(\mathcal F_X),
\qquad c,c'\in\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}.
\]
The recognition certificate proved later is conditional: if the compact
Igusa datum \(\mathfrak K_X\) exists, including the oriented Hall object,
protected integration, Gram descent \(\Pi_{X,*}\), chiral bar-cobar
comparison, presentation-level primitive Lie comparison, no-extra-relations
theorem, completed PBW compatibility, and radical quotient, then
\[
H^0\Prim_{\mathrm{prot}}(\Pi_{X,*}\mathcal F_X)
\cong
\mathfrak g_{\Delta_5}
\]
and the chiral cobar object is the formal current envelope
\(\mathsf{Den}_{\Delta_5,E}\).  This is a recognition criterion, not an
existence theorem.

\paragraph{Borcherds denominator.}
The target algebra is imported from the Borcherds--Gritsenko--Nikulin
construction.  With
\[
\alpha(n,l,m)=2nf_2-lf_3+2mf_{-2},
\]
the visible active coefficients satisfy
\[
\smult\mathfrak g_{\Delta_5,\alpha(n,l,m)}=f(nm,l),\qquad
\operatorname{den}(\mathfrak g_{\Delta_5})=64^{-1}\Delta_5(2Z).
\]
This determines signed root supermultiplicities and the denominator
identity.  It does not determine compact Hall constants.

\paragraph{OP scalar square.}
The reduced scalar branch is imported from
Oberdieck--Pixton, Oberdieck--Pandharipande, and Oberdieck:
\[
Z^X_{\mathrm{DT}}(T,Q,P)=Z^X_{\mathrm{OP}}(P,Q,T)
=-4096\,\Delta_5(Z)^{-2}.
\]
The constants are fixed once.  The theta-constant form satisfies
\[
[q^{1/2}r^{1/2}s^{1/2}]\Delta_5=64,\qquad
D_5=64^{-1}\Delta_5.
\]
OP's monic product is \(\chi_{10}^{\mathrm{OP}}=D_5^2\), hence
\[
\chi_{10}^{\mathrm{OP}}=4096^{-1}\Delta_5^2,\qquad
Z^X_{\mathrm{OP}}=-(\chi_{10}^{\mathrm{OP}})^{-1}
=-4096\Delta_5^{-2}.
\]
The number \(64\) is a theta-leading coefficient.  The number
\(-4096\) is the OP scalar normalization.  Neither proves the compact
orientation character.  The comparison
\[
\epsilon_o=\nu_{\Delta_5}
\]
between geometric orientation monodromy and the automorphic reflection
character remains part of the open compact realization datum.

\paragraph{Eight-row host certificates.}
The diagonal-divisor boundary problem concerns the eight
Clery--Gritsenko forms
\[
\Delta_5,\Delta_2,\Delta_1,\Delta_{1/2},
\nabla_3,\nabla_2,\nabla_{3/2},Q_1 .
\]
Rows \(1\)--\(4\) have Gritsenko--Nikulin denominator theorems.  Rows
\(5\)--\(8\) have Clery--Gritsenko products and Govindarajan CHL/WKB
denominator theorems; \(F_7=\nabla_{3/2}\) is on the required
\(\mu_4\)-multiplier cover.  A physical host for any boundary row
requires a certificate fixing the modular group or cover, character,
divisor, cusp Jacobi inputs, product lattice, Weyl vector, real roots,
reflection character, physical charge lattice, protected Gram-index,
orientation, reduced scalar theorem if one is claimed, and
primitive algebra comparison.  Without that certificate the row is only
an automorphic product plus any separately proved denominator theorem.

\begin{center}
\small
\begin{tabular}{p{0.23\textwidth}p{0.25\textwidth}p{0.41\textwidth}}
\hline
Structural level & Claim strength & Content \\
\hline
Virtual determinant &
proved here from \(K_0\) data plus imported Borcherds product &
\(\mathcal D_X=\Delta_5\).  No canonical half-Hilbert space or operator
product is constructed. \\
Scalar Behrend square &
imported theorem &
Oberdieck--Pixton, Oberdieck--Pandharipande, and Oberdieck give
\(Z^X_{\mathrm{DT}}=Z^X_{\mathrm{OP}}=-4096\Delta_5^{-2}\) in the
reduced quotient-by-\(E\), Behrend-weighted setting. \\
BKM denominator &
imported theorem &
Gritsenko--Nikulin give \(\mathfrak g_{\Delta_5}\) and
\(\operatorname{den}(\mathfrak g_{\Delta_5})=64^{-1}\Delta_5(2Z)\). \\
Compact Hall/factorization realization &
conditional/open &
If \(\mathfrak K_X\) exists, the primitive and chiral comparisons follow
by the recognition criterion.  Existence, \(\operatorname{Ran}(E)\)
hybrid locality,
protected integration, and orientation monodromy are open. \\
Eight-row host certificates &
framework; mostly open &
The catalogue and denominator rows are imported where cited.  Physical
row maps and scalar squares require row-by-row certificates. \\
\hline
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

All super vector spaces in the representation-theoretic constructions
are over \(\C\).  Real vector spaces occur only after tensoring
lattices with \(\R\) to discuss cones, chambers, and period domains.
Products may be written over \(\Gamma_{\mathrm{eff}}\); the active
factors are exactly the triples in \(\Gamma_{\mathrm{act}}\), where
the exponent \(f(nm,l)\) is non-zero.

\part{\texorpdfstring{The \(N=1\) Igusa square root}
{The N=1 Igusa square root}}

\section{The physical question}
\label{sec:physical-question}

A charged BPS state is not, in the first instance, a local field.  It
lies in a superselection sector.  Its charge is measured at infinity,
and its existence depends on a stability chamber.  Thus the ordinary
local operator algebra of an untwisted four-dimensional theory is not
the primary object of this paper.

At the level of the protected index the situation is different.  After
taking the cohomology of the chosen supercharge, long multiplets cancel.
The object which remains is a charge-graded virtual object,
not a positive Hilbert space, whose Euler characteristic is stable under
deformation.  The index remembers the cancellation law of a unitary
theory, not its positive inner product.

For \(X=K3\times E\) the expected local object in a compact realization
is a supplied holomorphic \(E_3\)-factorization algebra
$$
\mathcal A^{E_3}_X,\qquad X=K3\times E.
$$
The auxiliary notation \(\Phi^{\mathrm{FA}}_3(X)\), when used, is only a
placeholder for this source datum; no such functor is constructed in
this paper.  No external \(\Phi^{\mathrm{FA}}_3\) formalism is used here
as an existence theorem unless it supplies the chain-level local
observables, factorization maps, descent, anomaly/QME control, and
compact charge completion required below.  In a compact realization
\(\mathcal A^{E_3}_X\) is the object whose disjoint holomorphic
insertions factorize.  The elliptic curve \(E\) enters only after a
supplied chain-level \(K3\)-specialization whose output is denoted
$$
\mathcal F_X\in\mathrm{Fact}(\operatorname{Ran}(E)).
$$
This is the first compact-realization obstruction.  The
projection-finite sector, where \(p_E(\operatorname{Supp}A)\) is a finite
subset of \(E\), is naturally local on \(\operatorname{Ran}(E)\).  A
one-dimensional sector of positive elliptic degree is not.  If
\(C\subset K3\times E\) has positive elliptic degree, then
\((p_E)_*[C]\) is a positive multiple of \([E]\); hence \(p_E(C)\) is a
one-dimensional closed subset of the irreducible curve \(E\), and so
\(p_E(C)=E\).  Such a class is wrapped or global over \(E\), not
localized at finitely many points of \(E\).

This is the \(\operatorname{Ran}(E)\)-support-locality obstruction in
the K3-integrated chiral shadow.  Naive support-local factorization on
\(\operatorname{Ran}(E)\) sees projection-finite sectors, but by itself
it misses the positive \(s\)-direction of the Igusa product, the
direction which records elliptic degree after the OP/Borcherds variable
conversion.  A compact realization must therefore choose at least one
repair of the following kind: projection-finite local factorization
together with separate global Fock/Hecke modes for the wrapped
elliptic-degree sector, or a hybrid local/global wrapped factorization
theory.  This is a realization obstruction.  It is not a defect in the
Borcherds determinant or in the Gritsenko--Nikulin denominator identity.

Thus, in a realization, the curve-level rule is not imposed externally.
It is the one-dimensional chiral shadow of the holomorphic
\(E_3\)-observable: well-separated protected insertions on \(E\)
multiply, while collisions remember extension and bound-state data.  In
primitive form this is the expected bracket
$$
[\ ,\ ]:
\Prim_{c}^{\mathrm{prot}}(\mathcal F_X)
\otimes
\Prim_{c'}^{\mathrm{prot}}(\mathcal F_X)
\longrightarrow
\Prim_{c+c'}^{\mathrm{prot}}(\mathcal F_X),
\qquad c,c'\in\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}.
$$

The Igusa square-root problem is to construct or recognize this
primitive protected algebra and its Gram descent.  The determinant below
gives the decategorified signed Gram-index shadow that such a realization
would have:
$$
\sdim\Prim_{\gamma}^{\mathrm{prot}}(\Pi_{X,*}\mathcal F_X)
=f(nm,l),
\qquad \gamma=(n,l,m).
$$
The Borcherds--Kac--Moody denominator algebra gives the algebraic
candidate:
$$
H^0\Prim_{\mathrm{prot}}(\Pi_{X,*}\mathcal F_X)
\stackrel{?}{\cong}
\mathfrak g_{\Delta_5}.
$$
The theorem-level content of the paper is the determinant and
denominator comparison.  The displayed isomorphism is the compact
\(E_3\)/Hall/chiral realization problem.

The square root is therefore not an analytic ambiguity in
\(\Delta_5^2\).  It is the normalized automorphic determinant of the
virtual protected one-particle index.  The scalar square forgets the
automorphic reflection character; a compact Hall orientation realizing
that character is part of the open datum.

\subsection*{Schema of the local protected observable algebra}
\label{sec:local-protected-observable-algebra}

\begin{definition}[Local protected observable algebra; proposal-only schema]
\label{def:local-protected-observable-algebra}
For an open \(U\subset X=K3\times E\), let
\(\mathfrak M_c(U)\) denote the derived moduli stack of compactly
supported B-branes on \(U\) of physical Mukai charge
\(c\in\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}=\La_S\oplus\La_S\), in the sense of
Pantev--Toen--Vaquie--Vezzosi \cite{PTVV2013}, so that
\(\mathfrak M_c(U)\) carries a \((-1)\)-shifted symplectic structure;
let \(\Phi_c\) denote the perverse sheaf of vanishing cycles of any
local d-critical chart, in the sense of
Brav--Bussi--Dupont--Joyce--Szendroi \cite{BBDJS2015} (BPS sheaf, alias
DT sheaf), well defined globally as a pre-D-critical structure on
\(\mathfrak M_c(U)\); let \(o_c\) denote the orientation line, a
square root of the determinant line of the cotangent complex of
\(\mathfrak M_c(U)\), supplied as part of the Hall datum.  The
\emph{local protected observable algebra of \(X\) on \(U\)} is the
proposal
\[
\mathcal A_X(U)
:=\bigoplus_{c\in\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}}
H_*^{\mathrm{BM}}\!\bigl(\mathfrak M_c(U),\,
\Phi_c\otimes o_c\bigr),
\]
graded by physical charge.  For disjoint
\(U_1,\ldots,U_k\subset X\), the proposed factorization map is
\[
\mathcal A_X(U_1)\otimes\cdots\otimes\mathcal A_X(U_k)
\longrightarrow
\mathcal A_X(U_1\sqcup\cdots\sqcup U_k),
\]
defined chain-level by Massey--Saito Thom--Sebastiani for vanishing
cycles
\[
\Phi_{F_1\oplus\cdots\oplus F_k}\simeq
\Phi_{F_1}\boxtimes\cdots\boxtimes\Phi_{F_k}
\]
on disjoint d-critical charts, together with the Ext-vanishing
\(\operatorname{Ext}^*(\mathcal F,\mathcal G)=0\) for branes
\(\mathcal F,\mathcal G\) with disjoint supports.  This is the
proposed compact \(E_3\) source \(\mathcal A^{E_3}_X\) of the present
paper, in the sense that its disjoint-supports factorization on opens
of \(X=K3\times E\) is the holomorphic \(E_3\)-factorization datum.
\end{definition}

\begin{remark}
The components are external assumptions:
PTVV \((-1)\)-shifted symplectic structure on derived moduli of
B-branes \cite{PTVV2013}; BBDJS vanishing-cycle perverse sheaf and its
Thom--Sebastiani isomorphism (extending Massey 2001 and Saito 1990 to
the d-critical setting) \cite{BBDJS2015}; orientation lines from the
Joyce--Upmeier orientation theory \cite{JoyceUpmeier} or
Kontsevich--Soibelman \cite{KSCoHA}.  The factorization map relies on
disjoint-supports Ext-vanishing for compactly supported branes
(absent for non-compact supports, where one recovers chiral algebra
structure, not commutative factorization).  Compactness on
\(K3\times E\) is open because the relevant moduli of branes are
typically non-quasicompact in \(\La_S\)-charge; the sectorial
truncation of
Proposition~\ref{prop:sectorial-hall-truncation} is the candidate
truncation.
\end{remark}

\section{The one-particle index and its determinant}

For the determinant calculation set
$$
Z=\begin{pmatrix}z_1&z_2\\z_2&z_3\end{pmatrix},\qquad
q=e^{2\pi iz_1},\qquad r=e^{2\pi iz_2},\qquad s=e^{2\pi iz_3}.
$$
The Gram-index lattice is
$$
\Gamma_{\mathrm{ind}}=\Z^3,\qquad
\gamma=(n,l,m),\qquad x^\gamma=q^nr^ls^m.
$$
The standard cusp polarization is the ordered limit
$$0<|s|\ll |q|\ll |r|^{-1}\ll1.$$
It determines the semigroup
$$
\Gamma_{\mathrm{eff}}
=\{(n,l,m)\mid m>0,\ n\geq0,\ l\in\Z\}
\cup\{(n,l,0)\mid n>0,\ l\in\Z\}
\cup\{(0,l,0)\mid l<0\}.
$$
\(m>0\) is positive because \(s\) is the smallest parameter; if
\(m=0\), then \(n>0\) is positive because \(q\) is next; if \(m=n=0\),
positivity is \(l<0\) because \(|r|^{-1}\ll1\).  This is a chamber
convention for the completed product, not a microscopic charge
positivity statement.

\begin{definition}[Ramond-sector K3 index and its half]
Let $\mathcal H_{\mathrm{RR}}(S)$ be the Ramond--Ramond Hilbert space of
a unitary $\mathcal N=(4,4)$ sigma model on a K3 surface $S$.  Its
central charges are
$$c=\overline c=6.$$
This Hilbert space is a supplied worldsheet input for the protected K3
index.  It is not a construction of the compact \(K3\times E\)
D-brane Hilbert space.
Choose a right-moving Ramond supercharge $Q_R$ with
$$Q_R^2=0,\qquad
\{Q_R,Q_R^\dagger\}=
2\left(\overline L_0-\frac{\overline c}{24}\right).$$
The K3 elliptic genus is the protected supertrace
$$
Z_{\mathrm{K3}}(\tau,z)=
\operatorname{Tr}_{\mathcal H_{\mathrm{RR}}(S)}
(-1)^{F_L+F_R}q^{L_0-c/24}
\overline q^{\,\overline L_0-\overline c/24}r^{J_0}.
$$
The BPS space in degree $(n,l)$ is
$$
\mathcal H^{\mathrm{BPS}}_{n,l}(S):=
H^\bullet\!\left(
\{\psi\mid (L_0-c/24)\psi=n\psi,\ J_0\psi=l\psi\},Q_R
\right).
$$
\end{definition}

\begin{lemma}[Right-moving localization]
Then
$$
Z_{\mathrm{K3}}(\tau,z)=
\sum_{n\geq0,\;l\in\Z}
\sdim\mathcal H^{\mathrm{BPS}}_{n,l}(S)q^nr^l.
$$
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
If $\overline L_0-\overline c/24>0$, the displayed anticommutator pairs
states with opposite $(-1)^{F_R}$ parity.  Their supertrace cancels.
The unpaired states are the $Q_R$-harmonic representatives, hence the
graded superdimension of $Q_R$-cohomology gives the elliptic genus.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Where unitarity enters]
Unitarity is used here before the index is taken: it gives the adjoint
relation which pairs positive right-moving energy states and makes the
supertrace localize.  After passing to the protected index, the object is
virtual.  A coefficient \(f(n,l)\) is a superdimension, not a positive
dimension.  Negative coefficients record an odd excess in the protected
supertrace, or in the chosen \(K_0\)-representative.  They do not
determine the two parity dimensions without an additional Hilbert-space
or denominator-algebra parity datum.
\end{remark}

\begin{definition}[Grothendieck half-index representative]
Eichler--Zagier normalization \cite{EZ:1}:
$$Z_{\mathrm{K3}}(\tau,z)=2\phi_{0,1}(\tau,z),$$
$$\phi_{0,1}(\tau,z)
=\sum_{n\geq 0,\;l\in\Z}f(n,l)q^nr^l.$$
Thus
$$\sdim\mathcal H^{\mathrm{BPS}}_{n,l}(S)=2f(n,l).$$
The arbitrary Grothendieck representative
$$\mathbb U_{n,l}\in K_0(\mathrm{sVect}_{\mathrm{fd}}),
\qquad \sdim\mathbb U_{n,l}=f(n,l),$$
is the normalized half-index class used by the Borcherds lift.  It is
not asserted to be a canonical half of
$\mathcal H^{\mathrm{BPS}}_{n,l}(S)$ as a Hilbert space.
As a \(K_0\)-model one may take \(\mathbb U_{n,l}\) to be
\(\C_{\overline0}^{f(n,l)}\) when \(f(n,l)\ge0\), and
\(\C_{\overline1}^{-f(n,l)}\) when \(f(n,l)<0\).  No canonical choice of
basis, parity lift, or operator product is implied.
$$\phi_{0,1}=r^{-1}+10+r+O(q),\qquad
\frac{f(0,0)}{2}=5.$$
\end{definition}

\begin{lemma}[Fock trace and superdeterminant]
Let
$$V=\bigoplus_{\lambda\in P}V_\lambda$$
be a $P$-graded super vector space with finite-dimensional homogeneous
pieces and let $a_\lambda=\sdim V_\lambda$.  Put
$$\mathcal F(V)=\operatorname{Sym}(V_{\overline 0})
\otimes \bigwedge(V_{\overline 1}).$$
As a formal character,
$$\sch\mathcal F(V):=
\sum_{\mu\in P}\sdim\mathcal F(V)_\mu\,x^\mu
=\prod_{\lambda\in P}(1-x^\lambda)^{-a_\lambda}.$$
The inverse character is the superdeterminant
$$\sdet_V(1-x)=\prod_{\lambda\in P}(1-x^\lambda)^{a_\lambda}.$$
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
$$V_\lambda=\C_{\overline0}:\qquad
\sch\operatorname{Sym}(V_\lambda)=(1-x^\lambda)^{-1}.$$
$$V_\lambda=\C_{\overline1}:\qquad
\sch\bigwedge(V_\lambda)=1-x^\lambda.$$
Tensor product over a homogeneous basis proves the product.
\end{proof}

When \(P=\Gamma_{\mathrm{eff}}\), all products below are taken in the
cusp-completed semigroup algebra determined by
\(0<|s|\ll |q|\ll |r|^{-1}\ll1\).  Every coefficient receives only
finitely many contributions in this completion.

$$x^{(n,l,m)}=q^nr^ls^m.$$
Form now the virtual Borcherds determinant package.  The third index
\(m\) is the second-quantized/Borcherds degree.  The positive \(m\)
sector carries the Hecke--DMVV exponents \(f(nm,l)\).  The \(m=0\)
sector is a cusp/Weyl boundary package carrying the repeated boundary
indices \(f(0,l)\).  Neither sector is a microscopic one-particle Hilbert
space.
\[
\mathcal V^{\mathrm{bulk}}
:=\bigoplus_{\substack{(n,l,m)\in\Gamma_{\mathrm{eff}}\\m>0}}
\mathbb U_{nm,l},
\qquad
\mathcal V^{\mathrm{cusp}}
:=\bigoplus_{\substack{(n,l,0)\in\Gamma_{\mathrm{eff}}}}
\mathbb U_{0,l}.
\]
\[
\mathcal V=\mathcal V^{\mathrm{bulk}}\oplus\mathcal V^{\mathrm{cusp}},
\qquad
\mathcal V_{(n,l,m)}=\mathcal V_{n,l,m}:=\mathbb U_{nm,l},\qquad
\sdim\mathcal V_{n,l,m}=f(nm,l).
\]
This is a definition in \(K_0\), not a microscopic state space.  The
\(m>0\) sector is the \(K_0\)-level virtual half of the DMVV product
\cite{DMVV}, obtained by replacing
\(Z_{\mathrm{K3}}=2\phi_{0,1}\) by \(\phi_{0,1}\).  The normalized Fock
character in the Borcherds chamber is
$$\sch\mathcal F(\mathcal V)
=\prod_{\gamma\in\Gamma_{\mathrm{eff}}}(1-x^\gamma)^{-\sdim\mathcal V_\gamma}
=\prod_{(n,l,m)\in\Gamma_{\mathrm{eff}}}
(1-q^nr^ls^m)^{-f(nm,l)}.$$
$$\sdet_{\mathcal V}(1-x)
=\prod_{\gamma\in\Gamma_{\mathrm{eff}}}(1-x^\gamma)^{\sdim\mathcal V_\gamma}
=\prod_{(n,l,m)\in\Gamma_{\mathrm{eff}}}
(1-q^nr^ls^m)^{f(nm,l)}.$$
The sector $m>0$ is the normalized half of the second-quantized DMVV
index.  The terms with $m=0$ are cusp and Weyl-chamber boundary factors
of the Borcherds product; the determinant reads only their signed
indices $f(0,l)$.
The normalized cusp-form section below proves the leading coefficient
which fixes the Weyl monomial
$$v_0(Z)=64q^{1/2}r^{1/2}s^{1/2}.$$
$$v_0\notin\bigoplus_{\gamma\in\Gamma_{\mathrm{eff}}}\mathcal V_\gamma.$$

\begin{definition}[Normalized \(K_0\)-determinant]
$$\mathcal{D}_X(Z)
=v_0(Z)\sdet_{\mathcal V}(1-x)
=64q^{1/2}r^{1/2}s^{1/2}
\prod_{(n,l,m)\in\Gamma_{\mathrm{eff}}}
(1-q^nr^ls^m)^{f(nm,l)}.$$
$$\mathcal Z_{\mathrm{Borch}}^{\mathrm{vir}}(Z)
=\mathcal D_X(Z)^{-1}
=\frac{1}{64}q^{-1/2}r^{-1/2}s^{-1/2}
\prod_{(n,l,m)\in\Gamma_{\mathrm{eff}}}
(1-q^nr^ls^m)^{-f(nm,l)}.$$
The object constructed here is the virtual \(K_0\)-determinant; compact
BPS meaning is part of the separate realization problem.
\end{definition}

\begin{proposition}[Determinant normalization]
$$[q^{1/2}r^{1/2}s^{1/2}]\,\mathcal D_X=64,$$
$$\mathcal Z_{\mathrm{Borch}}^{\mathrm{vir}}
=\frac{1}{64}q^{-1/2}r^{-1/2}s^{-1/2}\sch\mathcal F(\mathcal V),$$
$$\mathcal D_X
=64q^{1/2}r^{1/2}s^{1/2}\sdet_{\mathcal V}(1-x).$$
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
$$\sch\mathcal F(\mathcal V)
=\prod_{(n,l,m)\in\Gamma_{\mathrm{eff}}}
(1-q^nr^ls^m)^{-f(nm,l)},\qquad
\sdet_{\mathcal V}(1-x)
=\prod_{(n,l,m)\in\Gamma_{\mathrm{eff}}}
(1-q^nr^ls^m)^{f(nm,l)}.$$
$$v_0(Z)\sdet_{\mathcal V}(1-x)=\mathcal D_X,\qquad
v_0(Z)^{-1}\sch\mathcal F(\mathcal V)
=\mathcal Z_{\mathrm{Borch}}^{\mathrm{vir}}.$$
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Virtuality of the square root]
\label{prop:virtuality-of-the-square-root}
The displayed construction produces a class
$$
[\mathcal V]\in
K_0(\Gamma_{\mathrm{eff}}\hbox{-graded finite-dimensional super vector spaces})
$$
together with its Fock determinant.  By itself this determinant does not
construct a Hilbert space, a vertex algebra, a holomorphic
\(E_3\)-factorization algebra, or a chiral factorization algebra whose
character is $\mathcal Z_{\mathrm{Borch}}^{\mathrm{vir}}$.

All denominator statements use only the equalities
$$\sdim\mathcal V_{(n,l,m)}=f(nm,l),\qquad
\mathcal D_X=v_0\sdet_{\mathcal V}(1-x).$$
The denominator algebra and formal current envelope are constructed
later from the Borcherds root datum, not from a canonical half of the K3
Hilbert space.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
By definition, $\mathcal V_{(n,l,m)}=\mathbb U_{nm,l}$ is specified only
through its class in $K_0(\mathrm{sVect}_{\mathrm{fd}})$ and through the
integer $\sdim\mathbb U_{nm,l}=f(nm,l)$.  The Fock trace and
superdeterminant lemma depends only on these signed dimensions.  No
operation in the construction supplies composition maps, operator
products, locality, or a Hilbert completion.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Dirac/Pfaffian recognition target]
\label{prop:dirac-pfaffian-recognition-target}
The class \([\mathcal V]\in K_0\) and its Fock determinant
\(\mathcal D_X=v_0\sdet_{\mathcal V}(1-x)=\Delta_5\) record signed
Gram-degree multiplicities and a formal infinite-product; they do not
produce an operator with a spectrum.  The structural upgrade demanded
by the protected-locality side of the constellation is an
\emph{open recognition target}:
\begin{quote}
construct on the compact \(K3\times E\) factorization datum of
Definition~\ref{def:compact-igusa-realization-datum} a first-order
protected operator/algebra
\(\mathbb D_X\) acting on a chiral protected module, whose
charge-graded Pfaffian satisfies
$$
\operatorname{Pf}_{\mathrm{prot}}(\mathbb D_X)
=\mathcal D_X=\Delta_5,
$$
and whose scalar trace, in the OP normalization of
Definition~\ref{def:op-normalization-branch} below, satisfies
$$
\operatorname{Tr}_{\mathrm{prot}}
\bigl((-1)^F(\mathbb D_X)^{-2}\bigr)
=-4096\,\Delta_5^{-2}.
$$
\end{quote}
Existence of \(\mathbb D_X\) is open; it would convert the \(K_0\)
identity of Proposition~\ref{prop:virtuality-of-the-square-root}
into a first-order protected statement.  The target carries the
sign-square ambiguity of
Conjecture~\ref{conj:protected-d-brane-index} and the orientation
monodromy of Open Problem~\ref{op:orientation-monodromy-character};
choosing a square root of \((\mathbb D_X)^{-2}\) requires the
orientation datum of that open problem and is not fixed by the OP
scalar.
\end{proposition}

\begin{theorem}[Dirac/Pfaffian recognition under \(K3\times E\) orientation existence]
\label{thm:dirac-pfaffian-recognition-conditional}
Suppose the following two data items are granted on the reduced compact
critical Hall/CoHA sector of \(X=K3\times E\) of
Definition~\ref{def:protected-hall-integration-criterion}.

\smallskip
\textup{(O1)} \emph{Strong multiplicative orientation datum.}  There
exists a Joyce--Upmeier-type orientation line \cite{JoyceUpmeier}
$$
o_{\mathcal C}\in\operatorname{Pic}(\mathfrak M^{or}_X),\qquad
o_{\mathcal C}^{\otimes 2}\;\simeq\;
\det\operatorname{RHom}(\mathcal C,\mathcal C),
$$
in the sense of Definition~\ref{def:orientation-line}, satisfying
$$
o_{\mathcal C\oplus\mathcal C'}
\;\simeq\;
o_{\mathcal C}\otimes o_{\mathcal C'}
\quad\text{compatibly with the extension correspondences},
$$
descending under the reduced \(E\)-quotient and lifting equivariantly
along the Weyl action transported by Gram-projection
\(\Pi:\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}\to\Gamma_{\mathrm{ind}}\).

\smallskip
\textup{(O1)\(^+\)} \emph{Weyl-equivariant cocycle extension.}  The
Weyl-equivariant lift of (O1) is a \(1\)-cocycle on
\(W^{(2)}(\La^{2,1}_{II})\) with values in \(\{\pm 1\}\), descending
to a sign character
\(\varepsilon_o:W^{(2)}(\La^{2,1}_{II})\to\{\pm 1\}\) (the orientation
monodromy character of
Open Problem~\ref{op:orientation-monodromy-character}).  Equivalently,
the restriction of the Joyce--Upmeier multiplicative orientation
cocycle \cite{JoyceUpmeier,JoyceTanakaUpmeier} to wall-reflection
generators is a homomorphism on all of \(W^{(2)}(\La^{2,1}_{II})\),
not merely on its Coxeter generators.

\smallskip
\textup{(O2)} \emph{Pfaffian local model on type-II walls.}  The
geometric reflection sign
$$
\varepsilon_o:W^{(2)}(\La^{2,1}_{II})\longrightarrow\{\pm1\}
$$
of Open Problem~\ref{op:orientation-monodromy-character} is computed,
on a simple type-II reflection \(s_\delta\), as the parity of the count
of oriented real normal modes of the orientation line at the wall
\(\Hpl_\delta\); equivalently, on a single oriented normal mode
\(s_\delta\) acts as \((-1)\) on the Pfaffian section and squares to the
identity on the determinant section.

\smallskip
Then:
\begin{enumerate}
\item[\textup{(i)}] (\emph{Pfaffian recognition.})  The recognition
target of Proposition~\ref{prop:dirac-pfaffian-recognition-target} is
realized.  There exists a first-order protected operator/algebra
\(\mathfrak D_X\) on the chiral protected module \(\mathcal A_X\) over
\(\Gamma_{\mathrm{eff}}\) whose graded Pfaffian section coincides with
the virtual determinant:
$$
\operatorname{Pf}_{\mathrm{prot}}(\mathfrak D_X)\;=\;\mathcal D_X\;=\;\Delta_5,
$$
and whose scalar trace, in the OP normalization of
Definition~\ref{def:op-normalization-branch}, satisfies
$$
\operatorname{Tr}_{\mathrm{prot}}\bigl((-1)^F\,\mathfrak D_X^{-2}\bigr)
\;=\;-4096\,\Delta_5^{-2}.
$$
\item[\textup{(ii)}] (\emph{Three-sign identification.})  For the three
type-II simple reflections \(\delta_i\) of the Weyl chamber
\(\Poly_{II}\) of Section~\textup{The Weyl chamber and the Weyl vector}
(notation \(\delta_1=2f_2-f_3\), \(\delta_2=2f_{-2}-f_3\),
\(\delta_3=f_3\)),
$$
\varepsilon_o(s_{\delta_i})\;=\;-1\;=\;\nu_{\Delta_5}(s_{\delta_i}),
\qquad i=1,2,3,
$$
and on the three \(\Aut(\Poly_{II})\simeq S_3\) chamber-permuting
reflections \(s_{f_{-2}-f_2},s_{f_2-f_3},s_{f_2+f_3}\),
$$
\varepsilon_o(s)\;=\;+1\;=\;\nu_{\Delta_5}(s).
$$
In particular,
$$
\varepsilon_o\big|_{W^{(2)}(\La^{2,1}_{II})}
\;=\;\nu_{\Delta_5}\big|_{W^{(2)}(\La^{2,1}_{II})}.
$$
\item[\textup{(iii)}] (\emph{Categorical upgrade.})  The virtual
\(K_0\)-determinant package \([\mathcal V]\), \(\mathcal D_X\) of
Proposition~\ref{prop:virtuality-of-the-square-root} is upgraded to
a chiral protected first-order theory whose decategorification is the
Borcherds product
$$
\operatorname{Pf}_{\mathrm{prot}}(\mathfrak D_X)\big|_{\mathfrak c_\infty}
=64\,q^{1/2}r^{1/2}s^{1/2}
\!\!\!\prod_{(n,l,m)\in\Gamma_{\mathrm{eff}}}\!\!
(1-q^nr^ls^m)^{f(nm,l)}=\Delta_5,
$$
and whose orientation monodromy character is the Maass character
\(\nu_{\Delta_5}\) restricted to \(W^{(2)}(\La^{2,1}_{II})\).
\end{enumerate}
\end{theorem}

Items (O1) and (O2) are open on the reduced \(K3\times E\) sector;
on Calabi--Yau threefolds (O1) is Joyce--Song \cite{JoyceSong},
the multiplicative orientation cocycle on
\(\mathrm{Perf}(X)\) is Joyce--Upmeier \cite{JoyceUpmeier} and
Joyce--Tanaka--Upmeier \cite{JoyceTanakaUpmeier}, on Calabi--Yau
fourfolds the unreduced orientation exists by Borisov--Joyce /
Cao--Gross--Joyce / Bojko--Borisov--Joyce
\cite{BorisovJoyce}, \cite{OhThomasI}, \cite{OhThomasII}, the rank-one
Pin\(^c\) lift on \(\mathrm{Hilb}^n(X)\) for smooth threefolds is
Cao--Kool--Monavari \cite{CaoKoolMonavari}, and further extensions to
non-compact and Joyce--Song settings are Liu \cite{LiuYalongOrientations}.
The cosection-induced parity flip
\(\mathrm{vd}^{\mathrm{red}}=\mathrm{vd}^{\mathrm{std}}+1\) of the
Maulik--Toda / Oberdieck reduced obstruction theory is absorbed into
(O1) as a \(\mathbb Z/2\)-grading shift
\(o^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C}=o^{\mathrm{std}}_{\mathcal C}\otimes\Pi\)
of the BBDJS \cite{BBDJS2015} line under cosection contraction of
the PTVV \cite{PTVV2013} \((-1)\)-shifted symplectic form by
\(\sigma_{K3}\) (clause (P4) of
Open Problem~\ref{op:orientation-monodromy-character}); the flip
sources the \((-1)^F\) sign in (i) and (iii) and pins the
Berezinian convention.

\begin{proof}[Proof of Theorem~\ref{thm:dirac-pfaffian-recognition-conditional}]

\emph{Step 1 (Pfaffian construction from (O1)).}
By Definition~\ref{def:orientation-line} the orientation line of a
stable charge-\(c\) object satisfies
\(o_{\mathcal C}^{\otimes 2}\simeq\det\operatorname{RHom}(\mathcal C,\mathcal C)\).
The hypothesis (O1) promotes this to an extension-multiplicative system:
on every direct sum \(\mathcal C\oplus\mathcal C'\),
\(o_{\mathcal C\oplus\mathcal C'}\simeq o_{\mathcal C}\otimes o_{\mathcal C'}\),
compatibly with the strict associators of the Hall extension stack and
descended under the reduced \(E\)-quotient.  The Pfaffian section
\(\operatorname{Pf}_{\mathrm{prot}}\) is then the canonical square-root section of
\(\det\operatorname{RHom}\) determined by \(o_{\mathcal C}\): it exists as a section
of \(o_{\mathcal C}\) precisely because (O1) supplies a global
trivialization of the squaring isomorphism, and it assembles, under the
multiplicative structure, into a charge-graded product over
\(\Gamma_{\mathrm{eff}}\) of single-mode Pfaffian factors.

Define \(\mathfrak D_X\) as the protected first-order operator on the
chiral protected module \(\mathcal A_X\) whose Berezinian/Pfaffian on
the charge-\((n,l,m)\) component is the canonical Pfaffian of the
graded Ext bundle \(\operatorname{Ext}^\bullet(\mathcal C_{(n,l,m)},\mathcal C_{(n,l,m)})\),
with sign normalized by the chosen \(o_{\mathcal C}\).  The graded
product collapses to
$$
\operatorname{Pf}_{\mathrm{prot}}(\mathfrak D_X)
=v_0\,\sdet_{\mathcal V}(1-x)
\quad\text{with}\quad v_0=64q^{1/2}r^{1/2}s^{1/2},
$$
where \(\sdet\) is the superdeterminant of
Proposition~\ref{prop:virtuality-of-the-square-root}; the key point is
that orientation data turns the formal \(\sdim\)-only superdeterminant
of that proposition into a section of the orientation line, not just a
formal infinite product in \(K_0(\mathrm{sVect}_{\mathrm{fd}})\).

\emph{Step 2 (Identification \(\operatorname{Pf}_{\mathrm{prot}}=\Delta_5\).)}
Proposition~\ref{prop:bgn-identification} (Borcherds--Gritsenko--Nikulin)
identifies \(v_0\,\sdet_{\mathcal V}(1-x)\) with the Igusa cusp form
\(\Delta_5\) at the level of Fourier coefficients.  Step~1 promotes
this from a formal product equality to an equality of Pfaffian
sections, since orientation data resolves the
\(\pm\)-ambiguity inherent in any abstract square root: the Borcherds
product comes with the sign convention \(c_\Delta(1,1,1)=64\) (positive
leading coefficient, Borcherds normalization), and the Pfaffian section
inherits the same sign on the unique top-cohomology generator of the
isotropic-cusp expansion of
Section~\textup{The normalized cusp form}.  Hence
\(\operatorname{Pf}_{\mathrm{prot}}(\mathfrak D_X)=\Delta_5\) as a section of
\(\mathcal L^5\otimes\nu_{\Delta_5}\).

\emph{Step 3 (Scalar square in OP normalization).}
Squaring forgets the orientation:
\(\bigl(\operatorname{Pf}_{\mathrm{prot}}(\mathfrak D_X)\bigr)^2
=\det\operatorname{RHom}(\mathcal C,\mathcal C)|_{\mathrm{tot}}=\Delta_5^2\), as
sections of \(\mathcal L^{10}\) (the squared automorphic line is the
trivially-charactered determinant, since
\(\Delta_5^2=\Delta_{10}\) is scalar by
Section~\textup{The normalized cusp form}).
The protected scalar trace is then
\(\operatorname{Tr}_{\mathrm{prot}}((-1)^F\mathfrak D_X^{-2})=C_X\,\Delta_5^{-2}\) for
some normalization scalar \(C_X\); the explicit \(C_X=-4096\) follows
from Proposition~\ref{prop:op-normalization} of Oberdieck--Pixton, which
gives
\(Z^X_{\mathrm{OP}}=-(\chi_{10}^{\mathrm{OP}})^{-1}=-4096\,\Delta_5^{-2}\),
together with the arithmetic \(-4096=-(64)^2\) of the squared
theta-leading coefficient and the OP scalar sign convention recorded in
Definition~\ref{def:op-normalization-branch}.

\emph{Step 4 (Orientation-character identity (ii)).}  By (O2), each
type-II simple reflection \(s_{\delta_i}\) acts on
\(o_{\mathcal C}\) by the parity of its count of oriented real normal
modes; by Lemma~\ref{lem:thm3-three-sign-computation} below, this count
is \(1\) for \(i=1,2,3\), giving \(\varepsilon_o(s_{\delta_i})=-1\).
The same lemma computes the
\(\Aut(\Poly_{II})\simeq S_3\) reflections to even normal-mode count,
giving \(\varepsilon_o=+1\) on those.  The displayed values match
Lemma~\ref{lem:maass-multiplier-restriction} on the same six elements.
The chamber decomposition
\(\Orth(\La^{2,1})_+
\simeq W^{(2)}(\La^{2,1}_{II})\rtimes\Aut(\Poly_{II})\) of
Section~\textup{The Weyl chamber and the Weyl vector} reduces the
character to its values on these six generators \emph{provided}
\(\varepsilon_o\) is a homomorphism on the infinite Coxeter
group \(W^{(2)}(\La^{2,1}_{II})\); this is exactly the strengthened
hypothesis (O1)\(^+\), supplied by
Lemma~\ref{lem:weyl-equivariant-orientation-cocycle} from (O1) plus the
\((\Z/2)^3\) abelianization of \(W^{(2)}(\La^{2,1}_{II})\).  Two
homomorphisms agreeing on a generating set agree, so
\(\varepsilon_o=\nu_{\Delta_5}\) on \(W^{(2)}(\La^{2,1}_{II})\).

\emph{Step 5 (Categorical upgrade (iii)).}  Steps 1--4 promote each
ingredient of Proposition~\ref{prop:virtuality-of-the-square-root}: the
class \([\mathcal V]\in K_0(\mathrm{sVect}_{\mathrm{fd}})\) lifts to the
\(o_{\mathcal C}\)-graded chiral module, the formal product
\(v_0\,\sdet_{\mathcal V}(1-x)\) lifts to the Pfaffian section
\(\operatorname{Pf}_{\mathrm{prot}}(\mathfrak D_X)\), and the formal
character-equality lifts to the orientation-character identity of (ii).
The decategorification of the chiral protected theory at the chosen
isotropic cusp \(\mathfrak c_\infty\) is the Borcherds product, and the
orientation monodromy character is \(\nu_{\Delta_5}\) on the type-II
Weyl group as computed.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Three-sign computation on the type-II simple walls]
\label{lem:thm3-three-sign-computation}
Under the Pfaffian local model (O2) of
Theorem~\ref{thm:dirac-pfaffian-recognition-conditional}, for each
\(\delta\in\{\delta_1,\delta_2,\delta_3\}\) the
orientation-monodromy reflection sign is
$$
\varepsilon_o(s_{\delta})\;=\;(-1)^{N_{\delta}}\;=\;-1,
$$
where \(N_\delta\) is the count of oriented real normal modes at the
wall \(\Hpl_\delta\), and for each
\(s\in\{s_{f_{-2}-f_2},s_{f_2-f_3},s_{f_2+f_3}\}\),
\(\varepsilon_o(s)=+1\).
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
\emph{Type-II simple walls.}  The three roots
\(\delta_1=2f_2-f_3\), \(\delta_2=2f_{-2}-f_3\), \(\delta_3=f_3\) have
Gram pairing
\((\delta_i,\delta_i)=2\), \((\delta_i,\delta_j)=-2\) for \(i\ne j\),
by the matrix displayed in
Section~\textup{The Weyl chamber and the Weyl vector}.  All three are
real simple roots of the Lorentzian Kac--Moody algebra
\(\autcor\): real because \(\langle\delta,\delta\rangle=+2>0\),
of multiplicity one because they appear in the simple-root data of the
Borcherds product (the only multiplicity-one positive support of
\(f(nm,l)\) consistent with the squared discriminant
\((\alpha(\gamma),\alpha(\gamma))=-2(4nm-l^2)\)).  In the Gram-index
chart of Definition~\ref{def:gram-index-degrees-weyl-chamber} (using
\(\alpha(\gamma)=2nf_2-lf_3+2mf_{-2}\)), the three simple walls
correspond to the lattice triples
$$
\delta_1\;\leftrightarrow\;(n,l,m)=(1,1,0),\qquad
\delta_2\;\leftrightarrow\;(0,1,1),\qquad
\delta_3\;\leftrightarrow\;(0,-1,0),
$$
matching the K3 elliptic-genus support
\(f(0,\pm1)=1\), \(f(0,0)=10\), \(f(nm,l)=0\) for \(4nm-l^2<-1\).
By Borcherds' product theorem, the Pfaffian section near
\(\Hpl_{\delta}\) factors as
$$
\operatorname{Pf}_{\mathrm{prot}}(\mathfrak D_X)
=u_\delta^{N_\delta}\cdot\hbox{(unit at \(\Hpl_\delta\))},
$$
where \(u_\delta=1-x^{\alpha(\delta)}\) is the local equation of the
wall.  The exponent \(N_\delta\) is the multiplicity of \(\delta\) as a
simple real root, i.e.\ \(N_\delta=f(nm,l)|_{\text{simple-root cell}}=1\)
for each of the three triples above.

By the Pfaffian local model (O2), an oriented real normal mode flips
the orientation line \(o_{\mathcal C}\) by \(-1\), squaring to the
trivial action on \(\det\operatorname{RHom}\).  Hence
$$
\varepsilon_o(s_{\delta_i})
=(-1)^{N_{\delta_i}}
=(-1)^{1}
=-1,\qquad i=1,2,3.
$$
The three rows of the explicit table:
\begin{center}
\small
\begin{tabular}{p{0.18\textwidth}p{0.32\textwidth}p{0.10\textwidth}p{0.07\textwidth}p{0.07\textwidth}}
\hline
\(\delta_i\) & wall geometry (charge label) & normal modes \(N_{\delta_i}\) & \(\varepsilon_o\) & \(\nu_{\Delta_5}\) \\
\hline
\(\delta_1=2f_2-f_3\) &
section + fibre + D0 collision: \((n,l,m)=(1,1,0)\); D2(section) wall & 1 & \(-1\) & \(-1\) \\
\(\delta_2=2f_{-2}-f_3\) &
fibre + section + D0 mirror leg under \(f_2\leftrightarrow f_{-2}\): \((0,1,1)\); D2(fibre) wall & 1 & \(-1\) & \(-1\) \\
\(\delta_3=f_3\) &
isotropic-cusp diagonal D6--D2 extension on the \(4nm-l^2=-1\) ray: \((0,-1,0)\) & 1 & \(-1\) & \(-1\) \\
\hline
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

\emph{The three \(\Aut(\Poly_{II})\simeq S_3\) reflections.}
The three chamber-permuting roots
\(\alpha_1=f_{-2}-f_2\), \(\alpha_2=f_2-f_3\), \(\alpha_3=f_2+f_3\)
all have squared norm \((\alpha_i,\alpha_i)=2\) by the Gram pairing
\((f_2,f_{-2})=-1\), \((f_3,f_3)=2\) of
Section~\textup{The Weyl chamber and the Weyl vector}.  They lie in
\(\La^{2,1}\setminus\La^{2,1}_{II}\) (type~I, not type~II), so they
do \emph{not} appear in the type-II simple-root system
\(\{\delta_1,\delta_2,\delta_3\}\) used by the Borcherds product
\cite[Theorem 2.1, Section~4]{GN}.  Compute the wall multiplicity
\(N_{\alpha}=\ord_{\Hpl_\alpha}(\Delta_5)\) directly via Borcherds'
divisor formula \cite[Section~4]{GN}, \cite{Gritsenko99}.

By Borcherds' theorem (specialized to \(\Delta_5\) in the type-II
parametrization \(\alpha(n,l,m)=2nf_2-lf_3+2mf_{-2}\) of
Definition~\ref{def:gram-index-degrees-weyl-chamber}, with K3
elliptic-genus coefficients \(f(n,l)\) of the weight-zero index-one
weak Jacobi form \(\phi_{0,1}\) \cite[\S2.2]{EZ:1}),
\[
N_{\alpha}\;=\;\ord_{\Hpl_\alpha}(\Delta_5)
\;=\;\sum_{k\ge1:\;\pm k\alpha=\alpha(\gamma_k),\,\gamma_k\in\Gamma_{\mathrm{eff}}}
f\bigl(n_k m_k,l_k\bigr),
\]
where \((n_k,l_k,m_k)\) is the unique triple realizing
\(\alpha(\gamma_k)=\pm k\alpha\) when one exists, and the sum is empty
otherwise.  Because the parametrization
\(\alpha(\gamma)=2nf_2-lf_3+2mf_{-2}\) requires the coefficients of
\(f_2\) and \(f_{-2}\) to be \emph{even}, only \(k\) with \(k\alpha\)
having even \(f_2\)- and \(f_{-2}\)-coefficients contribute.  The
table:
\begin{itemize}
\item[(i)] \(\alpha_1=f_{-2}-f_2\): the \(f_2\)- and
\(f_{-2}\)-coefficients are \(\mp1\), so \(k=1\) is excluded.  For
\(k=2\), \(2\alpha_1=2f_{-2}-2f_2\) gives \((n,l,m)=(-1,0,1)\); the
opposite orientation \(-2\alpha_1\) gives \((1,0,-1)\).  Neither lies
in \(\Gamma_{\mathrm{eff}}=\{n\ge0,m\ge0,n+m-l\ge0\}\) of
Lemma~\ref{lem:active-support-type-ii-cone}, since one of \(n,m\) is
negative.  All higher \(k\) inherit the same sign obstruction.  Hence
the sum is empty and \(N_{\alpha_1}=0\).
\item[(ii)] \(\alpha_2=f_2-f_3\): for \(k=1\), the \(f_2\)-coefficient
is odd, excluded.  For \(k=2\), \(2\alpha_2=2f_2-2f_3\) gives
\((n,l,m)=(1,2,0)\), with index value \(f(nm,l)=f(0,2)\).  By the
explicit Fourier expansion
\(\phi_{0,1}=\sum f(n,l)q^nr^l\) of \cite[\S2.2, Theorem~9.3 and
Table~p.~141]{EZ:1} (equivalently, the K3 elliptic-genus normalization
\(Z_{\mathrm{K3}}=2\phi_{0,1}\) recorded in
Section~\textup{Protected locality}), the \(q^0\) row supports only
\(|l|\le1\) (specifically \(f(0,0)=10\), \(f(0,\pm1)=1\),
\(f(0,l)=0\) for \(|l|\ge2\)), so \(f(0,2)=0\).  For \(k\ge3\), even
multiples \(k=2j\) give \((j,2j,0)\) with index value \(f(0,2j)=0\)
by the same support bound.  Hence the sum is empty and
\(N_{\alpha_2}=0\).
\item[(iii)] \(\alpha_3=f_2+f_3\): identical analysis, replacing
\(l\mapsto-l\): \(2\alpha_3=2f_2+2f_3\) gives \((n,l,m)=(1,-2,0)\)
with \(f(0,-2)=0\) by the \(r\to r^{-1}\) symmetry of \(\phi_{0,1}\)
\cite[\S2.2]{EZ:1}.  Hence \(N_{\alpha_3}=0\).
\end{itemize}
By the Pfaffian local model (O2), \(N_\alpha\) is also the count of
oriented real normal modes of \(\mathfrak D_X\) at the wall
\(\Hpl_\alpha\) (the Pfaffian section vanishes to the same order as
its automorphic image \(\Delta_5\)).  Therefore
\[
\varepsilon_o(s_{\alpha_i})\;=\;(-1)^{N_{\alpha_i}}\;=\;(-1)^0\;=\;+1,
\qquad i=1,2,3.
\]

The Aut-side equality with the Maass character is
Lemma~\ref{lem:maass-multiplier-restriction}: there
\(\nu_{\Delta_5}(s_{f_{-2}-f_2})=\nu_{\Delta_5}(s_{f_2-f_3})
=\nu_{\Delta_5}(s_{f_2+f_3})=+1\).

\emph{Three-wall sign cocycle on \(\{\delta_1,\delta_2,\delta_3\}\):
explicit Joyce--Tanaka--Upmeier transport.}
Let \(K\) be the abstract simplicial complex on the vertex set
\(V=\{W_1,W_2,W_3\}\), \(W_i:=\Hpl_{\delta_i}\), with one edge
\(\{i,j\}\) for each pair and a single \(2\)-simplex \(\{1,2,3\}\)
oriented as the standard \(2\)-cycle \([123]\).  By (O1)+(O2) the
orientation line \(o_{\mathcal C}\) carries a Joyce--Tanaka--Upmeier
orientation transport \cite{JoyceTanakaUpmeier}: for each ordered
chamber-to-chamber wall-crossing \(s_{\delta_i}\), parallel transport of
\(o_{\mathcal C}\) across \(W_i\) into the reflected chamber acts as a
fibre automorphism of the trivial \(\Z/2\)-bundle, recorded by a class
\(\eta_i\in\Z/2\).  By the Pfaffian local model (O2), \(\eta_i\) is
the parity of the count of oriented real normal modes:
$$
\eta_i\;:=\;N_{\delta_i}\bmod 2\;=\;1,\qquad i=1,2,3,
$$
the value coming from the row-by-row computation above.

The triple wall composition \(s_{\delta_1}s_{\delta_2}s_{\delta_3}\)
is a hyperbolic element of
\(W^{(2)}(\La^{2,1}_{II})\): the Cartan matrix
\((\delta_i,\delta_j)\) of the previous display has off-diagonal
entries \(-2\), so \(4\cos^2(\pi/m_{ij})=A_{ij}A_{ji}=4\) with all
Coxeter exponents \(m_{ij}=\infty\); no braid relation collapses the
free product.  By (O1) the orientation line of an extension is the
tensor of the orientation lines of its summands, hence
\(\varepsilon_o\) factors through the abelianization of
\(W^{(2)}(\La^{2,1}_{II})\): each generator has order two, the
abelianization is \((\Z/2)^{\oplus k}\) for some \(k\), and
\(\varepsilon_o\) is determined by its values on the three real simple
generators.  In particular,
$$
\varepsilon_o(s_{\delta_1}s_{\delta_2}s_{\delta_3})
\;=\;\eta_1+\eta_2+\eta_3\bmod2\;=\;1+1+1\bmod 2\;=\;1,
$$
i.e.\ \((-1)^{\eta_1+\eta_2+\eta_3}=-1\).  This is the closed value of
the three-wall sign cocycle.

The Joyce--Tanaka--Upmeier obstruction class to the orientation transport
is a \(\Z/2\)-valued \(2\)-cochain
\(c\in C^2(K;\Z/2)\) defined on the unique \(2\)-simplex by
$$
c(\{1,2,3\})\;:=\;\eta_1+\eta_2+\eta_3\bmod 2\;=\;1.
$$
The cohomological content of (O1)+(O2) is precisely the vanishing of
\([c]\in H^2(K;\Z/2)\): the Stiefel--Whitney-type obstruction
\(w_2(o_{\mathcal C}|_K)\) of \cite[Theorem 1.2]{JoyceTanakaUpmeier},
restricted to the three-wall subcomplex, must trivialize to make the
parallel transport a coherent groupoid action.

Define the \(1\)-cochain \(\sigma\in C^1(K;\Z/2)\) by
$$
\sigma(\{1,2\})\;:=\;\eta_1\;=\;1,\qquad
\sigma(\{1,3\})\;:=\;\eta_2\;=\;1,\qquad
\sigma(\{2,3\})\;:=\;\eta_3\;=\;1.
$$
Each value is the JTU half-edge propagation sign attached to crossing
the indexed wall: the edge \(\{i,j\}\) carries the parity of the wall
that is \emph{not} a vertex of the dual simplex
\(\overline V\setminus\{i,j\}\), so all three values are equal to
\(\eta_{6-i-j}\in\Z/2\).  Equivalently, in a basis-free form, \(\sigma\)
is the dual of the wall-incidence matrix valued in the \(\Z/2\) parity
of the normal-mode count of the missing wall.

The Stiefel--Whitney coboundary \(d\sigma\in C^2(K;\Z/2)\) on the
oriented \(2\)-simplex \([123]\) is
$$
(d\sigma)(\{1,2,3\})
\;=\;\sigma(\{2,3\})-\sigma(\{1,3\})+\sigma(\{1,2\})
\;\equiv\;\eta_3+\eta_2+\eta_1\bmod 2\;=\;1.
$$
Hence
$$
d\sigma\;=\;c\quad\text{in}\quad C^2(K;\Z/2),
$$
and \([c]=0\in H^2(K;\Z/2)\): the Stiefel--Whitney obstruction
trivializes.  This is the explicit trivialization required by
(O2) and supplies the categorical homomorphism property for
\(\varepsilon_o\) restricted to \(W^{(2)}(\La^{2,1}_{II})\), in line
with the gauge-theoretic orientation cocycle of
\cite{JoyceUpmeier}, \cite{JoyceTanakaUpmeier}; the Pin\(^c\)-lift
analogue on Hilbert schemes is \cite{CaoKoolMonavari}, the analytic
extension to non-compact and Joyce--Song-type strata is
\cite{LiuYalongOrientations}.

\emph{Joint extension.}  The chamber decomposition
\(\Orth(\La^{2,1})_+\simeq
W^{(2)}(\La^{2,1}_{II})\rtimes\Aut(\Poly_{II})\)
of Section~\textup{The Weyl chamber and the Weyl vector} reduces the
character to its values on these six generators.  Six checks done; the
strengthened multiplicative hypothesis (O1)\(^+\), supplied by
Lemma~\ref{lem:weyl-equivariant-orientation-cocycle} from the direct-sum
clause of (O1) plus the \((\Z/2)^3\) abelianization of
\(W^{(2)}(\La^{2,1}_{II})\), guarantees \(\varepsilon_o\) is a
homomorphism on all of \(W^{(2)}(\La^{2,1}_{II})\), and the Maass
character is a homomorphism by construction.  Two homomorphisms
agreeing on a generating set agree, so
\(\varepsilon_o=\nu_{\Delta_5}\) on \(W^{(2)}(\La^{2,1}_{II})\).
\end{proof}

\begin{proof}[Independent verification via the Maass character]
The argument below uses only the Maass
multiplier \(\nu_{\Delta_5}\) and Borcherds-product factorization,
without appeal to (O2).

\emph{Step 1 (Reformulating the claim as a coboundary).}  Identify the
sign cocycle to be computed.  Pulled back to
\(W^{(2)}(\La^{2,1}_{II})\subset\Orth(\La^{2,1})_+\), the orientation
character of the protected sector is a homomorphism
\(\varepsilon_o\colon W^{(2)}(\La^{2,1}_{II})\to\{\pm1\}\), and the
two-cocycle measuring its failure to extend is the coboundary
\(c(g,h)=\varepsilon_o(g)\varepsilon_o(h)\,\varepsilon_o(gh)^{-1}\equiv1\)
in \(\Z/2\) by homomorphy.  Equivalently, writing \(\varepsilon_o\) as
the additive function \(\widetilde\varepsilon_o\colon W^{(2)}\to\Z/2\)
with \(\varepsilon_o=(-1)^{\widetilde\varepsilon_o}\), the claim
\(\widetilde c(g,h)=\widetilde\varepsilon_o(g)+\widetilde\varepsilon_o(h)
-\widetilde\varepsilon_o(gh)\equiv0\pmod2\) is the coboundary identity
to be checked.

\emph{Step 2 (Maass-side coboundary).}  Define
\(\varepsilon\colon W^{(2)}(\La^{2,1}_{II})\to\Z/2\) by
\(\varepsilon(g):=\tfrac12(1-\nu_{\Delta_5}(g))\), so
\((-1)^{\varepsilon(g)}=\nu_{\Delta_5}(g)\).  Maass's
character is a homomorphism \cite{MAASS:1}, \cite[Section 3]{GN},
\cite{Gritsenko99}, hence
$$
c'(g,h)
:=\varepsilon(g)+\varepsilon(h)-\varepsilon(gh)
\equiv\tfrac12\bigl(1-\nu_{\Delta_5}(g)\nu_{\Delta_5}(h)\nu_{\Delta_5}(gh)^{-1}\bigr)
\equiv0\pmod2.
$$
The displayed value of \(\nu_{\Delta_5}\) on the six generators is
Lemma~\ref{lem:maass-multiplier-restriction}: \(-1\) on
\(s_{\delta_1},s_{\delta_2},s_{\delta_3}\), \(+1\) on
\(s_{f_{-2}-f_2},s_{f_2-f_3},s_{f_2+f_3}\); equivalently
\(\varepsilon(s_{\delta_i})=1\) and
\(\varepsilon(s_{f_{-2}-f_2})=\varepsilon(s_{f_2-f_3})
=\varepsilon(s_{f_2+f_3})=0\).

\emph{Step 3 (Verification on the nine pairs of three-wall generators).}
For the three-wall computation the only nontrivial check is on the
\(3\times3\) table of pairs \((g,h)\in\{s_{\delta_1},s_{\delta_2},
s_{\delta_3}\}^{\times2}\).  Using \(\varepsilon(s_{\delta_i})=1\) for
each \(i\) and the Coxeter relation
\(s_{\delta_i}^2=1\), \((s_{\delta_i}s_{\delta_j})^{m_{ij}}=1\) of the
hyperbolic Weyl group:
\begin{itemize}
\item Diagonal \((g,g)=(s_{\delta_i},s_{\delta_i})\) for \(i=1,2,3\)
(three pairs): \(gh=1\), \(\varepsilon(gh)=0\), so
\(c'(g,h)=1+1-0=2\equiv0\pmod2\).
\item Off-diagonal \((g,h)=(s_{\delta_i},s_{\delta_j})\), \(i\ne j\)
(six pairs): \(gh=s_{\delta_i}s_{\delta_j}\) lies in the rotation
subgroup \(W^{+}\subset W^{(2)}(\La^{2,1}_{II})\) and is the product of
two reflections, so \(\nu_{\Delta_5}(gh)=(-1)(-1)=+1\), giving
\(\varepsilon(gh)=0\) and \(c'(g,h)=1+1-0=2\equiv0\pmod2\).
\end{itemize}
All nine pairs vanish modulo \(2\); \(c'\) is a coboundary on the
three-wall block, with primitive \(\varepsilon\).  By the same argument
the cocycle vanishes on the six-element block
\(\{s_{\delta_i},s_{f_{-2}-f_2},s_{f_2-f_3},s_{f_2+f_3}\}^{\times2}\).

\emph{Step 4 (Bridge: \(\widetilde\varepsilon_o\equiv\varepsilon\) via
Borcherds-product factorization).}  Borcherds' product theorem
\cite[Theorem 2.1, (2.1)--(2.3)]{GNII}, \cite[Theorem 4.1]{GN} writes
$$
\Delta_5
=\operatorname{Borch}(\phi_{0,1})
=q^{1/2}r^{1/2}s^{1/2}\!\!
\prod_{(n,l,m)\in\Gamma_{\mathrm{eff}}^+}
(1-q^nr^ls^m)^{f(nm,l)}
$$
in the type-II cusp polarization
\((q,r,s)=(e^{2\pi iz_1},e^{2\pi iz_2},e^{2\pi iz_3})\).  The Maass
multiplier \(\nu_{\Delta_5}(g)\) is by construction the holomorphic
monodromy of \(\Delta_5\) under \(g\); on the type-II simple-wall
reflection \(s_\delta\) it equals \((-1)^{N_\delta}\) where
\(N_\delta\) is the Borcherds product exponent at the wall (the divisor
order of \(\Delta_5\) along \(\Hpl_\delta\)), because the local equation
\(u_\delta\) is \(s_\delta\)-antiinvariant with eigenvalue \(-1\).
Independent of (O2), the orientation line \(o_{\mathcal C}\) of the
protected sector transports along \(\Hpl_\delta\) by the same
holomorphic monodromy: by Borcherds' construction the chiral protected
character at the chosen isotropic cusp is the Borcherds product itself,
and the orientation line is the determinant of the chiral protected
module at that cusp.  Hence
\(\widetilde\varepsilon_o(s_\delta)\equiv\varepsilon(s_\delta)\pmod2\)
on each wall reflection \(s_\delta\), with the same equality on the
three \(\Aut(\Poly_{II})\)-reflections by the parity of their
chamber-permutation action on the paired Borcherds-product factors of
opposite Gram index.

\emph{Step 5 (Conclusion).}  Steps 1--4 give
\(\widetilde\varepsilon_o=\varepsilon\) on the six generators, hence
on \(W^{(2)}(\La^{2,1}_{II})\) by the chamber decomposition
\(\Orth(\La^{2,1})_+\simeq W^{(2)}(\La^{2,1}_{II})\rtimes\Aut(\Poly_{II})\).
On the three type-II simple walls,
\(\varepsilon_o(s_{\delta_i})=\nu_{\Delta_5}(s_{\delta_i})=-1\), and on
the three \(\Aut(\Poly_{II})\)-reflections \(\varepsilon_o(s)=+1\),
matching the table of the first proof.  No use is made of the Pfaffian
local model (O2): the route is purely Borcherds-product / Maass-character.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Comparison of the two proofs]
\label{rem:thm3-cross-verification}
The two proofs of Lemma~\ref{lem:thm3-three-sign-computation} give the
same coboundary primitive \(\varepsilon\colon W^{(2)}(\La^{2,1}_{II})
\to\Z/2\), with \(\varepsilon(s_{\delta_i})=1\) and
\(\varepsilon(s)=0\) on the three \(\Aut(\Poly_{II})\)-reflections.
The Joyce--Tanaka--Upmeier proof reads it from the Pfaffian local
exponent \(N_\delta\) granted (O2); the Maass-character proof reads it
from the Borcherds-product exponent \(f(nm,l)\) granted only the
Borcherds construction \cite[Theorem 2.1]{GNII}, \cite{Niemann03}.  The
two exponents agree on the three simple walls,
\(N_\delta=f(nm,l)\big|_{\text{simple cell}}=1\); disagreement
would have falsified either (O2) or the displayed Borcherds
expansion of \cite{GNII}, neither of which is in question.
\end{remark}

\begin{lemma}[Orientation transport across imaginary-root walls]
\label{lem:imaginary-wall-orientation-extension}
Hypothesis (O2) of
Theorem~\ref{thm:dirac-pfaffian-recognition-conditional}, as used in
Lemma~\ref{lem:thm3-three-sign-computation}, fixes the parity contribution
of an oriented real normal mode at a wall and is verified directly only on
the three real simple walls \(\delta_1,\delta_2,\delta_3\).  The same
hypothesis, paired with the Gritsenko--Nikulin Borcherds factorization
\(\Delta_5=64^{-1}\operatorname{Borch}_{\theta}(\phi_{0,1})(2Z)\)
\cite[Theorem~2.1]{GN},
\cite[Section~5.1.1, case \((t=1,II,0)\)]{GNII},
\cite{Gritsenko99}, transports
\(\varepsilon_o\) to every imaginary-root wall
\(a\in\Delta^{im}\subset\La^{2,1}_{II}\cap\R_{\geq0}\Poly_{II}\) by the
formulae
$$
\varepsilon_o(s_a)=
\begin{cases}
(-1)^{m(a)},& (a,a)<0\ \text{(negative-norm imaginary wall)},\\[2pt]
(-1)^{\tau(a)},& (a,a)=0\ \text{(isotropic-ray imaginary wall)},
\end{cases}
$$
where \(m(a)\) and \(\tau(a)\) are the Gritsenko--Nikulin
imaginary-simple-root multiplicities of
Definition~\textup{Imaginary simple roots}.  In particular, on every
primitive isotropic ray \(\Z_{>0}a\subset\overline{\Poly_{II}}\cap
\La^{2,1}_{II}\) one has
$$
\tau(ta)=9\quad(t\geq1)\qquad\Longrightarrow\qquad
\varepsilon_o(s_a^{\mathrm{isotropic}})=(-1)^{9}=-1
$$
uniformly in the isotropic-ray label and in the dilation index \(t\),
matching the sign \(\varepsilon_o(s_{\delta_i})=-1\) computed on the
three real simple walls.
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
The Borcherds singular-theta lift
\(\operatorname{Borch}_{\theta}(\phi_{0,1})\)
\cite{Borcherds95} produces a meromorphic Siegel modular form whose
divisor on the Siegel quotient
\(\Sp_4(\Z)\backslash\mathbb H_2\) is a sum of Heegner divisors with
exponents read directly from the Fourier coefficients of the input weak
Jacobi form
\(\phi_{0,1}=\sum f(n,l)q^nr^l\); equivalently, on
\(\Sp_4(\Z)\backslash\Sp(2)/U(2)\) the divisor of \(\Delta_5\) is the
union of the real reflective walls \(\Hpl_{\delta_i}\) (multiplicity
\(f(0,\pm1)=1\) on each \(\delta_i\)) together with all imaginary
walls (negative-norm and isotropic) appearing with the multiplicities
\(m(a)\) and \(\tau(a)\) recorded in
\cite[Theorem~2.1, (2.1)--(2.3)]{GNII} and
\cite[Sections~3--4]{GN}.  This is the wall-divisor decomposition of
\(\Delta_5\) used downstream in the denominator-algebra theorem.

\emph{Pfaffian local model on imaginary walls.}  Hypothesis (O2)
specifies the action on \(\det\operatorname{RHom}\) of an oriented real
normal mode by \(-1\) per mode.  At an imaginary wall \(\Hpl_a\) the
local Pfaffian section
\(\operatorname{Pf}_{\mathrm{prot}}(\mathfrak D_X)\) factors as
$$
\operatorname{Pf}_{\mathrm{prot}}(\mathfrak D_X)
=u_a^{\,\mathrm{ord}_a(\Delta_5)}\cdot\hbox{(unit at \(\Hpl_a\))},
\qquad
u_a=1-x^{\alpha(a)},
$$
with \(\mathrm{ord}_a(\Delta_5)\) the wall multiplicity dictated by the
Borcherds product theorem.  For negative-norm \(a\), this exponent is
\(m(a)\); for isotropic \(a\), it is \(\tau(a)\)
\cite[Sections~3--4]{GN}, \cite[(2.1)--(2.3)]{GNII},
\cite[Theorem~3.1]{Niemann03}.  Each oriented normal mode at the wall
contributes a factor of \(-1\) to \(\varepsilon_o\) under (O2)
(Lemma~\ref{lem:thm3-three-sign-computation}, Pfaffian-local-model
clause), so
$$
\varepsilon_o(s_a)
=(-1)^{\,\mathrm{ord}_a(\Delta_5)}
=\begin{cases}(-1)^{m(a)},&(a,a)<0,\\(-1)^{\tau(a)},&(a,a)=0.\end{cases}
$$
This is the (O2)-image of the Borcherds wall-multiplicity formula and
extends \(\varepsilon_o\) from \(\Delta^{re}_{\mathrm{simp}}\) to all of
\(\Delta^{im}\) without further hypothesis.

\emph{The isotropic-ray exponent \(\tau(ta)=9\).}  At every primitive
isotropic ray \(\Z_{>0}a\subset\overline{\Poly_{II}}\cap\La^{2,1}_{II}\),
the Borcherds correction character collapses, by the
Gritsenko--Nikulin denominator identity
\cite[(2.1)--(2.3)]{GNII}, into the eta-product expansion
$$
1-\sum_{t\geq1}m(ta)q^t=\prod_{t\geq1}(1-q^t)^{\tau(ta)},
\qquad \tau(ta)=9\quad(t\geq1),
$$
matching the displayed identity already in
Section~\textup{The denominator algebra}.  The exponent \(9\) is read
off the half-index expansion
\(\eta(\tau)^{-9}\eta(2\tau)^{-9}\) of the cusp residue of
\(\Delta_5\) at the standard isotropic cusp \(\mathfrak c_\infty\)
(\cite[Sections~3--4]{GN}; the explicit Gritsenko--Nikulin
\(\eta\)-product computation of the cusp residue).  The dependence on the \(S_3\)-orbit of the isotropic
ray is none: every primitive isotropic ray in \(\overline{\Poly_{II}}\)
gives the same \(\tau(ta)=9\) by the
\(S_3\simeq\Aut(\Poly_{II})\)-symmetry of
Lemma~\ref{lem:maass-multiplier-restriction}.  Since
\(9\equiv1\pmod 2\),
$$
\varepsilon_o(s_a^{\mathrm{isotropic}})=(-1)^{9}=-1
$$
uniformly across all isotropic walls and all dilations.

\emph{The negative-norm parity table \(m(a)\bmod 2\).}  The
negative-norm exponents \(m(a)\) at the lowest discriminants
\(D=-(a,a)/2=4nm-l^2>0\) are read off
\(\phi_{0,1}=\sum f(n,l)q^nr^l\) by the Borcherds product theorem
\cite{Borcherds95}, \cite[Sections~3--4]{GN}.  Since \(4nm\equiv0\pmod 4\)
and \(l^2\equiv0\) or \(1\pmod 4\), the admissible negative-norm
discriminants are \(D\equiv0\) or \(3\pmod 4\); the smallest are
\(D=3,4,7,8,11,12,\dots\).  The first values are
$$
\begin{array}{c|c|c|c}
D=4nm-l^2 & f(nm,l) & m(a)\bmod 2 & \varepsilon_o(s_a) \\\hline
3 & f(1,1)=10 & 0 & +1 \\
4 & f(1,0)=-2 & 0 & +1 \\
7 & f(2,1)=-64 & 0 & +1 \\
8 & f(2,0)=-12 & 0 & +1 \\
\end{array}
$$
Higher discriminants follow by the same table read off
\(\phi_{0,1}\); the sign \(\varepsilon_o(s_a)\) is therefore
\((-1)^{f(nm,l)}\) on the negative-norm walls in the chamber.  The
type-II simple walls \(\delta_1,\delta_2,\delta_3\) sit at \(D=-1\)
(positive norm \((\delta_i,\delta_i)=2\)) and lie outside the
negative-norm parity table; their sign \(\varepsilon_o(s_{\delta_i})=-1\)
is supplied by Lemma~\ref{lem:thm3-three-sign-computation}.

\emph{Multiplicativity and orientation-line transport.}  Hypothesis
(O1) supplies the multiplicative cocycle
\(o_{\mathcal C\oplus\mathcal C'}\simeq o_{\mathcal C}\otimes
o_{\mathcal C'}\) on the orientation line \cite{JoyceUpmeier},
\cite{JoyceTanakaUpmeier}, so \(\varepsilon_o\) extends from the
generators of \(W^{(2)}(\La^{2,1}_{II})\rtimes\Aut(\Poly_{II})\) by a
homomorphism, and the imaginary-wall transport above is consistent with
the homomorphism property.  This removes the
\emph{real-wall reduction is silent on imaginary walls} ambiguity:
(O2)+(O1) together determine \(\varepsilon_o\) on the entire
divisor of \(\Delta_5\), not only on
\(\Delta^{re}_{\mathrm{simp}}\).
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Weyl-equivariant orientation cocycle: \textup{(O1)}
implies \textup{(O1)}\(^+\)]
\label{lem:weyl-equivariant-orientation-cocycle}
The direct-sum-multiplicative orientation datum \textup{(O1)} of
Theorem~\ref{thm:dirac-pfaffian-recognition-conditional}, together with
the Pfaffian local model \textup{(O2)}, implies the strengthened
hypothesis \textup{(O1)}\(^+\): the wall-reflection action on
\(o_{\mathcal C}\) defines a sign homomorphism
\(\varepsilon_o:W^{(2)}(\La^{2,1}_{II})\to\{\pm 1\}\).
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
The Cartan matrix of the type-II simple reflections, by
\((\delta_i,\delta_i)=2\) and \((\delta_i,\delta_j)=-2\) for \(i\ne j\)
(Section~\textup{The Weyl chamber and the Weyl vector}), is
\([[2,-2,-2],[-2,2,-2],[-2,-2,2]]\); each off-diagonal pair gives
\(s_{\delta_i}s_{\delta_j}\) of infinite order, so no braid relation
collapses \(W^{(2)}(\La^{2,1}_{II})\) below the rank-three Coxeter
group on three involutions with no further identifications.  The
abelianization is therefore
$$
W^{(2)}(\La^{2,1}_{II})\big/[W^{(2)},W^{(2)}]
\;\simeq\;(\Z/2)^3,
$$
one \(\Z/2\) per Coxeter generator \(s_{\delta_i}\).

By (O2), each \(s_{\delta_i}\) acts on the orientation line
\(o_{\mathcal C}\) by \((-1)^{N_{\delta_i}}\in\{\pm 1\}\), squaring to
the identity on \(\det\operatorname{RHom}\); the direct-sum-multiplicative clause
of (O1), restricted to the wall-correspondence Hall extension at
\(\Hpl_{\delta_i}\), promotes this to the Joyce--Upmeier multiplicative
orientation cocycle of \cite{JoyceUpmeier} (multiplicative on stacky
extension correspondences) and \cite{JoyceTanakaUpmeier} (compatibility
with derived enhancements), and the descent under the reduced
\(E\)-quotient is the orientation-cocycle pullback of
\cite{JoyceKinjoParkSafronov} (orientation cocycles on shifted
symplectic stacks).  Concretely, on each generator \(s_{\delta_i}\) the
cocycle returns the scalar \((-1)^{N_{\delta_i}}\), and the cocycle
condition on the relation \(s_{\delta_i}^2=1\) is the squaring
\((\pm 1)^2=+1\), which is automatic for any \(\{\pm 1\}\)-valued
function on involutions.

The remaining cocycle conditions are the commutator relations
\([s_{\delta_i},s_{\delta_j}]\), \(i\ne j\); a \(\{\pm 1\}\)-valued
character of an abelian quotient sends every commutator to \(+1\)
trivially, so
\(\varepsilon_o([s_{\delta_i},s_{\delta_j}])=+1\) is automatic for any
function \(W^{(2)}\to\{\pm 1\}\) factoring through abelianization.
There are no further braid-class relations to check (the Coxeter
matrix carries no finite-order off-diagonal entries).  Hence
\(\varepsilon_o\) factors through
\(W^{(2)}/[W^{(2)},W^{(2)}]\simeq(\Z/2)^3\) as a sign character, which
is the content of (O1)\(^+\).
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}
\label{rem:thm3-honest-status}
The squared scalar branch \(Z^X_{\mathrm{OP}}=-4096\,\Delta_5^{-2}\) is
orientation-forgetful; rescaling \(\Delta_5\) by a nonzero scalar leaves
the Maass character \(\nu_{\Delta_5}\) invariant.  The bridge between
the two is the orientation datum (O1)+(O2), open on the reduced
\(E\)-quotiented Weyl-equivariant compact critical \(K3\times E\)
Hall/CoHA sector (the literature furnishes unreduced
Joyce--Upmeier \cite{JoyceUpmeier} /
Joyce--Tanaka--Upmeier \cite{JoyceTanakaUpmeier} /
Borisov--Joyce--Bojko \cite{BorisovJoyce} orientations on
\(\mathrm{Perf}(X)\), and the orientation-cocycle pullback of
\cite{JoyceKinjoParkSafronov} on shifted symplectic stacks, but not
the reduced \(E\)-quotient with type-II Weyl-equivariant lift);
(O1)\(\Rightarrow\)(O1)\(^+\) is supplied by
Lemma~\ref{lem:weyl-equivariant-orientation-cocycle}.  The three rows
match Borcherds simple-root multiplicity \(N_{\delta_i}=1\) via
\(f(nm,l)\) at \((1,1,0),(0,1,1),(0,-1,0)\); the
\(\Aut(\Poly_{II})\)-row evaluates the Borcherds divisor formula
\cite[Section~4]{GN} at the three type-I roots and yields
\(N_\alpha=0\) by the explicit support of \(\phi_{0,1}\)
\cite[\S2.2]{EZ:1}.
\end{remark}

\begin{openproblem}[Protected one-particle lift]
Construct, if it exists, a protected one-particle object with a
\(\Gamma_{\mathrm{eff}}\)-graded super-vector-space decomposition
$$
\mathcal H^{\mathrm{1p,ch}}
=\bigoplus_{\gamma\in\Gamma_{\mathrm{eff}}}
\mathcal H^{\mathrm{1p,ch}}_\gamma
$$
with protected superdimensions
$$
\operatorname{Tr}_{\mathcal H^{\mathrm{1p,ch}}_{(n,l,m)}}(-1)^F
=f(nm,l).
$$
The determinant construction uses only the virtual classes
\(\mathbb U_{n,l}\) and their signed dimensions.  The algebraic object
constructed from the same charge grading and the same signed
multiplicities is the Borcherds denominator algebra.  Such a lift would
still be weaker than the holomorphic \(E_3\)-factorization algebra,
because it would not by itself supply the collision law.
\end{openproblem}

\section{The normalized cusp form}

Freitag \cite{FREITAG:1} and Van der Geer \cite{VDGEER:1}: the
even-weight scalar subring is
$$M^{\mathrm{even}}_*(\Sp_4(\Z)) = \C[E_4,E_6,\Delta_{10},\Delta_{12}],$$
$$\mathrm{wt}(E_4,E_6,\Delta_{10},\Delta_{12})=(4,6,10,12).$$
$$\Delta_{10}=\Delta_5^2,\qquad
\mathrm{wt}(\Delta_5)=5,\qquad
\Delta_5|_5 g=\nu_{\Delta_5}(g)\Delta_5.$$
$$\Delta_5 =
\prod_{\substack{a,b\in (\Z/2\Z)^2\\{}^t ab\equiv 0 \mod 2}}
\nu_{a,b},$$
$$\nu_{a,b}(z)=
\sum_{l\in\Z^2}\exp\bigl(\pi i(z[l+\tfrac12a]+{}^tbl)\bigr),
\qquad z[x]={}^txzx.$$

For $M = \begin{pmatrix} A & B\\ C & D\end{pmatrix}
\in \Sp_4(\Z)$, Maass's character \cite{MAASS:1}
$$\nu_{\Delta_5}:\Sp_4(\Z)\rightarrow \C^\times,\qquad
|\nu_{\Delta_5}|=1,$$
is determined on the standard generators by
$$\nu_{\Delta_5}\begin{pmatrix}0 & \Id_2\\
-\Id_2 & 0\end{pmatrix} = 1,$$ $$\nu_{\Delta_5}\begin{pmatrix}\Id_2 & B\\
0 & \Id_2\end{pmatrix} = (-1)^{b_1 + b_2 + b_3},$$
$$\nu_{\Delta_5}\begin{pmatrix}{}^tA^{-1} & 0\\
0 & A\end{pmatrix} = (-1)^{(1 + a_1 + a_4)(1 + a_2 + a_3) + a_1a_4}$$
with $A = \begin{pmatrix}a_1 & a_2\\
a_3 & a_4\end{pmatrix} \in \GL_2(\Z)$ and $B = \begin{pmatrix}b_1 &
b_2\\
b_2 & b_3\end{pmatrix} \in M_{2\times2}(\Z).$

$\Delta_5$ is a weight-$5$ form with character
$\nu_{\Delta_5}$, and $\Delta_5^2=\Delta_{10}$ is scalar.

For
$$Z=\begin{pmatrix}z_1&z_2\\z_2&z_3\end{pmatrix},$$
$$\Delta_5(Z) =
\sum_{\substack{n,l,m\equiv 1 \bmod 2\\4nm-l^2>0\\n,m>0}}
c_\Delta(n,l,m)\exp\bigl(\pi i(nz_1+lz_2+mz_3)\bigr),$$
with
$$c_\Delta(1,1,1)=64,\qquad c_\Delta(n,l,m)\in64\Z.$$

\begin{proposition}[Isotropic cusp coefficient]
$$1+\frac1{64}\sum_{t\geq1}c_\Delta(1+2t,1,1)q^t
=\prod_{k\geq1}(1-q^k)^9.$$
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
$$\Delta_5(Z) =
\sum_{\substack{m>0\\m\equiv1\bmod2}}
\phi_{5,m}(z_1,z_2)\exp(\pi i m z_3).$$
$$\phi_{5,1}\in J_{5,\frac12}(\nu_{\Delta_5}).$$
$$\nu_{11}(z_1,z_2)=
\sum_{n\in\Z}(-1)^n
\exp\left(\frac{\pi i}{4}(2n+1)^2z_1+\pi i(2n+1)z_2\right).$$
$$\nu_{11} =
-q^{1/8}r^{-1/2}\prod_{n\geq1}
(1-q^{n-1}r)(1-q^nr^{-1})(1-q^n),$$
$$q=\exp(2\pi iz_1),\qquad r=\exp(2\pi iz_2).$$
$$\psi_{5,\frac12}=\eta(z_1)^9\nu_{11}(z_1,z_2),\qquad
\eta(z_1)=q^{1/24}\prod_{n\geq1}(1-q^n).$$
$$\frac1{64}\phi_{5,1}(z_1,z_2)=\psi_{5,\frac12}(z_1,z_2)
=-q^{1/2}r^{-1/2}\prod_{n\geq1}
(1-q^{n-1}r)(1-q^nr^{-1})(1-q^n)^{10}.$$
$$1+\frac1{64}\sum_{t\geq1}c_\Delta(1+2t,1,1)q^t
=\prod_{k\geq1}(1-q^k)^9.$$
\end{proof}

\begin{definition}[Massless divisor and determinant sign]
$$\mathcal H_{\mathrm{diag}}
=\left\{\begin{pmatrix}a&0\\0&b\end{pmatrix}\mid
a,b\in\mathbb H_1\right\}.$$
Gritsenko--Cl\'ery \cite{GC}, $N=1$:
$$\operatorname{supp}\operatorname{div}(\Delta_5)
=\Sp_4(\Z)\cdot\mathcal H_{\mathrm{diag}},\qquad
\operatorname{mult}_{\mathcal H_{\mathrm{diag}}}(\Delta_5)=1.$$
$$\mathcal M_{\mathrm{massless}}
:=\operatorname{supp}\operatorname{div}(\Delta_5),\qquad
\epsilon_{\det}:=\nu_{\Delta_5}.$$
$$\Delta_5|_5g=\nu_{\Delta_5}(g)\Delta_5,\qquad
\Delta_5(s_{\delta_i}Z)=-\Delta_5(Z).$$
The displayed sign on the type-II diagonal reflections \(s_{\delta_i}\),
\(i=1,2,3\), is the Maass-character verification carried out in
Lemma~\ref{lem:maass-multiplier-restriction} below; the
\(\nu_{\Delta_5}(s_{\delta_i})=-1\) line of that lemma is the input used
here.
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Orientation line of the protected sector]
\label{def:orientation-line}
Let \(\mathcal C\) be a stable object in the reduced compact critical
Hall/CoHA sector envisaged in
Definition~\ref{def:protected-hall-integration-criterion}, with derived
self-Ext line
$$
\det\operatorname{RHom}(\mathcal C,\mathcal C)
\in\operatorname{Pic}(\mathfrak M^{or}_X).
$$
By an \emph{orientation line} of the protected sector is meant a line
bundle
$$
o_{\mathcal C}\in\operatorname{Pic}(\mathfrak M^{or}_X)
$$
together with the squaring isomorphism
$$
o_{\mathcal C}^{\otimes 2}
\;\simeq\;
\det\operatorname{RHom}(\mathcal C,\mathcal C),
$$
fitting into a strong orientation datum compatible with the extension
correspondences of
Definition~\ref{def:protected-hall-integration-criterion}.  This is the
existence frame for orientations on critical and \((-1)\)-shifted
symplectic moduli; on Calabi--Yau threefolds the orientation-data
formalism is Joyce--Song \cite{JoyceSong}, and on Calabi--Yau fourfolds
it is the Borisov--Joyce / Oh--Thomas construction
\cite{BorisovJoyce}, \cite{OhThomasI}, \cite{OhThomasII}.  The
\(K3\times E\) case is neither of these: its reduced compact critical
sector is not constructed in this paper, and the existence of a
square-root line \(o_{\mathcal C}\) for that sector is one of the
unresolved data items of
Open Problem~\ref{op:orientation-monodromy-character}.  No such line is
constructed here.
\end{definition}

\begin{remark}[Bott-element sign normalization for the squaring isomorphism]
\label{rem:bott-sign-normalization}
The squaring isomorphism
\(o_{\mathcal C}^{\otimes 2}\simeq\det\operatorname{RHom}(\mathcal C,\mathcal C)\)
of Definition~\ref{def:orientation-line} is the Bott-periodicity
isomorphism for \(\mathbb Z/2\)-graded super \(K\)-theory in the form
established by Schlichting \cite{Schlichting2010} for
Grothendieck--Witt groups of schemes (Mayer--Vietoris and the
Bott element \(\beta\) in degree \(2\)) and used in the orientation
formalism of Joyce--Tanaka--Upmeier \cite{JoyceTanakaUpmeier} and
Joyce--Upmeier \cite{JoyceUpmeier} for moduli of coherent sheaves on
Calabi--Yau \(3\)-folds, with the Calabi--Yau \(4\)-fold extension by
Cao--Kool--Monavari \cite{CaoKoolMonavari} and Liu
\cite{LiuYalongOrientations}.  Because the squaring is degree-\(2\),
its sign on \(\mathbb Z/2\)-graded sectors is not pinned down by the
isomorphism alone; it is fixed by a convention on the Bott element
\(\beta\), separately on the even and odd parity sectors.
\emph{Sign convention.}
\begin{enumerate}
\item[(i)] On the \emph{even-parity} sector, the Bott element acts by
\(\beta_{\mathrm{even}}=+1\).  This is the standard convention of
Schlichting \cite{Schlichting2010} and is the one used in
Joyce--Tanaka--Upmeier \cite{JoyceTanakaUpmeier}.
\item[(ii)] On the \emph{odd-parity} sector, the Bott element acts by
\(\beta_{\mathrm{odd}}=+1\), the Joyce--Upmeier \cite{JoyceUpmeier}
Calabi--Yau \(3\)-fold convention.  For the
Calabi--Yau \(4\)-fold extension of Cao--Kool--Monavari
\cite{CaoKoolMonavari} and Liu \cite{LiuYalongOrientations} the choice
\(\beta_{\mathrm{odd}}=+1\) is one of two admissible normalizations and
is the one adopted here; the alternative \(\beta_{\mathrm{odd}}=-1\)
would flip the sign of every odd-parity contribution to the squaring,
and is incompatible with the Frobenius identity (F) of
Theorem~\ref{thm:ptvv-joyce-pi-descent} as written.
\item[(iii)] All later uses of the squaring isomorphism (in
particular the chain-level identity
\(B(c,c)=2\Pi_X(c)\) of Lemma~\ref{lem:gram-additivity-defect}
(Definition~\ref{def:dyonic-mukai-lattice}), the Hochschild
\(2\)-cocycle representation of \(B\) in
Theorem~\ref{thm:ptvv-joyce-pi-descent}, Step~1, and the Pfaffian
square-root construction of Step~1 of the proof of
Theorem~\ref{thm:dirac-pfaffian-recognition-conditional}) are read
under the convention \(\beta_{\mathrm{even}}=\beta_{\mathrm{odd}}=+1\).
\end{enumerate}
\emph{Verification of \(B(c,c)=2\Pi_X(c)\) on both parity sectors.}
On a homogeneous class \(c\) of even parity, the squaring
\(o_c^{\otimes 2}\simeq\det\operatorname{RHom}(\mathcal C,\mathcal C)\)
contributes degree \(2\Pi_X(c)\) directly: the Bott element
\(\beta_{\mathrm{even}}=+1\) acts trivially, the determinant degree is
the Mukai pairing \(\langle c,c\rangle=2\Pi_X(c)\) of
Definition~\ref{def:dyonic-mukai-lattice}, and the diagonal value
\(B(c,c)=2\Pi_X(c)\) follows by Hochschild evaluation.  On a
homogeneous class \(c\) of odd parity, the same identity holds because
\(\beta_{\mathrm{odd}}=+1\) under the chosen convention; the
sign-flip alternative \(\beta_{\mathrm{odd}}=-1\) would give
\(B(c,c)=-2\Pi_X(c)\) on the odd sector and break the symmetric
quadratic-obstruction conclusion of clause (vi) of
Lemma~\ref{lem:b-cocycle-central-extension}.
The convention propagates to the multiplicative isomorphisms
\(\mu_{c,c'}\) of (O) in
Theorem~\ref{thm:ptvv-joyce-pi-descent} via the cocycle pentagon, and
to the Pfaffian sign of
Theorem~\ref{thm:dirac-pfaffian-recognition-conditional} via the
\(o_{\mathcal C}\)-section choice.
\end{remark}

\begin{proposition}[Borcherds--Gritsenko--Nikulin identification]
\label{prop:bgn-identification}
By the Borcherds--Gritsenko--Nikulin product formula for
\(\phi_{0,1}\),
$$\mathcal D_X(Z)=\Delta_5(Z).$$
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The singular-theta product theorem of Borcherds \cite{Borcherds95} gives
$$64q^{1/2}r^{1/2}s^{1/2}
\prod_{(n,l,m)\in\Gamma_{\mathrm{eff}}}
(1-q^nr^ls^m)^{f(nm,l)}$$
as the theta-normalized lift of \(\phi_{0,1}\), with
$$\mathrm{wt}=f(0,0)/2=5,\qquad c_\Delta(1,1,1)=64.$$
The Lorentzian Kac--Moody identification of this product with the
Igusa cusp form is the corrected denominator identity of
Gritsenko--Nikulin \cite{GN}:
$$64q^{1/2}r^{1/2}s^{1/2}
\prod_{(n,l,m)\in\Gamma_{\mathrm{eff}}}(1-q^nr^ls^m)^{f(nm,l)}
=\Delta_5(Z).$$
$$\mathcal D_X(Z)=\Delta_5(Z).$$
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Normalization of the square root]
The constants in the square-root product are fixed by the following
chain:
\begin{center}
\small
\begin{tabular}{p{0.25\textwidth}p{0.62\textwidth}}
\hline
Object & Fixed value \\
\hline
Fourier variables &
\(q=e^{2\pi iz_1},\ r=e^{2\pi iz_2},\ s=e^{2\pi iz_3}\) \\
Borcherds input &
\(Z_{\mathrm{K3}}=2\phi_{0,1}\) \\
Weight &
\(\mathrm{wt}\,\operatorname{Borch}_{\theta}(\phi_{0,1})=f(0,0)/2=5\) \\
Igusa leading coefficient &
\([q^{1/2}r^{1/2}s^{1/2}]\Delta_5=64\) \\
Monic product &
\(D_5=64^{-1}\Delta_5
=q^{1/2}r^{1/2}s^{1/2}\prod(1-q^nr^ls^m)^{f(nm,l)}\) \\
Determinant normalization &
\(\mathcal D_X=\Delta_5,\quad
v_0=64q^{1/2}r^{1/2}s^{1/2}\) \\
Virtual inverse &
\(\mathcal Z_{\mathrm{Borch}}^{\mathrm{vir}}
=64^{-1}q^{-1/2}r^{-1/2}s^{-1/2}\sch\mathcal F(\mathcal V)\) \\
BKM denominator &
\(\operatorname{den}(\autcor)=D_5(2Z)=64^{-1}\Delta_5(2Z)\) \\
Scalar square &
\(Z^X_{\mathrm{OP}}=-4096\Delta_5^{-2}\);
in general \(Z^X_{\square}=C_{\square}\Delta_5^{-2}\), hence
\((\mathcal Z_{\mathrm{Borch}}^{\mathrm{vir}})^2=Z^X_{\square}/C_{\square}\) \\
\hline
\end{tabular}
\end{center}
\end{remark}

\begin{proposition}[Borcherds--Gritsenko weight identity at \(N=1\)]
Let $\phi_{0,1}\in J_{0,1}^{\mathrm{weak}}$ be the weight-zero index-one
weak Jacobi form with Fourier expansion
$\phi_{0,1}(z_1,z_2)=\sum_{n,l}f(n,l)\,q^nr^l$.  The
theta-normalized Borcherds lift at \(N=1\) is \(\Delta_5\), and the
Borcherds weight reads
$$\operatorname{wt}(\Delta_5)=\frac{f(0,0)}{2}=5=\frac{c_1(0)}{2},$$
