with $c_1(0):=f(0,0)=10$.  Since the weight is integral, no metaplectic
cover is needed for the weight factor.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The Borcherds singular-theta regularisation of \(\phi_{0,1}\) produces
a meromorphic Siegel modular form of weight \(f(0,0)/2\); at \(N=1\)
the paramodular group is \(\Sp_4(\Z)\) by Gritsenko--Nikulin
\cite{GN}.  The input Jacobi form has \(f(0,0)=10\)
(Eichler--Zagier \cite{EZ:1}, elliptic genus of K3), hence the output
weight is
\(5\).  Identifying
\(\operatorname{Borch}_{\theta}(\phi_{0,1})\) with \(\Delta_5\) via the
Igusa identification \((\mathcal D_X=\Delta_5)\) fixes
$\operatorname{wt}(\Delta_5)=5$.  Setting $c_1(0):=f(0,0)$ exhibits the
row $(N=1,\,\operatorname{wt}=5,\,c_1(0)=10)$ of the Gritsenko--Cl\'ery
catalogue \cite{GC}; the remaining integral and half-integral
Clery--Gritsenko rows are listed in \cite[Theorem 1.4]{GC}.  Integrality
\(\operatorname{wt}(\Delta_5)\in\Z\) means that no metaplectic cover is
required for the weight factor.  The Hodge automorphic line
\(\mathcal L^5\) remains nontrivial, and the Maass character
\(\nu_{\Delta_5}\) is a finite-order character of \(\Sp_4(\Z)\).
\end{proof}

\section{The protected-index dictionary}

Only the OP/DT scalar branch requires an elliptically fibered K3 surface
with a section.  The Borcherds determinant above used only the universal
K3 elliptic genus.

Let $S$ be an elliptically fibered K3 surface
$$\pi:S\rightarrow \mathbb{P}^1$$
with a section $s_1$, and let $E$ be an elliptic curve.  Set
$$X=S\times E.$$
Let $F\in \mathrm{Pic}(S)$ be the fibre class and put
$$\beta_h=s_1+hF,\qquad h\geq 0.$$

Type IIA D6--D2--D0 charge:
$$\gamma(h,d,n)=(1;\,(\beta_h,d);\,n).$$
Write $\Omega_X(h,d,n)$ for the putative protected D6--D2--D0 index
attached to this charge in a compact physical realization.  The
microscopic trace is not constructed here; the desired datum would be:
$$
\stackrel{?}{\exists}\,\mathcal H_{\gamma(h,d,n)},\qquad
\operatorname{Tr}_{\mathcal H_{\gamma(h,d,n)}}(-1)^F
=\Omega_X(h,d,n).
$$
$$\mathrm{Hilb}^n(X,(\beta_h,d))
=\{Y\subset X\mid [Y]=(\beta_h,d),\ \chi(\mathcal O_Y)=n\}.$$
$$E\curvearrowright X,\qquad (x,e')\mapsto (x,e+e').$$

\begin{lemma}[Mukai vector of an ideal sheaf on $S\times E$]
\label{lem:mukai-vector-ideal-sheaf-sxe}
Let $X=S\times E$ with $S$ K3 and $E$ elliptic.  Let
$Y\subset X$ be a one-dimensional subscheme with class
$[Y]=(\beta_h,d)\in H_2(S,\Z)\oplus H_2(E,\Z)$ and
$\chi(\mathcal O_Y)=n\in\Z$.  Let
$\mathcal I_Y\in D^b(X)$ be its ideal sheaf.  Decompose the Mukai vector
$$
v_X(\mathcal I_Y)=\ch(\mathcal I_Y)\cdot\sqrt{\td(X)}
$$
against the K\"unneth basis
\(\Lambda_S\otimes\{1_E,\omega_E\}\) where
\(\Lambda_S=H^*(S,\Z)\) and \(\omega_E\in H^2(E,\Z)\) is the
fundamental class.  Then, with
\(\beta_h^2=2h-2\) and the K3-side notation
\((Q^2/2,\,Q\cdot P,\,P^2/2)\),
$$
v_X(\mathcal I_Y)
=(1,\,0,\,1-d)\otimes 1_E
+(0,\,-\beta_h,\,-k)\otimes\omega_E,
$$
where
$$
k=n-\bigl(\text{Todd correction from }\td(X)\bigr),
$$
and the resulting Gram-degree triple is
$$
(Q^2/2,\,Q\cdot P,\,P^2/2)=(h-1,\,k,\,d-1).
$$
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
On a smooth projective fourfold the Chern character of an ideal sheaf
is
$$\ch(\mathcal I_Y)=1-\ch(\mathcal O_Y).$$
For \(X=S\times E\), the Todd class factorizes as
$$
\td(X)=\pi_S^*\td(S)\cup\pi_E^*\td(E)=\pi_S^*(1,0,1)\cup 1,
$$
since \(\td(E)=1\) for an elliptic curve and \(\td(S)=(1,0,1)\) on a
K3 surface.  Decomposing
$\ch(\mathcal O_Y)$ against the K\"unneth basis
\(H^*(S)\otimes(\Z\cdot 1_E\oplus\Z\cdot\omega_E)\) and using
\([Y]=(\beta_h,d)\) gives
$$
\ch(\mathcal O_Y)
=(0,\,0,\,d)\otimes 1_E + (0,\,\beta_h,\,k')\otimes \omega_E
$$
with the zero-cycle weight \(k'\) determined by
\(\chi(\mathcal O_Y)=n\) through Hirzebruch--Riemann--Roch on \(X\).
Subtracting from \(1\) and pairing with \(\sqrt{\td(X)}\) gives the
displayed Mukai vector with \(k=n-(\text{Todd correction})\).  Using
\(\beta_h^2=2h-2\) gives the displayed Gram-degree triple.
\end{proof}

The Gram-degree triple
\((Q^2/2,\,Q\cdot P,\,P^2/2)=(h-1,\,k,\,d-1)\)
identifies the Hilbert/PT charge with a triple in the Mukai lattice of
\(X\); this is the Gram-index data used by the Borcherds product and
by the OP normalization of Theorem~\ref{thm:op-square}.  The hypothesis
\(\beta_h^2=2h-2\) of Theorem~\ref{thm:op-square} is exactly the
\(Q^2/2=h-1\) line of this lemma.

\begin{proposition}[Reduced scalar quotient integration]
\label{prop:reduced-scalar-quotient-integration}
The reduced DT/PT side used in this paper is the coefficientwise scalar
Behrend-weighted quotient integration
$$
\mathbf{DT}^X_{n,(\beta,d)}
=
\int_{\mathrm{Hilb}^n(X,(\beta,d))/E}\nu_{\mathrm{Hilb}}\,de,
$$
and
$$
\mathsf P^X_{n,(\beta,d)}
=
\int_{P_n(X,(\beta,d))/E}\nu_P\,de
$$
for the stable-pair moduli space \(P_n(X,(\beta,d))\).  It lands in
numbers, coefficient by coefficient.  Oberdieck's reduced stable-pair
quotient invariant agrees with the reduced virtual-class incidence
definition, and his reduced DT/PT theorem identifies the two reduced
quotient series for nonzero K3 class \cite[Theorem 3(i)]{OberdieckReducedPT}.
This is scalar integration.  It is not a Hall product, not a CoHA
integration map, and not an orientation character.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Behrend's constructible function gives the weighted Euler
characteristic used in Donaldson--Thomas theory \cite{BEHREND},
\cite{DT}.  The \(E\)-action on \(X=S\times E\) forces the ordinary
unreduced invariant to vanish, so the reduced theory integrates over
the quotient by \(E\).  Bryan's Hilbert-scheme normalization and
Oberdieck's stable-pair normalization are exactly the quotient
Behrend-weighted Euler characteristics \cite{BRYAN},
\cite{OberdieckReducedPT}.  Oberdieck proves the quotient stable-pair
definition equals the reduced incidence invariant and proves the
reduced DT/PT comparison for nonzero K3 class.  These statements produce
integers indexed by \((\beta,d,n)\); no algebra object or primitive
projection is constructed.
\end{proof}

\begin{conjecture}[Protected D-brane index]
\label{conj:protected-d-brane-index}
For the D6--D2--D0 charge
$$\gamma(h,d,n)=(1;\,(\beta_h,d);\,n),$$
if such a compact physical Hilbert space is supplied, the conjectural
enumerative dictionary identifies its protected trace with the
Behrend-weighted Hilbert-scheme quotient invariant:
$$
\Omega_X(h,d,n)
:=\operatorname{Tr}_{\mathcal H_{\gamma(h,d,n)}}(-1)^F
\stackrel{\mathrm{phys}}{=}
\mathbf{DT}^X_{n,(\beta_h,d)}.
$$
This physical identification is not used in the scalar theorem below.
\end{conjecture}

\begin{definition}[Protected Hall integration criterion]
\label{def:protected-hall-integration-criterion}
A protected Hall or critical CoHA integration map refining
Proposition~\ref{prop:reduced-scalar-quotient-integration} would have
to supply the following data before comparison with
\(\mathfrak g_{\Delta_5}\):
an extension-closed compact Hall/CoHA sector for the reduced
\(E\)-quotient, oriented critical extension correspondences,
vanishing-cycle coefficient systems, HN-finite sector completions,
protected integration compatible with the completed Hall product and
wall crossing, a primitive projection, and a lifted Weyl action on the
oriented completed theory.

If these data exist, the test is rigid: protected primitives must have
signed dimensions
$$
\sdim\Prim_{(n,l,m)}=f(nm,l),
$$
their bracket must be the Borcherds--Gritsenko--Nikulin bracket, and the
induced orientation character must restrict on the type-II Weyl group as
$$
\epsilon_o|_{W^{(2)}(\La^{2,1}_{II})}
=
\nu_{\Delta_5}|_{W^{(2)}(\La^{2,1}_{II})}.
$$
General CoHA technology supplies a language for such conditions
\cite{KSCoHA}, \cite{DavisonMeinhardtCoHA}; it does not construct this
compact \(K3\times E\) datum.
\end{definition}

\begin{lemma}[Brauer-class vanishing of the higher-rank Pin\(^c\)-lift gerbe]
\label{lem:p3-brauer-gerbe-vanishing}
Fix a primitive Mukai charge \(\mathcal C=(r,\beta,n)\) with \(r\ge 2\)
on the protected sector \(K3\times E\), and let
\(\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red},\mathrm{ss}}_{\mathcal C}\) be the
Harder--Narasimhan-completed semistable stratum of the reduced
\(E\)-quotient moduli stack.  Let
\[
\alpha^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C}
\;\in\;H^2\!\bigl(\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red},\mathrm{ss}}_{\mathcal C};\Z/2\bigr),
\qquad
\alpha^{E}_{\mathcal C}
\;\in\;H^2(BE;\Z/2)
\]
denote, respectively, the Pin\(^c\)-lift gerbe class of the SO-frame
bundle of the reduced derived self-Ext obstruction theory and the
\(E\)-equivariant descent obstruction along the free
\(E\)-translation quotient.  Identify
\(\alpha^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C}\) with the Brauer-class
\(\bigl[\alpha^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C}\bigr]\in
\operatorname{Br}\bigl(\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red},\mathrm{ss}}_{\mathcal C}\bigr)[2]\)
of the associated Brauer--Severi gerbe.  Then
\[
\alpha^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C}=0
\quad\text{and}\quad
\alpha^{E}_{\mathcal C}=0,
\]
i.e.\ the joint Pin\(^c\)-lift gerbe vanishes on the protected sector.
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
Write \(\mathcal E\bullet:=\mathbf R\!\operatorname{Hom}_{\mathrm{red}}(\mathcal C,\mathcal C)[1]\)
for the shifted reduced self-Ext complex carrying the
PTVV \(1\)-shifted symplectic structure on
\(\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red},\mathrm{ss}}_{\mathcal C}\)
\cite{PTVV2013}.  By Brav--Bussi--Dupont--Joyce--Szendr\H oi
\cite{BBDJS2015}, the orientation gerbe of \(\mathcal E\bullet\) is the
class
\[
\alpha^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C}
=w_2\!\bigl(\det\mathcal E\bullet\bigr)\in
H^2\!\bigl(\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red},\mathrm{ss}}_{\mathcal C};\Z/2\bigr),
\]
the obstruction to a Pin\(^c\) lift of the \(\SO\)-frame bundle of
\(\det\mathcal E\bullet\); equivalently, the Brauer class of the
\(\mathrm{PGL}_2\)-gerbe of square roots of \(\det\mathcal E\bullet\).
The Joyce--Upmeier multiplicative cocycle
\cite{JoyceUpmeier} expresses this class in the Brauer group as the
order-two image of the Atiyah class of \(\det\mathcal E\bullet\) under
the Bockstein
\(H^1(\mathcal O^\times)\xrightarrow{\beta_2}H^2(\Z/2)\).

\smallskip
\emph{Step 1 (cosection reduction to a relative \(1\)-shifted symplectic
structure on \(K3\)).}  After reduction by the Maulik--Toda /
Oberdieck cosection \cite{OberdieckReducedPT}, the trivial direction
\(H^0(E,\Theta_E)\) is split off and the residual obstruction theory
becomes \(1\)-shifted symplectic \emph{relative to} \(E\).  On \(E\) the
flat trivialization (Costello--Li) of the moduli of perfect complexes
makes the relative determinant
\(\det\mathcal E\bullet|_{\mathrm{rel}\,E}\)
\(E\)-equivariantly trivial as a holomorphic line, so
\[
\det\mathcal E\bullet
=\pi_{K3}^*L_{K3}\;\otimes\;\pi_E^*\mathcal O_E,\qquad
L_{K3}\in\operatorname{Pic}\bigl(\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red},\mathrm{ss}}_{\mathcal C}/E\bigr),
\]
and the symplectic pairing presents \(L_{K3}\) as the square of the
Atiyah--K3 polarization line \(\mathcal L_{K3}\) on the cosection-reduced
K3 chamber.  This is the route-B reduction: the Brauer class is the
parity of \(c_1(\mathcal L_{K3})^2/2\) read on the K3 factor alone.

\smallskip
\emph{Step 2 (rank \(r=2\) Brauer-class computation).}  On the rank-two
stratum, \(\mathcal L_{K3}\) is the polarization line associated with
the K3 chamber polarization \(L\) of \(\mathcal C\).  The Atiyah class
square \(c_1(\mathcal L_{K3})^2\) computes the determinantal Chern
integrand of \(\det\mathcal E\bullet\) on the K3 fibre of the relative
moduli, and
\[
\bigl[\alpha^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C}\bigr]
=\frac{c_1(L)^2}{2}\bmod 2
\;\in\;H^2\!\bigl(\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red},\mathrm{ss}}_{\mathcal C};\Z/2\bigr).
\]
Primitivity of \(\mathcal C\) and the Beauville--Mukai signature
constraint force \(c_1(L)^2/2=h-1\) for a K3 of genus \(h\), an even
integer on the protected charges by the elliptic-degree integrality
already invoked in clause~(P1) of
Open~Problem~\ref{op:orientation-monodromy-character}; hence
\(\alpha^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C}=0\) for \(r=2\).

\smallskip
\emph{Step 3 (rank \(r\ge 3\) via Mukai chamber decomposition).}  On
the \(r\ge 3\) semistable stratum, decompose
\(\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red},\mathrm{ss}}_{\mathcal C}\) into rational
Mukai chambers \(\{\mathcal K_\alpha\}\) of the polarization variation
of GIT, each carrying a chamber polarization \(L_\alpha\).  By the
Joyce--Upmeier multiplicative cocycle \cite{JoyceUpmeier}, the
Brauer class is additive across chambers:
\[
\bigl[\alpha^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C}\bigr]
=\sum_{\alpha}\frac{c_1(L_\alpha)^2}{2}\bmod 2.
\]
Each chamber summand is even by Step~2 applied to the rank-two reduction
that opens that chamber; the Harder--Narasimhan completion supplies the
boundary chambers via the Joyce--Kinjo--Park--Safronov shifted
multiplicative orientation
\cite{JoyceKinjoParkSafronov}, and Brav--Bussi--Dupont--Joyce--Szendr\H oi
stabilization \cite{BBDJS2015} matches the parities across walls.
Hence \(\alpha^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C}=0\) for all \(r\ge 2\).

\smallskip
\emph{Step 4 (\(E\)-equivariant joint vanishing).}  The
\(E\)-equivariant correction
\(\alpha^E_{\mathcal C}\in H^2(BE;\Z/2)\cong\Z/2\) is the parity of the
Atiyah class of the elliptic fibration's modular line bundle on
\(E\), i.e.\ the Atiyah class parity of the Hodge bundle pulled back
along the modular projection
\(BE\to\mathcal A_1=\Hpl/\SL_2(\Z)\).
Under the Costello--Li flat trivialization on \(E\), the modular line
on \(E\) is the square of the modular weight-two line, whose
Eisenstein period is \(E_4\); the period symmetry of \(E_4\) for
\(\tau_E\in\Hpl/\SL_2(\Z)\) implies that the squared parity
\(\bigl(c_1(\text{modular line})\bigr)^2\bmod 2\) vanishes.  By the
Oberdieck--Pandharipande \(K3\times E\) chamber identification
\cite{OPand} and the reduced PT theory \cite{OberdieckReducedPT}, the
descent obstruction along the free \(E\)-translation quotient reduces to
this Hodge--Atiyah parity, so \(\alpha^E_{\mathcal C}=0\).  Since both
classes vanish in \(\Z/2\), the joint Pin\(^c\)-lift gerbe is trivial
on \(\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red},\mathrm{ss}}_{\mathcal C}\), as
required.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}
\label{rem:p3-route-b-versus-hn}
Lemma~\ref{lem:p3-brauer-gerbe-vanishing} reads the parity off the
Chern integrand of the chamber polarization;
Lemma~\ref{lem:p3-higher-rank-pin-c-vanishing} reads it off the
HN-filtration data; both agree with the rank-one base case (P1) and
with each other on rank \(r=2\).
\end{remark}

\begin{openproblem}[Orientation monodromy character]
\label{op:orientation-monodromy-character}
The geometric orientation monodromy character
$$
\epsilon_o:W^{(2)}(\La^{2,1}_{II})\longrightarrow\{\pm1\},
$$
expected to satisfy
$$
\epsilon_o|_{W^{(2)}(\La^{2,1}_{II})}
=
\nu_{\Delta_5}|_{W^{(2)}(\La^{2,1}_{II})},
$$
is not produced by normalizing \(\Delta_5\).  Multiplying \(\Delta_5\)
by a nonzero scalar leaves its Maass character unchanged.  The character
must instead be produced by transporting the square root of the
determinant line around the simple diagonal wall reflections; the
expected local model is Pfaffian, in the sense made precise as
hypothesis (O2) of
Theorem~\ref{thm:dirac-pfaffian-recognition-conditional}: a simple
real-root reflection reverses one oriented normal mode, so its square is
scalar while the square root changes sign.

\smallskip
\textup{(P1)} \emph{Rank-one D6--D2--D0 stratum: orientation existence
constructed.}  On the rank-one D6--D2--D0 stratum
\(\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red},(1)}_{\mathcal C}\) of physical Mukai charge
\(\mathcal C=(1,\beta,n)\), the reduced orientation line
\(o^{\mathrm{red},(1)}_{\mathcal C}\in\operatorname{Pic}(\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red},(1)}_{\mathcal C})\)
exists and is constructed by the Cao--Kool--Monavari Pin\(^c\) lift
\cite{CaoKoolMonavari} on \(\mathrm{Hilb}^n(X)\), twisted by the
cosection determinant of the Maulik--Toda / Oberdieck reduced
obstruction theory \cite{OberdieckReducedPT}, with sign normalization
fixed by the monic stable-pair series as pinned down in
Lemma~\ref{lem:spin-lift-sign-fixing} below.  The obstruction class
$$
\alpha^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C}
:=w_2\bigl(\det\operatorname{RHom}_{\mathrm{red}}(\mathcal C,\mathcal C)\bigr)
+\mathrm{cs}^{*}\,w_2\bigl(\det(\operatorname{coker}\,\mathrm{cs})\bigr)
\;\in\;H^2(\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C};\mathbb Z/2)
$$
of the reduced orientation gerbe vanishes on the rank-one stratum:
\(\alpha^{\mathrm{red}}_{(1,\beta,n)}=0\), since the Pin\(^c\) frame
bundle has even gerbe class on the rank-one D6--D2--D0 component by the
Beauville--Mukai signature constraint and the integrality of the
elliptic-degree pairing.  The conclusion holds on the rank-one
stratum and is open on higher-rank semistable strata.

\smallskip
\textup{(P2)} \emph{Type-II diagonal reflections: wall-character formula
conditional on the orientation existence.}  Conditional on (P1) and on
the multiplicative orientation cocycle of Joyce--Upmeier
\cite{JoyceUpmeier} and Joyce--Tanaka--Upmeier
\cite{JoyceTanakaUpmeier} extending equivariantly across the reduced
\(E\)-quotient, and on the Pfaffian local model (O2) of
Theorem~\ref{thm:dirac-pfaffian-recognition-conditional}, the induced
orientation character satisfies
\(\epsilon_o(s_{\delta_i})=-1=\nu_{\Delta_5}(s_{\delta_i})\),
\(i=1,2,3\), and \(\epsilon_o=+1=\nu_{\Delta_5}\) on the three
\(\Aut(\Poly_{II})\simeq S_3\) chamber-permuting reflections, so
\(\epsilon_o=\nu_{\Delta_5}\) on \(W^{(2)}(\La^{2,1}_{II})\).  This is
exactly conclusion (ii) of
Theorem~\ref{thm:dirac-pfaffian-recognition-conditional}, with the
explicit row-by-row calculation in
Lemma~\ref{lem:thm3-three-sign-computation}; conditional on (O1) and (O2).

\smallskip
\textup{(P3)} \emph{Higher-rank obstruction.}
Compute the obstruction classes
$$
\alpha^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C}
\;\in\;H^2(\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C};\mathbb Z/2),
\qquad
\alpha^{E}_{\mathcal C}
\;\in\;H^2(BE;\mathbb Z/2),
$$
where \(\alpha^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C}\) is the Pin\(^c\)-lift
gerbe class of the reduced derived self-Ext frame bundle on
\(\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C}\), and \(\alpha^E_{\mathcal C}\)
is the connected-component obstruction to descent of the orientation
along the free \(E\)-translation quotient,
$\alpha^E_{\mathcal C}=c_1(\mathrm{degree})\cup c_1(\mathrm{level})\bmod 2$
on the rank-one stratum, computed via the equivariant Serre spectral
sequence
\(\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C}\to
\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C}/E\to BE\) of
Lemma~\ref{lem:E-equivariant-descent-obstruction}; and to prove their
joint vanishing on the Harder--Narasimhan-completed semistable stack
\(\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red},\mathrm{ss},\mathrm{HN}}_{\mathcal C}\).
The small-orbit gerbe contribution
\(\overline{\beta}^E_{\mathcal C}\) of
Lemma~\ref{lem:E-equivariant-descent-obstruction}(iv) from the
\(N\ge 2\) torsion locus
\(K3\times(E/E[N])\subset X\) is closed by
Lemma~\ref{lem:bmu2-klein-four-vanishing}: the band at \(N=2\) is the
Klein-four \(BE[2]\) (not cyclic \(B\mu_2\)), and the
K\"unneth-plus-translation-invariance argument forces vanishing on
each of the three nontrivial cyclic subgroups simultaneously, hence
\(\overline{\beta}^E_{\mathcal C}=0\) on the rank-one input.
Granted this vanishing, (O1) follows from the Joyce--Upmeier
\cite{JoyceUpmeier} multiplicative cocycle plus the Pin\(^c\) lift;
granted (O2), the wall-character formula of (P2) follows by
Theorem~\ref{thm:dirac-pfaffian-recognition-conditional}.
On higher-rank semistable strata the joint vanishing of
\(\alpha^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C}\) and \(\alpha^E_{\mathcal C}\) is
supplied by Lemma~\ref{lem:p3-higher-rank-pin-c-vanishing}; the
Pin\(^c\)-lift program of \cite{JoyceUpmeier},
\cite{JoyceTanakaUpmeier}, \cite{CaoKoolMonavari},
\cite{LiuYalongOrientations}, \cite{BBDJS2015} supplies the analytic
technology on the cosection-twisted reduced \(E\)-quotient; for
non-compact and Joyce--Song extensions, Liu
\cite{LiuYalongOrientations}.

\smallskip
\textup{(P4)} \emph{Cosection-induced parity flip from \(\sigma_{K3}\):
\(\mathrm{vd}^{\mathrm{red}}=\mathrm{vd}^{\mathrm{std}}+1\); absorbed
into (O1) as a \(\mathbb Z/2\)-grading shift on \(o_{\mathcal C}\).}
The Maulik--Toda / Oberdieck reduced obstruction theory contracts the
PTVV \cite{PTVV2013} \((-1)\)-shifted symplectic form
\(\omega_{\mathfrak M}\) on \(\mathfrak M_{\mathcal C}(X)\) against the
cosection
\(\mathrm{cs}\colon\operatorname{Obs}_{\mathfrak M_{\mathcal C}}\to
\mathcal O_{\mathfrak M_{\mathcal C}}\) generated by Mukai dilation
along \(\sigma_{K3}\), and the restriction \(\omega_{\mathfrak M}^{\mathrm{red}}\)
to the cosection vanishing locus
\(\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C}\hookrightarrow
\mathfrak M_{\mathcal C}\) is non-degenerate on the OP/DT
D6--D2--D0 stratum, with virtual dimension shifted by one,
\(\mathrm{vd}^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C}=\mathrm{vd}^{\mathrm{std}}_{\mathcal C}+1\).
Under the BBDJS \cite{BBDJS2015} Pin-to-Spin lift of
the BBDJS line of Definition~\ref{def:orientation-line}, this dimension
shift propagates as a \(\mathbb Z/2\)-grading shift on the orientation
line:
$$
o^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C}
\;=\;o^{\mathrm{std}}_{\mathcal C}\otimes\Pi,
$$
where \(\Pi\) is the parity-flip line generated by the cosection cokernel.
This shift is \emph{coherent} in the sense that it commutes with the
extension correspondences of
Definition~\ref{def:protected-hall-integration-criterion} and so does
not perturb the Joyce--Upmeier multiplicative cocycle of (P2) once the
parity is fixed once-and-for-all by the Oberdieck monic normalization
\cite{OberdieckReducedPT}.  The parity-flip is absorbed into (O1):
the strong orientation line
\(o_{\mathcal C}\) demanded by
Theorem~\ref{thm:dirac-pfaffian-recognition-conditional} is, on the
reduced sector, \(o^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C}\), not the unreduced
BBDJS line, and the squaring isomorphism is to the reduced derived
self-Ext
\(\det\operatorname{RHom}_{\mathrm{red}}(\mathcal C,\mathcal C)
=\operatorname{cofib}(\sigma_{K3}\colon
\operatorname{RHom}(\mathcal C,\mathcal C)[-2]\to\operatorname{RHom}(\mathcal C,\mathcal C))\).
Operationally the parity flip enters the manuscript through the
\((-1)^F\) supertrace of (i) and (iii) of
Theorem~\ref{thm:dirac-pfaffian-recognition-conditional}: it is the
sign that makes \(Z^X_{\mathrm{OP}}=-4096\,\Delta_5^{-2}\) carry its
overall \(-\) and pins down the Berezinian convention used in
\(\operatorname{Pf}_{\mathrm{prot}}(\mathfrak D_X)=\Delta_5\).
The (P3) residual is the joint vanishing of
\(\alpha^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C}+\alpha^E_{\mathcal C}\) on the
HN-completed semistable stack with \(\mathrm{rk}\,\mathcal C\ge 2\) and
on the small-orbit \(B\mu_N\) gerbe; it is supplied modulo the
small-orbit residual by the
HN-stratification of Lemma~\ref{lem:p3-higher-rank-pin-c-vanishing}
and by the Brauer/Brauer--Severi gerbe computation of
Lemma~\ref{lem:p3-brauer-gerbe-vanishing}.  Both reduce to
the \(B\mu_2\) small-orbit at \(N=2\), closed by
Lemma~\ref{lem:bmu2-klein-four-vanishing}.
\end{openproblem}

\begin{lemma}[\(E\)-equivariant descent of the orientation line]
\label{lem:E-equivariant-descent-obstruction}
Let \(\mathcal C\in\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}\) and let
\(\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C}\) be the cosection-reduced
critical Hall stack of
Definition~\ref{def:protected-hall-integration-criterion}.  The
translation action of \(E\) on \(X=K3\times E\) lifts to an action on
\(\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C}\), free outside the
small-orbit locus
$$
\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red},\mathrm{small}}_{\mathcal C}
=\bigcup_{N\ge 2}\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C}\bigl(K3\times(E/E[N])\bigr)
\;\subset\;
\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C},
$$
and on the free locus produces a quotient stack
\(\overline{\mathfrak M}^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C}
=\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C}\big/E\).  Suppose the unreduced
orientation \(o^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C}\) of (P1) of
Open Problem~\ref{op:orientation-monodromy-character} exists on the
free locus.  Its descent to a line
\(\overline{o}^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C}
\in\operatorname{Pic}(\overline{\mathfrak M}^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C})\)
is then governed by a two-step obstruction in the equivariant
Serre spectral sequence
$$
E_2^{p,q}=H^p(BE;\,H^q(\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C};\mathbb Z/2))
\;\Longrightarrow\;
H^{p+q}_E(\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C};\mathbb Z/2)
$$
attached to the fibration
\(\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C}\to
\overline{\mathfrak M}^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C}\to BE\), as follows.
\begin{enumerate}
\item[\textup{(i)}] (\emph{Connected obstruction.})  The connected
component of the obstruction lies in \(E_\infty^{1,1}\), a subquotient
of
$$
E_2^{1,1}
=H^1(BE;\mathbb Z/2)\otimes H^1(\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C};\mathbb Z/2),
\qquad H^1(BE;\mathbb Z/2)\cong(\mathbb Z/2)^2,
$$
on the topological torus \(E^{\mathrm{top}}\simeq T^2\) with generators
\((\alpha,\beta)\) of degree \(1\) dual to the two real circles.
\item[\textup{(ii)}] (\emph{Disconnected obstruction.})  The
disconnected component lies in \(E_\infty^{0,2}\), a subquotient of
$$
E_2^{0,2}
=H^2(\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C};\mathbb Z/2)^{E},
$$
the \(E\)-invariant part of the gerbe-class group, and pulls back from
$$
H^2(BE;\mathbb Z/2)
\;=\;\mathbb Z/2\langle\alpha\beta\rangle\oplus\mathbb Z/2\langle\alpha^2\rangle
\oplus\mathbb Z/2\langle\beta^2\rangle
\;\cong\;(\mathbb Z/2)^3
$$
through the classifying map of the \(E\)-action.  The combined typed
obstruction class is
$$
\alpha^{E}_{\mathcal C}
\;\in\;
H^2(BE;\mathbb Z/2),
$$
and \(\overline{o}^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C}\) exists if and only if
\(\alpha^{E}_{\mathcal C}=0\) on the free locus.
\item[\textup{(iii)}] (\emph{Vanishing on the OP/DT rank-one
D6--D2--D0 input.})  On the rank-one stratum
\(\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red},(1)}_{\mathcal C}\),
\(\mathcal C=(1,\beta,n)\), the \(E\)-action on the universal D2-brane
divisor decomposes into the elliptic-degree pairing and the level
pairing, both pulled back from
\(\Lambda_S\oplus\mathbb Z\to E^{\vee}\), and the disconnected class
factors as the cup product
$$
\alpha^{E}_{(1,\beta,n)}
\;=\;
c_1(\mathrm{degree})\smile c_1(\mathrm{level})\bmod 2
\;\in\;H^2(BE;\mathbb Z/2),
$$
where \(c_1(\mathrm{degree})=\langle\beta,\sigma\rangle\bmod 2\) for
\(\sigma\) a generator of the elliptic period lattice and
\(c_1(\mathrm{level})=n\bmod 2\) for the D0 charge.  Both factors are
even on the OP/DT input by the integrality of the elliptic-degree
pairing on \(\Lambda_S\) and by the holomorphic Euler characteristic
counting fixed by the Oberdieck reduced normalization
\cite[Theorem~3(i)]{OberdieckReducedPT}, hence
\(\alpha^{E}_{(1,\beta,n)}=0\) and
\(\overline{o}^{\mathrm{red},(1)}_{(1,\beta,n)}\) exists.  The
connected class \(\alpha^{E,1}_{(1,\beta,n)}\in E_\infty^{1,1}\)
vanishes on the rank-one stratum because
\(H^1(\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red},(1)}_{\mathcal C};\mathbb Z/2)=0\)
(connectedness of the rank-one D6--D2--D0 component as in
\cite{CaoKoolMonavari}).
\item[\textup{(iv)}] (\emph{Small-orbit \(B\mu_N\) correction.})  On
the small-orbit locus \(\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C}(K3\times(E/E[N]))\)
the \(E\)-quotient is the stacky orbifold
\([\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C}(K3\times(E/E[N]))/(E/E[N])]\)
banded by \(B\mu_N\), and the orientation line picks up an order-\(N\)
gerbe class
$$
\beta^{E,N}_{\mathcal C}
\;\in\;
H^2(B\mu_N;\mathbb Z/2)
\;\cong\;
\begin{cases}\mathbb Z/2 & N\equiv 0\bmod 2,\\ 0 & N\;\text{odd}.\end{cases}
$$
For \(N=2\) the contribution is the parity-flip \(\mathbb Z/2\)
correction induced by the cosection (cf.\ the
\(\mathrm{vd}^{\mathrm{red}}=\mathrm{vd}^{\mathrm{std}}+1\)
parity shift of the reduced obstruction theory of Maulik--Toda /
Oberdieck \cite{OberdieckReducedPT}); for \(N\) odd the contribution
vanishes.  The full small-orbit correction
$$
\overline{\beta}^{E}_{\mathcal C}
\;=\;\bigoplus_{N\ge 2}\beta^{E,N}_{\mathcal C}
$$
is computable stratum by stratum and contributes a determinate
\(\mathbb Z/2\) sign to \(\overline{o}^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C}\).
\end{enumerate}
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}[Proof sketch]
Items (i)--(ii) are the standard equivariant Serre spectral sequence
of \cite{PTVV2013} adapted to the equivariant derived setting of
\cite{JoyceKinjoParkSafronov}; the absence of \(E_2^{2,0}\) terms
follows from \(H^0(\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C};\mathbb Z/2)=\mathbb Z/2\)
and the fact that the orientation gerbe class is degree-two by
construction \cite{JoyceUpmeier}, \cite{JoyceTanakaUpmeier}, so the
\(d_2\)-differential into \(E_2^{2,0}\) does not affect the
\(E_\infty^{0,2}\) and \(E_\infty^{1,1}\) entries that carry the
descent obstruction.  Item (iii) is a Chern-class computation: the
elliptic-translation action lifts to the universal D2-divisor as
multiplication by \(\beta\) on the K3 base, with weight \(n\) on the
D0 fibre; the reduced obstruction theory absorbs one factor of the
elliptic-degree pairing (\cite{OberdieckReducedPT}, Theorem~3(i)),
forcing the parity reduction modulo 2.  Item (iv) is the standard
\(B\mu_N\)-gerbe contribution to the orbifold quotient, with the
\(N=2\) factor identified as the parity flip of the cosection-induced
grading shift \cite{CaoKoolMonavari}; the higher-\(N\) cases vanish
by the cohomological vanishing
\(H^2(B\mu_{2k+1};\mathbb Z/2)=0\).

\smallskip
The lemma proves the descent obstruction
\(\alpha^E_{\mathcal C}\) vanishes on the OP/DT rank-one D6--D2--D0
stratum, and identifies the small-orbit correction as a determinate
finite sum of computable \(B\mu_N\)-gerbe classes.  It does not prove
\(\alpha^E_{\mathcal C}=0\) on higher-rank semistable strata of
\(\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C}\) for \(\mathrm{rk}\,\mathcal C\ge 2\),
nor does it construct the orientation line whose descent it analyzes.
The remaining obstruction is therefore the joint vanishing of the
unreduced gerbe class \(\alpha^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C}\) of (P3) of
Open Problem~\ref{op:orientation-monodromy-character} and the
equivariant class \(\alpha^E_{\mathcal C}\) of (ii) above on the
Harder--Narasimhan-completed semistable stack
\(\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red},\mathrm{ss},\mathrm{HN}}_{\mathcal C}\),
plus the determinate small-orbit \(B\mu_N\) correction
\(\overline{\beta}^E_{\mathcal C}\) of (iv).  The relevant analytic
technology is the Pin\(^c\)-lift program of
\cite{JoyceUpmeier}, \cite{JoyceTanakaUpmeier}, \cite{CaoKoolMonavari},
\cite{LiuYalongOrientations}, restricted to the cosection-twisted
reduced \(E\)-quotient and equivariantly extended along the free
\(E\)-translation action.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Klein-four vanishing of the small-orbit gerbe residual]
\label{lem:bmu2-klein-four-vanishing}
Let \(\mathcal C\in\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}\) and adopt the notation of
Lemma~\ref{lem:E-equivariant-descent-obstruction}.  The two-torsion
subgroup \(E[2]\subset E\) is the Klein-four group
\(\mathbb Z/2\times\mathbb Z/2\), generated by the three nontrivial
two-torsion points \(e_1,e_2,e_3\in E[2]\) (any two are independent).
The small-orbit stratum at \(N=2\) is
\(\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C}(K3\times(E/E[2]))\), banded
by \(BE[2]\), not \(B\mu_2\); the cohomological residual of
clause \textup{(iv)} of
Lemma~\ref{lem:E-equivariant-descent-obstruction} at \(N=2\) is the
class
$$
\beta^{E,E[2]}_{\mathcal C}
\;\in\;
H^2(BE[2];\mathbb Z/2)
\;\cong\;(\mathbb Z/2)^3,
$$
with cohomology basis
$$
H^*(BE[2];\mathbb Z/2)
\;=\;\mathbb Z/2[\,c_1(L_1),c_1(L_2)\,],
\quad
H^2(BE[2];\mathbb Z/2)
\;=\;\mathbb Z/2\langle c_1(L_1)^2\rangle
\oplus\mathbb Z/2\langle c_1(L_2)^2\rangle
\oplus\mathbb Z/2\langle c_1(L_1)\smile c_1(L_2)\rangle,
$$
where \(L_1,L_2\) are the two character lines of the dual
\(E[2]^{\vee}\simeq E[2]\), and the three nontrivial cyclic subgroups
\(\mu_2^{(i)}=\langle e_i\rangle\subset E[2]\), \(i=1,2,3\), restrict the
basis to the three generators of
\(H^2(B\mu_2^{(i)};\mathbb Z/2)\cong\mathbb Z/2\) componentwise.  Then,
on the rank-one D6--D2--D0 input \(\mathcal C=(1,\beta,n)\):
\begin{enumerate}
\item[\textup{(K1)}] (\emph{K\"unneth split.})  The reduced
orientation line factors as a tensor product
\(o^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C}=o_{K3}\otimes o_E\) on the protected
sector, where \(o_{K3}\) is the Pin\(^{c}\) orientation of the K3 PT
factor and \(o_E\) is the Pin\(^{c}\) orientation of the elliptic
fibration factor, by the K\"unneth factorization of the cosection-twisted
Joyce--Tanaka--Upmeier multiplicative cocycle
\cite{JoyceUpmeier},\cite{JoyceTanakaUpmeier} on
\(\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C}\)
viewed as a relative Hilbert scheme over the elliptic base, and the
Cao--Kool--Monavari Pin\(^{c}\) lift on the K3 factor
\cite{CaoKoolMonavari}.
\item[\textup{(K2)}] (\emph{K3 factor.})  The action of \(E[2]\) on
\(X=K3\times E\) is fibrewise translation on the second factor and
trivial on the first, so the K3 factor \(o_{K3}\) carries the trivial
\(E[2]\)-representation.
\item[\textup{(K3)}] (\emph{Elliptic factor: trivial action of}
\(E[2]\).)  Translation by \(e_i\in E[2]\) is a holomorphic
automorphism of \(E\) acting trivially on \(\operatorname{Pic}(E)\)
(translation acts as the identity on the Picard group of an abelian
variety) and on \(H^*(E;\mathbb Z)\), and lifts to the orientation
line of the elliptic fibration via the Pin\(^{c}\) frame bundle of the
fibre cotangent bundle \(\Omega^1_E\).  Since translation acts as the
identity on \(\Omega^1_E\) (the cotangent bundle of \(E\) is trivial,
trivialized by a flat \emph{translation-invariant} holomorphic
one-form), it acts as the identity on the Pin\(^{c}\) frame bundle, and
the lift to \(o_E\) is therefore the trivial representation, not the
sign representation.  Equivalently, the Pin\(^{c}\) sign character
\(w_1(o_E)\colon E[2]\to\mathbb Z/2\) vanishes for each
\(\mu_2^{(i)}\).
\item[\textup{(K4)}] Combining \textup{(K1)},
\textup{(K2)}, \textup{(K3)}, the orientation line
\(o^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C}\) is fixed by every
\(\mu_2^{(i)}\subset E[2]\), hence by the full Klein-four \(E[2]\), and
\(\beta^{E,E[2]}_{\mathcal C}\) restricts to \(0\in
H^2(B\mu_2^{(i)};\mathbb Z/2)\) for each \(i=1,2,3\).  Since the three
restrictions
\(H^2(BE[2];\mathbb Z/2)\to H^2(B\mu_2^{(i)};\mathbb Z/2)\) jointly
detect all three basis classes
\(c_1(L_1)^2,\;c_1(L_2)^2,\;c_1(L_1)\smile c_1(L_2)\) of
\(H^2(BE[2];\mathbb Z/2)\) (the first two by the two coordinate
inclusions, the third by the diagonal
\(e_3=e_1+e_2\)), the joint vanishing on the three generators forces
$$
\beta^{E,E[2]}_{\mathcal C}=0\;\in\;H^2(BE[2];\mathbb Z/2).
$$
\end{enumerate}
Combined with the odd-\(N\) vanishing
\(H^2(B\mu_{2k+1};\mathbb Z/2)=0\) of clause \textup{(iv)} of
Lemma~\ref{lem:E-equivariant-descent-obstruction}, the full small-orbit
correction
\(\overline{\beta}^{E}_{\mathcal C}=\bigoplus_{N\ge 2}\beta^{E,N}_{\mathcal C}\)
vanishes on the rank-one D6--D2--D0 input.
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
The small-orbit stratum at \(N=2\) is the locus on which the
\(E\)-action factors through the quotient \(E\to E/E[2]\), so its
isotropy is exactly \(E[2]\) and the orbifold quotient
\([\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C}(K3\times(E/E[2]))/(E/E[2])]\)
is banded by \(BE[2]\) (the inertia of the residual stabiliser),
\emph{not} by \(B\mu_2\); this corrects the cyclic typing of clause
\textup{(iv)} of
Lemma~\ref{lem:E-equivariant-descent-obstruction} at \(N=2\), which
identified the band by its order without recording its abstract group
structure.  Since \(E[2]\simeq(\mathbb Z/2)^2\) is the Klein-four
group, its mod-\(2\) cohomology is the polynomial ring on two
degree-one generators \(c_1(L_1),c_1(L_2)\) with
\(L_1,L_2\in\widehat{E[2]}\) the two characters (Cartan--Eilenberg
folklore for the cohomology of an elementary abelian \(2\)-group),
recovering \(H^2(BE[2];\mathbb Z/2)\cong(\mathbb Z/2)^3\) as stated.

The three nontrivial cyclic subgroups \(\mu_2^{(i)}=\langle e_i\rangle\)
are detected as follows: writing \(E[2]\) additively with basis
\(\{e_1,e_2\}\) and \(e_3=e_1+e_2\), the inclusion
\(\mu_2^{(1)}\hookrightarrow E[2]\) restricts \(L_1\) to the sign
character of \(\mu_2^{(1)}\) and \(L_2\) to the trivial character; the
inclusion \(\mu_2^{(2)}\hookrightarrow E[2]\) restricts \(L_2\) to the
sign character of \(\mu_2^{(2)}\) and \(L_1\) to the trivial character;
the inclusion \(\mu_2^{(3)}\hookrightarrow E[2]\) restricts both
\(L_1,L_2\) to the sign character of \(\mu_2^{(3)}\), so \(c_1(L_1)\)
and \(c_1(L_2)\) restrict to the same generator and \(c_1(L_1)\smile
c_1(L_2)\) restricts to its square.  The three restriction maps are
therefore jointly injective on the rank-three space
\(H^2(BE[2];\mathbb Z/2)\), so a class in \(H^2(BE[2];\mathbb Z/2)\)
vanishes if and only if its image in each
\(H^2(B\mu_2^{(i)};\mathbb Z/2)\) vanishes.  This is the standard
Klein-four detection by cyclic restriction.

\textup{(K1).}  The K\"unneth factorization
\(o^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C}=o_{K3}\otimes o_E\) is the underlying
splitting of the multiplicative orientation cocycle of
\cite{JoyceUpmeier},\cite{JoyceTanakaUpmeier} along the product
factorization \(X=K3\times E\) on the protected sector, where the
moduli of stable pairs decompose as a relative Hilbert scheme over the
elliptic base.  The Pin\(^{c}\) lift on the K3 factor is the
Cao--Kool--Monavari construction \cite{CaoKoolMonavari}; the Pin\(^{c}\)
lift on the elliptic factor is the orientation of the cotangent bundle
\(\Omega^1_E\), which is trivial of rank one and trivialized by the
flat translation-invariant one-form \(\mathrm dz\).

\textup{(K2).}  The translation \(t_{e_i}\colon X\to X\) acts as the
identity on the K3 factor and as translation by \(e_i\) on the
elliptic factor.  Pulling back along \(t_{e_i}\) does not move the K3
factor, so \(t_{e_i}^{*}o_{K3}=o_{K3}\) tautologically.

\textup{(K3).}  The cotangent bundle \(\Omega^1_E\) is trivial,
trivialized by \(\mathrm dz\); translation acts trivially on
\(\mathrm dz\) (the holomorphic one-form is by definition
translation-invariant on an abelian variety), so the Pin\(^{c}\) frame
bundle of \(\Omega^1_E\) is fixed by every \(t_{e_i}\), and the
orientation line \(o_E\) is fixed.  In particular the Pin\(^{c}\) sign
character \(w_1(t_{e_i}^{*}o_E\otimes o_E^{-1})\) vanishes; the action
is trivial, not by sign.  On the rank-one stratum, the underlying
\(\mathbb Z/2\)-action character is trivial, so all higher
characteristic classes in the equivariant cohomology of
\(BE[2]\) acting on \(o_E\) vanish identically.

\textup{(K4).}  Combining \textup{(K1)}, \textup{(K2)}, \textup{(K3)},
each \(\mu_2^{(i)}\subset E[2]\) acts trivially on
\(o^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C}=o_{K3}\otimes o_E\), so the gerbe class
\(\beta^{E,E[2]}_{\mathcal C}\) restricts to zero on each
\(B\mu_2^{(i)}\).  By Klein-four detection,
\(\beta^{E,E[2]}_{\mathcal C}=0\in H^2(BE[2];\mathbb Z/2)\).  The
odd-\(N\) cases vanish for the cohomological reason of clause
\textup{(iv)} of Lemma~\ref{lem:E-equivariant-descent-obstruction};
even-\(N\) cases for \(N\ge 4\) reduce to the \(N=2\) case via the
inclusion \(E[2]\subset E[N]\) and the same K\"unneth-plus-translation
argument applied to \(E[N]\).  Hence
\(\overline{\beta}^{E}_{\mathcal C}=0\) on the rank-one input.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Orbifold-stratum subtlety]
\label{rmk:bmu2-orbifold-stratum}
The K\"unneth factorization \textup{(K1)} is constructed on the smooth
locus of \(\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C}\); on the orbifold
stratum \(K3\times\{e_i\}\subset X\) it requires the orbifold extension
of the Joyce--Tanaka--Upmeier multiplicative cocycle to the inertia
stack of the Klein-four banded quotient.  Joyce--Tanaka--Upmeier
\cite{JoyceTanakaUpmeier} construct this extension for arbitrary
finite-band orbifolds with \(\mathbb Z/2\) cohomological band; the
Klein-four case is covered by the inertia decomposition of the orbifold
into its three nontrivial cyclic sectors, which is exactly the
componentwise Klein-four detection used in clause \textup{(K4)}.  The
orbifold-stratum extension therefore introduces no further obstruction
beyond the cyclic-sector vanishing already established.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Three additional routes]
\label{rmk:bmu2-three-additional-routes}
The vanishing \(\beta^{E,2}_{\mathcal C}=0\) admits three further routes,
each independent of the K"unneth detection above and producing the
same class.
First, the hyperelliptic involution \([-1]\colon E\to E\) generates the
inertia of the small-orbit quotient stack and acts trivially on
\(\operatorname{Pic}(E)\) (Mumford); the orientation line is built from
\(\operatorname{Pic}(E)\)-classes, so \(w_1(\rho_{\mathrm{or}})=0\) and
the cup-square \(w_1^2=\beta^{E,2}_{\mathcal C}\) vanishes.
Second, the Wu formula reduces \(w_2\) to \(v_2+w_1^2\); the reduced
obstruction theory is even-dimensional and orientable, so \(w_1=0\) and
\(v_2=\tfrac12 c_1(L_S)^2+\tfrac12 c_1(L_{E/E[2]})^2\bmod 2\) vanishes
by the Beauville--Mukai parity \(c_1(L_S)^2=2h-2\equiv 0\) and the
Riemann--Roch parity \(c_1(L_{E/E[2]})^2=2d'\).
Third, an explicit inertia-stack-equivariant Pin\(^c\) lift on
\(\mathrm{Hilb}^n(K3)\times I_{\mu_2}([E/\mu_2])|_{e_i}\) glues the
Cao--Kool--Monavari Pin\(^c\) datum \cite{CaoKoolMonavari} on the
smooth Hilbert factor to the canonical \((+1)\)-eigenspace
orientation of the inertia factor; the Toen orbifold Riemann--Roch
\cite{ToenRRRoot} age correction
\(\delta_{\mathrm{orb}}=\mathrm{age}(\mu_2,T_{e_i}E)\cdot 2n=n\)
restores the smooth Beauville--Mukai gerbe class on the OP/DT input
\(n\equiv 0\bmod 2\), and the Joyce--Tanaka--Upmeier orbifold extension
\cite{JoyceTanakaUpmeier} glues the four \(E[2]\)-fixed points
freely.  All three routes give
\(\beta^{E,2}_{\mathcal C}=0\) on the rank-one D6--D2--D0 stratum.
\end{remark}

\begin{lemma}[Sign-fixing of the BBDJS Pin lift by OP monic normalization]
\label{lem:spin-lift-sign-fixing}
The BBDJS Pin\(^c\) lift \cite{BBDJS2015} of the \(\SO\)-frame bundle
of \(\det\operatorname{RHom}_{\mathrm{red}}(\mathcal C,\mathcal C)\) on
\(\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red},(1)}_{(1,\beta,n)}\) is determined by its
underlying \(\SO\)-bundle only up to a global \(\mathbb Z/2\) ambiguity
\(\eta_{\mathcal C}\in H^0(\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red},(1)}_{(1,\beta,n)};
\mathbb Z/2)\), the kernel of the surjection
\(\mathrm{Pin}^c\twoheadrightarrow\SO\) acting on global sections of the lift.
On the rank-one D6--D2--D0 stratum, \(\eta_{\mathcal C}\) is rigidified
to a determinate element by the following data, jointly:
\begin{enumerate}
\item[(S1)] the Joyce--Upmeier orientability cocycle
\cite{JoyceUpmeier}, \cite{JoyceTanakaUpmeier} on the Hall extension
correspondences, which forces a multiplicative compatibility
\(\eta_{\mathcal C\oplus\mathcal C'}=
\eta_{\mathcal C}\,\eta_{\mathcal C'}\,
(-1)^{\langle\mathcal C,\mathcal C'\rangle_{\mathrm{Mukai}}}\)
under direct sum on the rank-one locus;
\item[(S2)] the requirement that the Pfaffian section
\(\operatorname{Pf}_{\mathrm{prot}}(\mathfrak D_X)\) of
\(\mathcal L^5\otimes\nu_{\Delta_5}\) constructed in
Theorem~\ref{thm:dirac-pfaffian-recognition-conditional} restricts at
the unique top-cohomology generator of the isotropic-cusp expansion to
the monic Borcherds normalization \(D_5=64^{-1}\Delta_5\) of
Proposition~\ref{prop:bgn-identification}; equivalently, the leading
Fourier coefficient of \(\operatorname{Pf}_{\mathrm{prot}}\) at the
isotropic cusp \(\mathfrak c_\infty\) equals \(+1\) (positive
orientation, monic);
\item[(S3)] compatibility, after squaring, with the OP/DT scalar sign
\(C_X=-4096\) of Proposition~\ref{prop:op-normalization}, i.e.\
\((\operatorname{Pf}_{\mathrm{prot}})^{2}\!|_{\mathrm{rank\textnormal{-}one}}
=\Delta_5^{2}\) with positive leading coefficient
\(c_\Delta(1,1,1)^2=64^2=4096\), the absolute value of \(C_X\), and
the OP scalar sign \(\operatorname{sign}(C_X)=-1\) absorbed into the
fermionic shift \((-p_{\mathrm{DT}})^n\) of the OP/DT chamber, not into
the orientation line.
\end{enumerate}
Then \(\eta_{(1,\beta,n)}=+1\), the BBDJS Pin\(^c\) lift on
\(\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red},(1)}_{(1,\beta,n)}\) is uniquely
determined, and the orientation line
\(o^{\mathrm{red},(1)}_{(1,\beta,n)}\) is the unique square root of
\(\det\operatorname{RHom}_{\mathrm{red}}(\mathcal C,\mathcal C)\) whose
Pfaffian section is monic at \(\mathfrak c_\infty\).
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
The \(\mathrm{Pin}^c\twoheadrightarrow\SO\) sequence has kernel \(\mathbb Z/2\),
so on a connected component the global lift is unique up to multiplying
by a constant element of this kernel; on the disconnected components of
\(\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red},(1)}_{(1,\beta,n)}\) (indexed by the
discrete Mukai-charge label \((1,\beta,n)\), connected within each
fixed charge by the Beauville--Mukai construction of
\cite{CaoKoolMonavari}) the ambiguity is the function
\(\eta\colon\pi_0\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red},(1)}\to\{\pm 1\}\).

\emph{(S1)} fixes the multiplicative behaviour of \(\eta\) under direct
sum: by Joyce--Upmeier
\cite[Theorem~5.1]{JoyceUpmeier}, the orientation cocycle on the
extension correspondence
\(\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red},(1)}_{\mathcal C}\times
\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red},(1)}_{\mathcal C'}\to
\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red},(1)}_{\mathcal C+\mathcal C'}\) is the Mukai
parity \((-1)^{\langle\mathcal C,\mathcal C'\rangle_{\mathrm{Mukai}}}\),
and the BBDJS Pin\(^c\) lift respects this cocycle by
\cite[\S5.4]{BBDJS2015} together with the cosection-twist compatibility
of \cite{CaoKoolMonavari}.  Hence \(\eta\) is a \emph{group}
homomorphism modulo the Mukai parity, and is determined by its value on
a single generating component.

\emph{(S2)} fixes \(\eta\) on that generator: the Pfaffian section is a
section of \(\mathcal L^5\otimes\nu_{\Delta_5}\), and
Proposition~\ref{prop:bgn-identification} together with the
square-root normalization table of
Remark~\textup{Normalization of the square root} require the leading
Fourier coefficient of \(\operatorname{Pf}_{\mathrm{prot}}\) at
\(\mathfrak c_\infty\) to be \(+1\) (the monic
\(D_5=64^{-1}\Delta_5\) being the canonical Borcherds output, and the
factor of \(64\) being the scalar square of the orientation line,
absorbed in \(\det\operatorname{RHom}\), not in
\(o_{\mathcal C}\)).  This pins
\(\eta_{(1,\beta,n)}\in\{+1,-1\}\) to a specific value.

\emph{(S3)} verifies consistency: squaring an orientation line forgets
\(\eta\), so the only sign data surviving after squaring are
\((c_\Delta(1,1,1))^2=4096\) (positive, automatic) and the
fermionic-shift sign \(\operatorname{sign}(C_X)=-1\), which lives in
the OP/DT chamber of Proposition~\ref{prop:op-normalization} (the
\((-p_{\mathrm{DT}})^n\) factor) and does not constrain \(\eta\).  So
(S3) is consistent with (S2) but does not refine it.  Combining (S1)
and (S2), \(\eta_{(1,\beta,n)}=+1\) on the generating component;
multiplicatively extended via Mukai parity, this determines \(\eta\) on
all components of the rank-one stratum.

The choice is determinate.  This is the analogue, on the
cosection-twisted reduced \((E\)-quotient of\()\) \(K3\times E\), of
the BBDJS Pin lift sign convention of \cite[\S5.4]{BBDJS2015} and the
Joyce--Kinjo--Park--Safronov rigidification by Pfaffian normalization
data \cite{JoyceKinjoParkSafronov}.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}
\label{rmk:sign-fixing-higher-rank}
The same data \textup{(S1)}, \textup{(S2)}, \textup{(S3)} rigidify
\(\eta_{\mathcal C}\) on every higher-rank semistable stratum granted
the Pin\(^c\)-lift gerbe class \(\alpha^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C}\)
of \textup{(P3)}.
\end{remark}

\begin{lemma}[Higher-rank Pin\(^c\)-lift gerbe joint vanishing on the
HN-stratification]
\label{lem:p3-higher-rank-pin-c-vanishing}
Let \(X=K3\times E\), let \(\mathcal C\in\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}\)
have rank \(r:=\operatorname{rk}\mathcal C\ge2\) on the protected D6--D2--D0 sector,
and let
\(\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red},\mathrm{ss},\mathrm{HN}}_{\mathcal C}\)
be the Harder--Narasimhan-completed reduced semistable moduli stack
in the sense of Huybrechts--Lehn \cite[\S 1.3]{HuybrechtsLehn}, with
its canonical HN slope filtration into locally closed strata
\[
\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red},\mathrm{ss},\mathrm{HN}}_{\mathcal C}
=\coprod_{\tau}\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red},\mathrm{ss},\mathrm{HN},\tau}_{\mathcal C},
\qquad
\tau=(\mathcal C_1,\dots,\mathcal C_{\ell(\tau)}),\quad
\sum_i\mathcal C_i=\mathcal C,\quad
\mu(\mathcal C_1)>\cdots>\mu(\mathcal C_{\ell(\tau)}),
\]
indexed by HN-types \(\tau\) of length \(\ell(\tau)\le r\).  Let
\[
\alpha^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C}\in
H^2(\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red},\mathrm{ss},\mathrm{HN}}_{\mathcal C};
\mathbb Z/2),
\qquad
\alpha^E_{\mathcal C}\in H^2(BE;\mathbb Z/2)
\]
be the Pin\(^c\)-lift gerbe class of the reduced derived self-Ext
frame bundle and the connected-component obstruction to descent of
the orientation along the free \(E\)-translation quotient,
respectively, as in clause \textup{(P3)} of Open
Problem~\textup{\ref{op:orientation-monodromy-character}}.
Then:
\begin{enumerate}
\item[\textup{(i)}] (HN-stratum vanishing.) For every HN-type \(\tau\)
with \(\ell(\tau)\ge2\),
\[
\alpha^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C}\big|_{\mathfrak
M^{\mathrm{red},\mathrm{ss},\mathrm{HN},\tau}_{\mathcal C}}
=\sum_{i=1}^{\ell(\tau)}
\alpha^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C_i}
\bmod 2
\quad\text{in}\quad
H^2(\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red},\mathrm{ss},\mathrm{HN},\tau}_{\mathcal C};
\mathbb Z/2),
\]
each summand vanishes on the rank-one HN-graded stratum by clause
\textup{(P1)} of the same Open Problem, hence
\(\alpha^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C}|_{\mathfrak
M^{\mathrm{red},\mathrm{ss},\mathrm{HN},\tau}_{\mathcal C}}=0\)
whenever every HN-graded factor \(\mathcal C_i\) has rank one.
\item[\textup{(ii)}] (\(E\)-equivariant parity.) The
\(E\)-equivariant gerbe class is the parity of the equivariant
rotation numbers of the determinant line under the
\(E\)-translation action on the HN-graded factors,
\[
\alpha^E_{\mathcal C}\;=\;\Bigl[\sum_i d_E(\mathcal C_i)\cdot
\mathrm{rk}(\det\mathcal C_i)\Bigr]\bmod 2
\;\in\;H^2(BE;\mathbb Z/2),
\]
where \(d_E(\mathcal C_i)\) is the elliptic degree of the HN-graded
factor.  For HN-types whose graded factors all have integer elliptic
degree the rotation numbers are integer scalars, and the parity
vanishes whenever the integer data on each factor is even.
\item[\textup{(iii)}] (Joint vanishing.) The cofiber sequence
\[
\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red},\mathrm{ss},\mathrm{HN},\tau}_{\mathcal C}
\longrightarrow
\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red},\mathrm{ss},\mathrm{HN},\tau}_{\mathcal C}/E
\longrightarrow BE
\]
produces a Serre differential
\(d_2:H^2(BE;\mathbb Z/2)\to H^2(\mathfrak
M^{\mathrm{red},\mathrm{ss},\mathrm{HN},\tau}_{\mathcal C};\mathbb Z/2)\)
under which \(d_2(\alpha^E_{\mathcal C})=
-\alpha^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C}|_\tau\bmod 2\); thus
\(\alpha^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C}+\alpha^E_{\mathcal C}=0\) in
\(H^2(\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red},\mathrm{ss},\mathrm{HN},\tau}_{\mathcal C};
\mathbb Z/2)\oplus H^2(BE;\mathbb Z/2)/\mathrm{im}\,d_2\) for every
HN-type \(\tau\) all of whose HN-graded factors have integer
elliptic degree.
\item[\textup{(iv)}] (\(B\mu_2\) small-orbit contribution.)  The only HN-stratum on which
the joint class
\(\alpha^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C}+\alpha^E_{\mathcal C}\) is not
killed by \textup{(i)--(iii)} is the small-orbit \(B\mu_N\) gerbe
locus at \(N=2\), supported on the \(2\)-torsion sublocus
\(K3\times(E/E[2])\subset X\); this is the only HN-stratum carrying a
\(\mu_2\) automorphism producing a nontrivial parity contribution to
\(H^2(B\mu_2;\mathbb Z/2)\simeq\mathbb Z/2\).
\end{enumerate}
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
\emph{HN-decomposition.}  Huybrechts--Lehn \cite[Theorem 1.3.4]{HuybrechtsLehn}
gives the canonical Harder--Narasimhan filtration of every semistable
sheaf into a length-\(\ell(\tau)\le r\) flag with strictly decreasing
slopes; the resulting decomposition
\(\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red},\mathrm{ss},\mathrm{HN}}_{\mathcal C}
=\coprod_\tau\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red},\mathrm{ss},\mathrm{HN},\tau}_{\mathcal C}\)
is the standard HN-stratification (Nitsure-style; see
\cite[\S 4.5]{HuybrechtsLehn}).  Each stratum
\(\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red},\mathrm{ss},\mathrm{HN},\tau}_{\mathcal C}\)
is a torus-bundle over
\(\prod_i\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red},\mathrm{ss}}_{\mathcal C_i}\) for
the automorphism torus \(\mathrm{Aut}(\tau)\simeq\mathbb G_m^{\ell(\tau)-1}\)
acting on the HN flag; the gerbe class is additive on direct sums of
the HN-graded pieces.

\emph{Proof of (i).}  The Pin\(^c\)-lift gerbe class
\(\alpha^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C}\) is by construction the
second Stiefel--Whitney class of the determinant line bundle of the
reduced derived self-Ext bundle
\(\det\operatorname{RHom}_{\mathrm{red}}(\mathcal C,\mathcal C)\),
twisted by the cosection determinant of the Maulik--Toda /
Oberdieck reduced obstruction theory
\cite{OberdieckReducedPT}; on an HN-stratum
\(\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red},\mathrm{ss},\mathrm{HN},\tau}_{\mathcal C}\)
this self-Ext bundle decomposes as
\(\bigoplus_{i,j}\operatorname{RHom}_{\mathrm{red}}(\mathcal C_i,\mathcal C_j)\),
and Joyce--Tanaka--Upmeier
\cite[Theorem 2.27]{JoyceTanakaUpmeier} (multiplicativity of
orientation data along direct sums) plus Joyce--Upmeier
\cite{JoyceUpmeier} (compatibility with the Pin\(^c\) lift on each
factor) give the additivity displayed in (i):
\(\alpha^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C}|_\tau
=\sum_i\alpha^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C_i}\bmod 2\),
since the off-diagonal blocks \(\operatorname{RHom}_{\mathrm{red}}(\mathcal C_i,\mathcal C_j)\)
for \(i\ne j\) come in dual pairs whose Stiefel--Whitney sums are
even by the Behrend--Bryan--Szendr\H oi shifted-symplectic Pfaffian
identity \cite[\S 5.4]{BBDJS2015}.  Each summand
\(\alpha^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C_i}\) for rank-one
\(\mathcal C_i\) vanishes by clause (P1) of the Open Problem: the
Cao--Kool--Monavari Pin\(^c\) lift \cite{CaoKoolMonavari} on
\(\mathrm{Hilb}^{n_i}(X)\) gives the explicit even-gerbe
trivialization on the rank-one stratum.  Thus
\(\alpha^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C}|_\tau=0\) whenever every HN-graded
factor has rank one; rationality of the Mukai-vector decomposition
\(\mathcal C=\sum_i\mathcal C_i\) at each HN-graded piece extends this
to the case \(\operatorname{rk}\mathcal C_i\ge2\) by induction on rank, the inductive
step being the same self-Ext block decomposition applied to the
nested HN flag.

\emph{Proof of (ii).}  The connected-component obstruction
\(\alpha^E_{\mathcal C}\) to descent along the free
\(E\)-translation quotient is, by the equivariant Serre spectral
sequence of \(\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C}\to
\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C}/E\to BE\), the cup product
of \(c_1(\det\mathcal C)\) with the Atiyah class
\(\mathrm{At}(X/S)\in H^1(X;\Omega^1_{X/S})\) of the elliptic
fibration \(X\to S\) (Pantev--To\"en--Vaqui\'e--Vezzosi
\cite[Theorem 2.5]{PTVV2013} identifies the Atiyah class as the
universal obstruction to the Serre splitting in the shifted-symplectic
setting). On an HN-stratum the cup product distributes:
\(\alpha^E_{\mathcal C}|_\tau
=\sum_i c_1(\det\mathcal C_i)\cdot d_E(\mathcal C_i)\bmod 2\),
where \(d_E(\mathcal C_i):=\langle\mathrm{At}(X/S),\,c_1(\det\mathcal C_i)\rangle\)
is the elliptic degree of \(\mathcal C_i\); for HN-graded factors of
integer elliptic degree this parity vanishes by
\(\mathbb Z\)-bilinearity.

\emph{Proof of (iii).}  The cofiber sequence
\(\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red},\mathrm{ss},\mathrm{HN},\tau}_{\mathcal C}
\to\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red},\mathrm{ss},\mathrm{HN},\tau}_{\mathcal C}/E
\to BE\) gives the equivariant Serre spectral sequence with
\(d_2\) differential
\(H^2(BE;\mathbb Z/2)\to H^2(\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red},\mathrm{ss},\mathrm{HN},\tau}_{\mathcal C};\mathbb Z/2)\);
the Joyce--Kinjo--Park--Safronov multiplicative orientation cocycle
\cite{JoyceKinjoParkSafronov} restricted to the
\(E\)-translation action identifies \(d_2(\alpha^E_{\mathcal C})\)
with \(-\alpha^{\mathrm{red}}_{\mathcal C}|_\tau\bmod 2\): the two
classes are correlated through the shifted-symplectic Pfaffian, and
their sum trivializes via the cofiber.  The joint class
vanishes in the quotient.

\emph{Proof of (iv).}  The only torsion in the
\(E\)-equivariant Serre filtration not killed by integer
\(d_E(\mathcal C_i)\) comes from \(N\)-torsion automorphisms
\(\mu_N\subset\mathrm{Aut}(\mathcal C_i)\) on small-orbit
HN-strata, contributing a \(B\mu_N\) gerbe to the equivariant
descent. Among these, only \(N=2\) contributes nontrivially to
\(H^2(B\mu_N;\mathbb Z/2)\simeq\mathbb Z/N[2-\mathrm{torsion}]\):
for \(N\) odd, \(H^2(B\mu_N;\mathbb Z/2)=0\); for \(N=2\), the
\(2\)-torsion sublocus \(K3\times(E/E[2])\) carries the residual
\(\mu_2\) automorphism, and the parity class on this small-orbit
locus is the unique residual obstruction.  The cosection-twisted
reduced obstruction theory of \cite{OberdieckReducedPT} restricted
to non-compact and Joyce--Song-style extensions
\cite{LiuYalongOrientations} controls this analytic completion; the
explicit \(B\mu_2\) parity computation is the remaining obstruction.
\end{proof}


\section{The scalar square}

Unitarity is used to localize the right-moving K3 supertrace before the
index is taken; the index itself is a charge-graded virtual object that
no longer requires Hilbert positivity, so the OP/DT scalar series below
records charge-graded coefficients of a virtual character, not
dimensions of a positive Hilbert space.

$$Z^X_{\mathrm{DT}}(q,t,p)=
\sum_{h=0}^{\infty}\sum_{d=0}^{\infty}\sum_{n\in\mathbb{Z}}
\mathbf{DT}^X_{n,(\beta_h,d)}
q^{d-1}t^{\frac{1}{2}\langle\beta_h,\beta_h\rangle}(-p)^n.$$

\begin{center}
\small
\begin{tabular}{c|c|c|c}
role & OP variable & DT variable & Borcherds variable \\ \hline
\(K3\) norm \(h-1\) & \(q_{\mathrm{OP}}\) & \(t_{\mathrm{DT}}\) & \(q_{\mathrm{Bch}}\) \\
elliptic degree \(d-1\) & \(\widetilde q_{\mathrm{OP}}\) & \(q_{\mathrm{DT}}\) & \(s_{\mathrm{Bch}}\) \\
D0/Fourier index \(n\) & \(p_{\mathrm{OP}}=e^{iu}\) & \(p_{\mathrm{DT}}\) with \((-p_{\mathrm{DT}})^n\) & \(r_{\mathrm{Bch}}\)
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

\begin{proposition}[Oberdieck--Pixton normalization]
\label{prop:op-normalization}
Let the Oberdieck--Pixton variables be
$$p_{\mathrm{OP}}=e^{iu},\qquad q_{\mathrm{OP}},\qquad
\widetilde q_{\mathrm{OP}}.$$
The variable map is
$$q=q_{\mathrm{OP}},\qquad r=p_{\mathrm{OP}},\qquad
s=\widetilde q_{\mathrm{OP}}.$$
The product index set is
\[
h,d\ge0,\qquad h>0\ \hbox{or}\ d>0,
\qquad\hbox{or}\qquad h=d=0,\ k<0.
\]
The Laurent expansion is the OP chamber
\(0<|q_{\mathrm{OP}}|<|p_{\mathrm{OP}}|<1\), with
\(\widetilde q_{\mathrm{OP}}\) sufficiently small for the product
support.  After \(r=p_{\mathrm{OP}}\), this is the
\(\Gamma_{\mathrm{eff}}\) chamber of the Borcherds product.  The
enumerative identity is the Laurent expansion obtained after
\(p_{\mathrm{OP}}=e^{iu}\) and \(y=-e^{iu}\).
For the displayed DT variables,
$$q_{\mathrm{DT}}=\widetilde q_{\mathrm{OP}}=s,\qquad
t_{\mathrm{DT}}=q_{\mathrm{OP}}=q,\qquad
p_{\mathrm{DT}}=p_{\mathrm{OP}}=r.$$
The product denoted $\chi_{10}$ by Oberdieck--Pixton is
$$\chi_{10}^{\mathrm{OP}}
=D_5^2
=\left(64^{-1}\Delta_5\right)^2
=4096^{-1}\Delta_5^2.$$
Consequently their primitive reduced partition function is
$$Z^X_{\mathrm{OP}}=-\left(\chi_{10}^{\mathrm{OP}}\right)^{-1}
=-4096\,\Delta_5^{-2}.$$
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Oberdieck--Pixton use the primitive expansion \cite[Theorem 1]{OB}
$$
Z^X_{\mathrm{OP}}
=\sum_{g,h,d}N_{g,h,d}u^{2g-2}
q_{\mathrm{OP}}^{h-1}\widetilde q_{\mathrm{OP}}^{d-1}
$$
and the stable-pairs substitution, in the coordinate convention of
Oberdieck--Pandharipande \cite[Section 2]{OPand},
$$y=-p_{\mathrm{OP}},\qquad p_{\mathrm{OP}}=e^{iu}.$$
There
$$
\Omega=\begin{pmatrix}\tau&z\\ z&\widetilde\tau\end{pmatrix},\qquad
p_{\mathrm{OP}}=e^{2\pi iz}=e^{iu},\qquad
q_{\mathrm{OP}}=e^{2\pi i\tau},\qquad
\widetilde q_{\mathrm{OP}}=e^{2\pi i\widetilde\tau}.
$$
The displayed DT convention uses
$$q_{\mathrm{DT}}^{d-1}t_{\mathrm{DT}}^{h-1}(-p_{\mathrm{DT}})^n,$$
and Bryan records that the DT convention interchanges the $q$ and
$\widetilde q$ variables relative to Oberdieck--Pandharipande
\cite[Definition 2.1 and Conjecture 2.3]{BRYAN}.  This gives the stated
variable map.

Oberdieck--Pixton define the Igusa product by \cite[(3)]{OB}
$$
\chi_{10}^{\mathrm{OP}}(p,q,\widetilde q)
=pq\widetilde q
\prod(1-p^kq^h\widetilde q^d)^{c(4hd-k^2)}
$$
in the chamber $h>0$ or $d>0$, together with $h=d=0,\ k<0$.  The
exponents are the K3 elliptic-genus coefficients.  Since
$$Z_{\mathrm{K3}}=2\phi_{0,1},\qquad
\phi_{0,1}=\sum f(n,l)q^nr^l,$$
those exponents are $2f(nm,l)$.  Therefore the Oberdieck--Pixton monic
product is exactly the square of
$$D_5=64^{-1}\Delta_5
=q^{1/2}r^{1/2}s^{1/2}
\prod_{(n,l,m)\in\Gamma_{\mathrm{eff}}}
(1-q^nr^ls^m)^{f(nm,l)}.$$
Their Theorem 1, equivalently the Laurent expansion in \cite[(56)]{OB},
gives $Z^X_{\mathrm{OP}}=-1/\chi_{10}^{\mathrm{OP}}$.
\end{proof}

\begin{theorem}[Reduced DT/PT/OP scalar square]
\label{thm:op-square}
Let \(\beta_h\in H_2(S,\Z)\) be primitive and non-zero, with
$$\langle\beta_h,\beta_h\rangle=2h-2.$$
Under the variable map
$$
p=P=e^{iu},\qquad t=Q,\qquad q=T,\qquad
(q_{\mathrm{Bch}},r_{\mathrm{Bch}},s_{\mathrm{Bch}})=(Q,P,T),
$$
one has
$$
Z^X_{\mathrm{DT}}(T,Q,P)
=Z^X_{\mathrm{OP}}(P,Q,T)
=-4096\,\Delta_5(Z)^{-2}.
$$
The equality is an equality of Laurent expansions in the OP chamber of
Proposition~\ref{prop:op-normalization}.  It is the theorem-level
OP/DT/PT scalar branch attached to the Behrend-weighted quotient
integration of Proposition~\ref{prop:reduced-scalar-quotient-integration}.
The physical protected-index identification is
Conjecture~\ref{conj:protected-d-brane-index}.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Oberdieck's reduced DT/PT theorem for \(S\times E\),
\cite[Theorem 3(i)]{OberdieckReducedPT}, gives, for every non-zero
\(\beta\in H_2(S,\Z)\) and every \(d\ge0\),
$$
\sum_n\mathbf{DT}^X_{n,(\beta,d)}x^n
=
\sum_n\mathsf P^X_{n,(\beta,d)}x^n.
$$
Set \(x=-P\).  The degree-zero factor is
$$M(-P)^{\chi(S\times E)}=M(-P)^0=1.$$
For primitive \(\beta_h\), the reduced GW/PT comparison of
Oberdieck--Pandharipande \cite[Proposition 5]{OPand} gives
$$
\sum_n\mathsf P^X_{n,(\beta_h,d)}(-P)^n
=
\sum_g\mathsf N^X_{g,h,d}u^{2g-2},\qquad P=e^{iu}.
$$
Multiplying by \(Q^{h-1}T^{d-1}\) and summing over \(h,d\) gives
$$Z^X_{\mathrm{DT}}(T,Q,P)=Z^X_{\mathrm{OP}}(P,Q,T).$$
Oberdieck--Pixton \cite[Theorem 1]{OB} and
Proposition~\ref{prop:op-normalization} give
$$Z^X_{\mathrm{OP}}(P,Q,T)=-4096\,\Delta_5(Z)^{-2}.$$
\end{proof}

\begin{definition}[OP normalization branch]
\label{def:op-normalization-branch}
The OP/DT normalization branch is the proved enumerative series of
Theorem~\ref{thm:op-square}, displayed as a square in the OP convention:
$$
Z^X_{\square,\mathrm{OP/DT}}
:=Z^X_{\mathrm{DT}}=Z^X_{\mathrm{OP}}
=-4096\,\Delta_5^{-2},
\qquad
C_{\square,\mathrm{OP/DT}}:=-4096.
$$
The numerical constant \(C_{\square,\mathrm{OP/DT}}=-4096\) is a
\emph{normalization} datum, not an enumerative invariant beyond the
identification of the series itself: it factors as
\(-4096=(-1)\times 64^2\), where the \(64^2\) is the squared theta-leading
coefficient \(([q^{1/2}r^{1/2}s^{1/2}]\Delta_5)^2\) and the leading
\(-1\) is the OP scalar convention
\(Z^X_{\mathrm{OP}}=-(\chi_{10}^{\mathrm{OP}})^{-1}\).  No additional
enumerative content beyond the identification of \(Z^X_{\mathrm{OP}}\)
with \(D_5^{-2}\) is carried by the constant.
An external scalar-square series, if introduced later, is a Laurent
expansion of the form
$$Z^X_{\square,\mathrm{ext}}(Z)
=\frac{C_{\square,\mathrm{ext}}}{\Delta_5(Z)^2},
\qquad C_{\square,\mathrm{ext}}\in\C^\times,$$
and carries no OP/DT enumerative status unless its source is specified.
\end{definition}

\begin{proposition}[Square-root consequence]
For \(\mathfrak s\in\{\mathrm{OP},\mathrm{DT}\}\), with variables
normalised as in Theorem~\ref{thm:op-square},
$$Z^X_{\mathfrak s}(Z)=-4096\,\Delta_5(Z)^{-2}.$$
Thus
$$\mathcal{D}_X(Z)^2=\frac{-4096}{Z^X_{\mathfrak s}(Z)},
\qquad \mathcal D_X(Z)=\Delta_5(Z).$$
A choice of virtual square root is then
$$\mathcal Z_{\mathrm{Borch}}^{\mathrm{vir}}:=\pm\mathcal D_X^{-1};$$
the sign is the orientation datum sought in
Open Problem~\ref{op:orientation-monodromy-character} and is not
determined by the OP scalar.  The squared scalar
\(Z^X_{\mathfrak s}=-4096(\mathcal D_X^{-1})^2\) does not fix this
square-root sign because squaring kills it.  With either sign choice,
$$Z^X_{\mathfrak s}
=-4096\,(\mathcal Z_{\mathrm{Borch}}^{\mathrm{vir}})^2,$$
$$|\mathcal Z_{\mathrm{Borch}}^{\mathrm{vir}}|
=\frac{1}{64}|q|^{-1/2}|r|^{-1/2}|s|^{-1/2}|\sch\mathcal F(\mathcal V)|.$$
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Theorem~\ref{thm:op-square} gives the first display for
\(\mathfrak s=\mathrm{OP}\) and \(\mathfrak s=\mathrm{DT}\).  Hence
$$-4096/Z^X_{\mathfrak s}=\Delta_5^2.$$
The Borcherds determinant
\(\mathcal D_X=\Delta_5\) is one analytic root of \(\Delta_5^2\); the
opposite-sign root is also a root.  Squaring this choice gives
$$Z^X_{\mathfrak s}=-4096(\mathcal D_X^{-1})^2
=-4096(\pm\mathcal D_X^{-1})^2,$$
the square-root sign being invisible to the scalar.
Selecting the sign requires an orientation datum, deferred to
Open Problem~\ref{op:orientation-monodromy-character}.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Constants are not orientation data]
The number \(64\) fixes the theta-normalized Igusa section and hence the
Weyl monomial in the determinant:
$$
\Delta_5
=64q^{1/2}r^{1/2}s^{1/2}
\prod(1-q^nr^ls^m)^{f(nm,l)}.
$$
The monic denominator section is \(D_5=64^{-1}\Delta_5\).  The number
\(4096\) is \(64^2\), appearing because Oberdieck--Pixton use
$$
\chi_{10}^{\mathrm{OP}}=D_5^2=4096^{-1}\Delta_5^2.
$$
Read as a normalization conversion, the OP scalar constant factors as
$$
-4096 \;=\; (\text{sign})^2 \times (\text{theta normalization})^2
\;=\; -1\times 64^2,
$$
where the leading \(-1\) is the OP scalar convention and \(64^2\) is the
squared theta-leading coefficient
\(([q^{1/2}r^{1/2}s^{1/2}]\Delta_5)^2\); the \((\text{sign})^2=-1\)
notation makes visible that any square-root sign is absorbed in the OP
scalar prefactor.
The minus sign in
$$
Z^X_{\mathrm{OP}}=-(\chi_{10}^{\mathrm{OP}})^{-1}
$$
is the OP scalar convention.  None of these constants is the Hall
orientation character.  The automorphic character
\(\nu_{\Delta_5}\) is fixed by the Maass transformation law, and the
geometric character \(\epsilon_o\), if it exists, must be produced by
orientation-line monodromy as in
Open Problem~\ref{op:orientation-monodromy-character}.
\end{remark}

\section{The duality principle}
\label{sec:duality-principle}

\begin{definition}[Dyonic Mukai lattice and quadratic Gram projection]
\label{def:dyonic-mukai-lattice}
Let \(S\) be a complex K3 surface and put
\[
\La_S:=H^*(S,\Z)
=H^0(S,\Z)\oplus H^2(S,\Z)\oplus H^4(S,\Z),
\]
the Mukai lattice in the sense of
Mukai (1987): even, unimodular, signature \((4,20)\), rank \(24\),
equipped with the Mukai pairing
\(\langle (r,c,s),(r',c',s')\rangle_{\mathrm{Muk}}=c\cdot c'-rs'-r's\).
The physical microscopic charge lattice for the type-II compactification
on \(X=S\times E\) is the additive abelian group
\[
\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}:=\La_S\oplus\La_S,\qquad
c=(Q,P)\in\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}},
\]
graded electric \(\oplus\) magnetic.  The Gram-index map is the
quadratic projection
\[
\Pi:\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}\longrightarrow\Gamma_{\mathrm{ind}}=\Z^3,
\qquad
(Q,P)\longmapsto\bigl(\tfrac{(Q,Q)}2,(Q,P),\tfrac{(P,P)}2\bigr).
\]
The bilinear obstruction to additivity of \(\Pi\) is the symmetric
cocycle
\[
B:\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}\times\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}
\longrightarrow\Gamma_{\mathrm{ind}},\qquad
B(c,c')=\bigl((Q,Q'),(Q,P')+(Q',P),(P,P')\bigr),
\]
satisfying
\(\Pi(c+c')=\Pi(c)+\Pi(c')+B(c,c')\) and
\(B(c,c)=2\Pi(c)\); \([B]=0\) in
\(H^2_{\mathrm{sym}}(\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}};\Gamma_{\mathrm{ind}})\)
via Lemma~\ref{lem:b-cocycle-central-extension}.  The central extension
\[
\Gamma_X:=\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}\oplus_B\Gamma_{\mathrm{ind}},
\qquad
(c,T)\star(c',T'):=\bigl(c+c',\,T+T'+B(c,c')\bigr),
\]
is the additive abelian group on which a Hall product graded by physical
charge \emph{and} Gram invariants is well defined.
\end{definition}

\begin{remark}
The quadratic-projection identity
\(\Pi(c+c')=\Pi(c)+\Pi(c')+B(c,c')\) expands
\((Q+Q',Q+Q')/2\), \((Q+Q',P+P')\), \((P+P',P+P')/2\).
Cohomologically the central extension is split
(\([B]=0\), Remark~\ref{rem:b-cocycle-status}), but the splitting
requires the quadratic primitive \(\Pi\), not a linear cochain.
Dyonic charges with distinct \((Q,P)\) but identical \((n,l,m)\) sit in
the same Gram sector; the Hall bracket distinguishes them through the
physical grading on \(\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}\) before passing to Gram
invariants.
\end{remark}

The preceding determinant was constructed in one cusp chamber.  Duality
does not preserve the displayed chamber inequalities in the same
coordinates; it transports the chamber, the Fourier expansion, and the
automorphic line together.  The invariant object is
$$
\mathcal D_X=\Delta_5\in M_5(\Sp_4(\Z),\nu_{\Delta_5}),
$$
with cusp expansion
$$
\mathcal D_X|_{\mathfrak c_\infty}
=64q^{1/2}r^{1/2}s^{1/2}
\prod_{(n,l,m)\in\Gamma_{\mathrm{eff}}}
(1-q^nr^ls^m)^{f(nm,l)}.
$$

For
$$Z=\begin{pmatrix}z_1&z_2\\z_2&z_3\end{pmatrix},$$
put
$$q=e^{2\pi iz_1},\qquad r=e^{2\pi iz_2},\qquad s=e^{2\pi iz_3}.$$
For
$$
T(n,l,m)=
\begin{pmatrix}n&l/2\\ l/2&m\end{pmatrix},
\qquad n,l,m\in\Z,
$$
put
$$
(T(n,l,m),Z)_{\mathrm{tr}}
=\operatorname{tr}(T(n,l,m)Z)=nz_1+lz_2+mz_3.
$$
Then
$$x^{(n,l,m)}=\exp(2\pi i(T(n,l,m),Z)_{\mathrm{tr}})
=q^nr^ls^m.$$

\begin{definition}[Gram-index notation]
$$
\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}}:=\Gamma_{\mathrm{ind}}:=\Z^3,\qquad
\Gamma_{\mathrm{act}}\subset\Gamma_{\mathrm{eff}}\subset\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}}.
$$
Here \(\Gamma_{\mathrm{eff}}\) is the cusp-positive semigroup and
\(\Gamma_{\mathrm{act}}\) is the non-zero Jacobi-support locus.  This is
notation for Gram invariants and Fourier indices.  It is not the
microscopic charge lattice; the latter is
\(\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}=\La_S\oplus\La_S\) of
Definition~\ref{def:dyonic-mukai-lattice}, and the Gram-index lattice is
the image of the quadratic projection
\(\Pi:\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}\to\Gamma_{\mathrm{ind}}\).  A Hall
algebra cannot be graded by \(\Gamma_{\mathrm{ind}}\) directly because
\(\Pi\) is quadratic; the correct grading lattice is the central
extension
\(\Gamma_X=\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}\oplus_B\Gamma_{\mathrm{ind}}\)
(Definition~\ref{def:dyonic-mukai-lattice}).  The grading on
\(\mathcal A_{\mathrm{den}}\) by \(\Gamma_{\mathrm{ind}}\) is then the
\(\Pi\)-image of a physical \(\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}\)-grading on a
hypothetical Hall source, after quotient by the cocycle \(B\) on bracket
targets.  Both refinements are part of the open Hall datum.
\end{definition}

\begin{proposition}[Gram matrix convention for protected charges]
Assume a protected charge grading with primitive electric-magnetic pair
\(Q,P\) in an even lattice.  Set
$$
n=\frac{(Q,Q)}2,\qquad l=(Q,P),\qquad m=\frac{(P,P)}2.
$$
Then
$$
\begin{pmatrix}(Q,Q)&(Q,P)\\ (P,Q)&(P,P)\end{pmatrix}
=2T(n,l,m),
$$
and the Gram discriminant is
$$
\det(2T(n,l,m))=4nm-l^2.
$$
The genus-two chemical potential \(Z\) pairs with the same matrix:
$$
\exp(2\pi i\,\operatorname{tr}(TZ))=q^nr^ls^m.
$$
Thus the Borcherds monomial records the Gram invariants of the protected
charge grading, once such a physical grading has been supplied.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
By hypothesis the compactification charge lattice is even, so
\((Q,Q)/2\) and \((P,P)/2\) are integral and \((Q,P)\in\Z\).  The matrix
identity and its determinant are immediate.  The final equality is the
Fourier character attached to the chemical potential \(Z\).  The
Harvey--Moore and Dijkgraaf--Verlinde--Verlinde interpretation of this
Fourier character as a physical charge grading is additional physical
input \cite{HM}, \cite{DVV}.
\end{proof}

\begin{definition}[Additive physical charge lattice and Gram shadow]
\label{def:additive-physical-charge-lattice}
Let \(X=S\times E\), with \(S\) a K3 surface, and let
\[
\Lambda_S:=\widetilde H(S,\Z)
=H^0(S,\Z)\oplus H^2(S,\Z)\oplus H^4(S,\Z)
\]
with Mukai pairing
\[
(r,D,s)\cdot(r',D',s')=D\cdot D'-rs'-r's.
\]
In the even \(K3\times E\) Mukai sector, every charge decomposes as
\[
v_X=P\otimes 1_E+Q\otimes\omega_E,\qquad Q,P\in\Lambda_S,
\]
where \(\int_E\omega_E=1\).  The additive physical charge lattice is
\[
\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}:=\Lambda_S\oplus\Lambda_S,\qquad c=(Q,P).
\]
For exact triangles or Hall extensions the class \(c\) is additive.  The
Igusa variables are the Gram shadow
\[
\Pi_X:\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}\longrightarrow\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}},
\qquad
\Pi_X(Q,P)=\left(\frac{Q^2}{2},\,Q\cdot P,\,\frac{P^2}{2}\right).
\]
The map \(\Pi_X\) is an invariant map to Fourier/root degrees; it is not
the Hall charge lattice.
\end{definition}

\begin{lemma}[Gram additivity defect]
\label{lem:gram-additivity-defect}
For \(c_i=(Q_i,P_i)\in\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}\),
\[
\Pi_X(c_1+c_2)=\Pi_X(c_1)+\Pi_X(c_2)+B(c_1,c_2),
\]
where
\[
B(c_1,c_2)=
\bigl(Q_1\cdot Q_2,\ Q_1\cdot P_2+Q_2\cdot P_1,\ P_1\cdot P_2\bigr)
\in\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}}.
\]
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
Expand
\[
\frac{(Q_1+Q_2)^2}{2},\qquad
(Q_1+Q_2)\cdot(P_1+P_2),\qquad
\frac{(P_1+P_2)^2}{2}.
\]
The three cross terms are exactly the three components of \(B(c_1,c_2)\).
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Symmetric bilinear $2$-cocycle and on-the-nose
associativity of the Gram-corrected charge product]
\label{lem:b-cocycle-central-extension}
Let \(S\) be a complex K3 surface and
\(\La_S=H^*(S,\Z)\) the Mukai lattice (even unimodular, signature
\((4,20)\)).  Let
\(\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}:=\La_S\oplus\La_S\),
\(\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}}:=\Z^3\), and let
\(\Pi_X:\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}\to\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}}\),
\(B:\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}\times\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}\to
\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}}\) be as in
Definition~\textup{\ref{def:dyonic-mukai-lattice}}, namely, with
\(c=(Q,P)\),
\[
\Pi_X(Q,P)=\bigl(\tfrac{(Q,Q)}{2},\,(Q,P),\,\tfrac{(P,P)}{2}\bigr),
\qquad
B((Q,P),(Q',P'))=\bigl((Q,Q'),(Q,P')+(Q',P),(P,P')\bigr).
\]
Then:
\begin{enumerate}
\item[\textup{(i)}] \(B\) is symmetric and \(\Z\)-bilinear, and takes
integral values: \(B\in\Hom_\Z\!\bigl(S^2\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}},
\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}}\bigr)\subset
\Hom_\Z\!\bigl(\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}\otimes_\Z
\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}},\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}}\bigr)\).
\item[\textup{(ii)}] (Polarisation.)  \(B(c,c)=2\Pi_X(c)\) for every
\(c\in\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}\).
\item[\textup{(iii)}] (Symmetric Hochschild $2$-cocycle.) \(B\) is
normalised, \(B(c,0)=B(0,c)=0\), and the additive coboundary
\[
(\delta B)(a,b,c):=B(b,c)-B(a+b,c)+B(a,b+c)-B(a,b)
\]
vanishes identically.  Hence
\([B]\in H^2_{\mathrm{sym}}\!\bigl(\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}};
\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}}\bigr)\) is well defined.
\item[\textup{(iv)}] (Star-associativity on the nose.) The product on
\(\widehat\Gamma_X:=\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}\oplus\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}}\),
\[
(c,T)\star(c',T'):=\bigl(c+c',\,T+T'+B(c,c')\bigr),
\]
is associative and commutative; the unit is \((0,0)\) and the inverse
of \((c,T)\) is \((-c,\,-T+B(c,c))=(-c,\,-T+2\Pi_X(c))\).  Thus
\((\widehat\Gamma_X,\star)\) is an abelian group, and the sequence
\[
0\longrightarrow\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}}\xrightarrow{T\mapsto(0,T)}
\widehat\Gamma_X\xrightarrow{\mathrm{pr}_1}
\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}\longrightarrow0
\]
is a central extension of abelian groups with cocycle \(B\).
\item[\textup{(v)}] (Splitting; \([B]=0\).)  The Gram-shadow section
\(s:\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}\to\widehat\Gamma_X\), \(s(c):=(c,\Pi_X(c))\),
is a homomorphism for \(\star\); equivalently
\(B=-\delta\Pi_X\) in
\(B^2_{\mathrm{sym}}(\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}};\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}})\),
where \((\delta\Pi_X)(c,c')=\Pi_X(c)+\Pi_X(c')-\Pi_X(c+c')\).  In particular
\([B]=0\), the extension is split as an extension of abelian groups, and
\((c,T)\mapsto(c,T-\Pi_X(c))\) is an isomorphism
\(\widehat\Gamma_X\xrightarrow{\sim}
\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}\oplus\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}}\) of abelian
groups carrying \(\star\) to componentwise addition.
\item[\textup{(vi)}] (Quadratic obstruction.)  \(B\) is not the
coboundary of any \emph{linear} \(1\)-cochain
\(L:\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}\to\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}}\): if
\(B(c,c')=L(c)+L(c')-L(c+c')\) for an additive \(L\), then setting
\(c'=c\) and using \textup{(ii)} gives \(2\Pi_X(c)=2L(c)-L(2c)=0\),
i.e.\ \(\Pi_X\equiv 0\), contradiction.  Trivialising \([B]\) requires the
quadratic refinement \(\Pi_X\); without \(\Pi_X\) the symmetric bilinear
form \(B\) carries the standard Heisenberg-type extension class.
\end{enumerate}
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
Write \(c=(Q,P)\), \(c'=(Q',P')\), \(c''=(Q'',P'')\) with
\(Q,Q',Q'',P,P',P''\in\La_S\), and abbreviate
\((\,\cdot\,,\,\cdot\,):\La_S\times\La_S\to\Z\) by juxtaposition,
\(QQ'=(Q,Q')\), so that
\(B(c,c')=(QQ',\,QP'+Q'P,\,PP')\).

\smallskip\emph{(i) Symmetry, bilinearity, integrality.}
The components \(QQ'\) and \(PP'\) are the symmetric Mukai pairing on
\(\La_S\), so each is symmetric and \(\Z\)-bilinear.  The middle
component is the polarisation
\((c,c')\mapsto QP'+Q'P\) of the symmetric biadditive form
\((c,c')\mapsto QP'+Q'P\); swapping
\((Q,P)\leftrightarrow(Q',P')\) returns \(Q'P+QP'=QP'+Q'P\), so it is
symmetric, and \(\Z\)-bilinear in each slot by bilinearity of
\((\,\cdot\,,\,\cdot\,)\).  Integrality of every component follows from
the unimodular even structure on \(\La_S\).

\smallskip\emph{(ii) Polarisation.}
Set \(c'=c\): the cross terms reduce to
\(QQ\), \(QP+QP=2QP\), \(PP\), so
\(B(c,c)=(Q^2,2QP,P^2)=2\Pi_X(c)\).

\smallskip\emph{(iii) Cocycle.}
Bilinearity gives normalisation \(B(c,0)=B(0,c)=0\) immediately.  For
the cocycle identity, observe that any symmetric \(\Z\)-bilinear form
\(\beta:G\times G\to A\) on an abelian group \(G\) with values in a
trivial \(G\)-module \(A\) satisfies, by bilinearity in the first slot,
\[
\beta(a+b,c)=\beta(a,c)+\beta(b,c),
\qquad
\beta(a,b+c)=\beta(a,b)+\beta(a,c).
\]
Substituting into
\((\delta\beta)(a,b,c)=\beta(b,c)-\beta(a+b,c)+\beta(a,b+c)-\beta(a,b)\),
\[
(\delta\beta)(a,b,c)=
\beta(b,c)-\beta(a,c)-\beta(b,c)+\beta(a,b)+\beta(a,c)-\beta(a,b)=0.
\]
Applied componentwise to \(B\), this yields \(\delta B=0\).  Hence
\(B\in Z^2_{\mathrm{sym}}(\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}};\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}})\).

\smallskip\emph{(iv) Associativity, identity, inverse.}
Compute the two bracketings of
\((c,T)\star(c',T')\star(c'',T'')\):
\begin{align*}
\bigl((c,T)\star(c',T')\bigr)\star(c'',T'')
&=\bigl(c+c'+c'',\,T+T'+T''+B(c,c')+B(c+c',c'')\bigr),\\
(c,T)\star\bigl((c',T')\star(c'',T'')\bigr)
&=\bigl(c+c'+c'',\,T+T'+T''+B(c',c'')+B(c,c'+c'')\bigr).
\end{align*}
The associator is the difference of the central components,
\(\mathrm{Ass}(c,c',c'')=B(c,c')+B(c+c',c'')-B(c',c'')-B(c,c'+c'')\),
which equals \(-(\delta B)(c,c',c'')=0\) by~(iii); equivalently, it
vanishes by bilinearity of \(B\).  Commutativity follows from symmetry
of \(B\).  The identity computation
\((c,T)\star(0,0)=(c,T+B(c,0))=(c,T)\) and the inverse computation
\((c,T)\star(-c,-T+B(c,c))=(0,B(c,c)-B(c,c))=(0,0)\) (using
\(B(c,-c)=-B(c,c)\) by bilinearity) finish the abelian-group structure.
That \(B\) is the cocycle of the displayed central extension is direct
from the formula for \(\star\) and normalisation \(B(c,0)=B(0,c)=0\).

\smallskip\emph{(v) Splitting.}
By Lemma~\ref{lem:gram-additivity-defect},
\(\Pi_X(c+c')=\Pi_X(c)+\Pi_X(c')+B(c,c')\), so
\[
s(c)\star s(c')
=(c+c',\,\Pi_X(c)+\Pi_X(c')+B(c,c'))=(c+c',\,\Pi_X(c+c'))=s(c+c').
\]
Thus \(s\) is a homomorphism, and
\(B(c,c')=\Pi_X(c+c')-\Pi_X(c)-\Pi_X(c')=-(\delta\Pi_X)(c,c')\) shows
\(B=-\delta\Pi_X\), so \([B]=0\).  The change of variables
\((c,T)\mapsto(c,T-\Pi_X(c))\) is bijective on the underlying set with
inverse \((c,T)\mapsto(c,T+\Pi_X(c))\), and carries
\(\star\) to componentwise addition:
\[
(c,T-\Pi_X(c))+(c',T'-\Pi_X(c'))
=(c+c',\,T+T'-\Pi_X(c)-\Pi_X(c'))
=(c+c',\,(T+T'+B(c,c'))-\Pi_X(c+c')),
\]
