matching the change of variables applied to
\((c+c',T+T'+B(c,c'))=(c,T)\star(c',T')\).

\smallskip\emph{(vi) Quadratic obstruction.}
Suppose \(B=\delta L\) for some additive
\(L:\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}\to\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}}\), i.e.\
\(B(c,c')=L(c)+L(c')-L(c+c')\).  Setting \(c'=c\),
\(B(c,c)=2L(c)-L(2c)\); but \(L\) additive gives \(L(2c)=2L(c)\), so
\(B(c,c)=0\), contradicting \(B(c,c)=2\Pi_X(c)\) for any
\(c=(Q,P)\) with \((Q,Q),(Q,P),(P,P)\) not all zero.  Hence no linear
trivialisation exists; the quadratic primitive \(\Pi_X\) is necessary.

\smallskip\emph{(vii) Chain-level lift; strict associativity in the
PTVV/Joyce host.}
Clauses (i)--(iv) place \((\widehat\Gamma_X,\star)\) inside the abelian
category of discrete abelian groups.  The construction of the central
extension is used downstream as a strict monoid in the chain-level host of
Definition~\ref{def:local-protected-observable-algebra}: the bracket on
\(\widetilde P_X\) and the bilinear cocycle \(B\) act on the
critical-Hall complex of compactly supported B-branes, which lives in
chain complexes of \(\Q\)-vector spaces (or, with orientation lines
included, in the dg-category of \((-1)\)-shifted symplectic perfect
modules of \cite{PTVV2013}).  It is therefore necessary to lift (iv)
from H\(^0\) to the chain level.

\smallskip\emph{Chain-level data.}  Let \(C_*:=C_*(-,\Z)\) denote the
normalised bar/Eilenberg--Mac Lane chain complex functor.  Apply
\(C_*\) to the discrete abelian groups \(\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}\),
\(\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}}\), \(\widehat\Gamma_X\), placing them in
homological degree zero.  The bilinear cocycle \(B\) of (i) is
already a discrete chain map
\[
\mathbf B:\;C_*(\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}})\otimes
C_*(\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}})\longrightarrow
C_*(\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}}),
\]
with no higher components, since \(B\) is \emph{strictly} bilinear in
each slot by (i) (no chain-level corrections survive because the
source and target are concentrated in degree zero).  The star product
extends to a degree-zero chain map
\[
\mu:\;C_*(\widehat\Gamma_X)\otimes C_*(\widehat\Gamma_X)
\longrightarrow C_*(\widehat\Gamma_X),
\qquad
\mu\bigl((c,T)\otimes(c',T')\bigr)
=\bigl(c+c',\,T+T'+\mathbf B(c,c')\bigr).
\]
Coupled with the orientation lines \(o_c\) of
Definition~\ref{def:orientation-line} and the multiplicative
isomorphisms \(\mu_{c,c'}:o_{c+c'}\xrightarrow\sim o_c\otimes o_{c'}\)
of Joyce--Upmeier \cite{JoyceUpmeier} and
Joyce--Kinjo--Park--Safronov \cite{JoyceKinjoParkSafronov}, the same
formula promotes to a degree-zero chain map of
\((-1)\)-shifted symplectic perfect complexes on the Cartesian
extension correspondence
\(\mathfrak M_{X,c}\times\mathfrak M_{X,c'}\to\mathfrak M_{X,c+c'}\)
of \cite{PTVV2013}, with \(\mathbf B\) acting on the
\(\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}}\)-grading factor and \(\mu_{c,c'}\) on the
orientation-line factor.

\smallskip\emph{The associator vanishes pointwise.}
By (iv) the associator of \(\mu\) at \(H^0\) is
\[
\alpha(c,c',c'')\;:=\;
\mathbf B(c,c')+\mathbf B(c+c',c'')
-\mathbf B(c',c'')-\mathbf B(c,c'+c'')
\;=\;-(\delta\mathbf B)(c,c',c'')\;=\;0,
\]
\emph{strictly} as an element of \(C_0(\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}})\), not
merely up to a boundary.  The bounding homotopy
\(h:\mu\circ(\mu\otimes\id)\Rightarrow\mu\circ(\id\otimes\mu)\)
required by step~(ii) of the proof skeleton is therefore the
\emph{canonical zero homotopy}: \(h\equiv 0\) bounds
\(\alpha\equiv 0\).  No nontrivial chain-level homotopy is needed
because the obstruction itself vanishes on the nose.  The PTVV
\((-1)\)-shifted symplectic Frobenius pairing on
\(\mathfrak M_{X,c}\times\mathfrak M_{X,c'}\) of \cite{PTVV2013}
contributes to \(\mu\) only through its integrated bilinear class
\(\mathbf B\) on \(\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}}\); the Joyce--Upmeier
orientation cocycle \cite{JoyceUpmeier} contributes only through the
discrete multiplicative isomorphism \(\mu_{c,c'}\); and (i) pins both
contributions to a strictly bilinear function of \((c,c')\).  In
particular the BBDJS vanishing-cycle Thom--Sebastiani isomorphism
\cite{BBDJS2015} on disjoint d-critical charts is monoidal at the
chain level, so it carries no associator correction beyond what
\(\mathbf B\) already records.

\smallskip\emph{Pentagon identity.}
The four-fold associator measures the discrepancy between two
bracketings of \((c_1,T_1)\star(c_2,T_2)\star(c_3,T_3)\star(c_4,T_4)\)
along the two pentagon paths.  In the centre component this is
\(\bigl(\delta\delta\mathbf B\bigr)(c_1,c_2,c_3,c_4)\), which vanishes
identically because \(\delta^2=0\) on the Hochschild complex.  Term by
term: each pentagon edge is a single application of the associator
\(\alpha\) of the previous paragraph; the associator vanishes
pointwise, hence its iterates do as well.  In the orientation
component the pentagon is the cocycle pentagon
\[
\mu_{c+c',c''}\circ\mu_{c,c'}=\mu_{c,c'+c''}\circ\mu_{c',c''}
\]
of Joyce--Upmeier \cite{JoyceUpmeier} and
Joyce--Kinjo--Park--Safronov \cite{JoyceKinjoParkSafronov}, recorded
in hypothesis (O) of
Theorem~\ref{thm:ptvv-joyce-pi-descent}.  Multiplicativity is precisely
the strict pentagon for \(\{\mu_{c,c'}\}\); under (O) the pentagon
holds on the nose, with no bounding 2-cell required.

\smallskip\emph{Higher Stasheff coherences collapse.}
Stasheff's associahedra organise the higher coherences of an
\(A_\infty\)-monoid as polytopes
\(K_n\) for \(n\ge 4\), with \((n-2)\)-cells parametrising
\(n\)-fold reassociations.  For \((\widehat\Gamma_X,\mu)\) every cell
of \(K_n\) is computed by an iterated comparison of bracketings of
\((c_1,T_1)\star\cdots\star(c_n,T_n)\); on the centre component each
such comparison is a sum of values of \(\mathbf B\) evaluated on
sums and differences of subsets of \(\{c_1,\ldots,c_n\}\), and by
strict bilinearity (i) every such sum collapses to a single multilinear
expression independent of the bracketing.  Equivalently, the bar
construction \(B_*(\widehat\Gamma_X)\) of the discrete monoid
\((\widehat\Gamma_X,\star)\) is acyclic in positive degrees because
\(\widehat\Gamma_X\) is a discrete abelian group (this is the standard
fact that the Eilenberg--Mac Lane bar complex of a discrete abelian
group has trivial higher homotopy groups), so every higher Stasheff
coherence \(h_n\) (\(n\ge 3\)) admits the canonical zero bounding
chain.  No additional choice is required.  On the orientation factor
the same conclusion holds: a multiplicative system
\(\{\mu_{c,c'}\}\) satisfying the strict pentagon is, by Mac Lane's
coherence theorem, a strict monoidal natural transformation; all
higher coherences are uniquely determined by the strict pentagon and
identity, and they all hold strictly.  Combining the two factors,
\((\widehat\Gamma_X,\mu)\), enriched in the chain category of the
PTVV/Joyce host, is a strictly associative monoid: an
\(A_\infty\)-monoid whose Stasheff coherences \(h_n\) are all
identically zero, not merely homotopic to zero.

\smallskip
The H\(^0\)-level associativity of (iv) lifts to strict associativity
at the chain level of the PTVV/Joyce host of
Definition~\ref{def:local-protected-observable-algebra}, conditional on
the strict-pentagon multiplicative orientation of (O) in
Theorem~\ref{thm:ptvv-joyce-pi-descent}: for the discrete monoid
\((\widehat\Gamma_X,\star)\) no homotopy-coherent correction is
required.  Absent (O) the chain-level lift is \(A_\infty\)-coherent,
controlled by a Hochschild \(2\)-cocycle representative of \([B]\)
trivial by (v).
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}
\label{rem:b-cocycle-status}
The chain-level lift of (iv) is strict, not merely
\(A_\infty\)-coherent, conditional on hypothesis (O) of
Theorem~\ref{thm:ptvv-joyce-pi-descent} (strict pentagon for the
multiplicative orientation cocycle \(\{\mu_{c,c'}\}\) of
\cite{JoyceUpmeier}, \cite{JoyceKinjoParkSafronov}):
\(\widehat\Gamma_X\) is a discrete abelian group, so its bar complex
is acyclic in positive degrees; higher Stasheff coherences are
iterated values of the bilinear cocycle \(B\) and vanish on the nose
by the cocycle identity of (iii); the orientation factor contributes
only the strict pentagon of (O).  Absent (O), the lift is
\(A_\infty\)-coherent, controlled by a Hochschild \(2\)-cocycle
representative of \([B]\) cohomologically trivial by (v), with all
coherences bounded by the determinant-line Hochschild
\(1\)-cochain \(\Theta\) of
Theorem~\ref{thm:ptvv-joyce-pi-descent}, Step~2.
\end{remark}

\begin{definition}[Gram-corrected charge extension]
\label{def:gram-corrected-charge-extension}
Set
\[
\widehat\Gamma_X:=\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}\oplus\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}}.
\]
For \(c,c'\in\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}\) and
\(T,T'\in\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}}\), define
\[
(c,T)\star(c',T')
:=(c+c',\,T+T'+B(c,c')).
\]
The section
\[
s:\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}\longrightarrow\widehat\Gamma_X,\qquad
s(c)=(c,\Pi_X(c))
\]
is additive for \(\star\).  Thus the compact Hall object, if constructed,
is graded upstairs by \(\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}\); the
\(\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}}\)-graded Igusa object is obtained only after
Gram pushforward or an equivalent cocycle-corrected descent.
\end{definition}

\begin{proof}
By Lemma~\ref{lem:b-cocycle-central-extension}(i),(iii),(iv), \(\star\) is
associative and commutative, the identity is \((0,0)\), and the inverse
of \((c,T)\) is \((-c,-T+B(c,c))\); the section \(s\) is the splitting
of clause~(v).
\end{proof}

\begin{definition}[Gram-index pairing]
For
$$\gamma=(n,l,m),\qquad \gamma'=(n',l',m'),$$
define
$$
\langle\gamma,\gamma'\rangle_{\mathrm{ind}}
=2(nm'+n'm)-ll'.
$$
The Gram discriminant is
$$
\Delta_{\mathrm{gram}}(\gamma)
=\langle\gamma,\gamma\rangle_{\mathrm{ind}}
=4nm-l^2.
$$
\end{definition}

\begin{remark}[Chamber transport]
The pairing \(\langle\ ,\ \rangle_{\mathrm{ind}}\) is the pairing on
Gram invariants.  The order on \(\Gamma_{\mathrm{eff}}\) is a Fock
polarization at one cusp.  A duality element transports this
polarization to the corresponding product chamber at the transported
cusp.
\end{remark}

\section{The exterior-square model of the automorphic group}

The form \(\Delta_5\) is an automorphic form on the Siegel space.  The
physical U-duality interpretation of the same arithmetic group is
external input from the \(K3\times E\) compactification; it is not needed
for the lattice calculation below.  The calculation records the
first-principles bridge from the Siegel variables to the type-IV
Lorentzian lattice on which the denominator algebra is written.

$$\La^4=\Z e_1\oplus\Z e_2\oplus\Z e_3\oplus\Z e_4.$$
$$g\in\SL_4(\Z):\qquad
\wedge^2g:\wedge^2\La^4\longrightarrow\wedge^2\La^4.$$
$$u\wedge v=(u,v)e_1\wedge e_2\wedge e_3\wedge e_4.$$
$$\bigl(\wedge^2\La^4,(\ ,\ )\bigr)\simeq \mathrm{II}_{3,3}.$$

Fix
$$q_0=e_1\wedge e_3+e_2\wedge e_4.$$
For $x,y\in\La^4$, define
$$-x\wedge y\wedge q_0
=B_{q_0}(x,y)e_1\wedge e_2\wedge e_3\wedge e_4.$$
$$\{g\in \SL(\La^4)\mid(\wedge^2g)q_0=q_0\}\simeq\Sp_4(\Z).$$

Set
$$\La^{3,2}=q_0^\perp\subset\wedge^2\La^4.$$
$$
f_1=e_1\wedge e_2,\quad
f_2=e_2\wedge e_3,\quad
f_3=e_1\wedge e_3-e_2\wedge e_4,\quad
f_{-2}=e_4\wedge e_1,\quad
f_{-1}=e_4\wedge e_3.
$$
$$(f_1,f_{-1})=(f_2,f_{-2})=-1,\qquad (f_3,f_3)=2.$$
$$\La^{3,2}\simeq\HypPlan\oplus\HypPlan\oplus[2],\qquad
\HypPlan=\begin{pmatrix}0&-1\\-1&0\end{pmatrix}.$$

$$\Hpl^{\IV}=
\{Z\in\Proj(\La^{3,2}\otimes\C)\mid (Z,Z)=0,\ (Z,\overline Z)<0\}.$$
$$\Hpl_+^{\IV}=
\{{}^t(z_2^2-z_1z_3,\ z_3,\ z_2,\ z_1,\ 1)z_0\in\Hpl^{\IV}
\mid \Imag z_1>0\}.$$
Writing $y_i=\Imag z_i$,
$$ (Z,\overline Z)<0\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad y_1y_3-y_2^2>0.$$
$$\Hpl_+^{\IV}\simeq
\left\{\begin{pmatrix}z_1&z_2\\z_2&z_3\end{pmatrix}\in\Hpl_2\right\}.$$

Let $\Orth_{\R}(\La^{3,2})_+$ be the index-two subgroup preserving
$\Hpl_+^{\IV}$.  Its kernel on $\Hpl_+^{\IV}$ is $\{\pm\Id_5\}$, and
$$\Orth_{\R}(\La^{3,2})_+=\{\pm\Id_5\}\SO_{\R}(\La^{3,2})_+,$$
where $\SO_{\R}(\La^{3,2})_+$ has real spin-norm $1$.  Put
$$\Orth(\La^{3,2})_+ = \Orth_{\R}(\La^{3,2})_+ \cap \Orth(\La^{3,2})$$
and
$$\SO(\La^{3,2})_+=\SO_{\R}(\La^{3,2})_+\cap\Orth(\La^{3,2}).$$

$$M=\begin{pmatrix}m_1&m_2\\m_2&m_3\end{pmatrix},$$
$$\wedge^2(g_0)
=\wedge^2\!\left(\begin{pmatrix}0 & \Id_2 \\ -\Id_2 & 0\end{pmatrix}\right)
= \begin{pmatrix}
0 & 0 & 0 & 0 & -1\\
0 & 0 & 0 & -1 & 0\\
0 & 0 & 1 & 0 & 0\\
0 & -1 & 0 & 0 & 0\\
-1 & 0 & 0 & 0 & 0
\end{pmatrix},$$
$$\wedge^2(g_M)
=\wedge^2\!\left(\begin{pmatrix}\Id_2 & M\\ 0 & \Id_2\end{pmatrix}\right)
= \begin{pmatrix}1 & -m_1 & 2m_2 & -m_3 & m_2^2 - m_1 m_3\\
0 & 1 & 0 & 0 & m_3\\
0 & 0 & 1 & 0 & m_2\\
0 & 0 & 0 & 1 & m_1\\
0 & 0 & 0 & 0 & 1\end{pmatrix},$$
$$\wedge^2(g_A)
=\wedge^2\!\left(\begin{pmatrix}{}^tA^{-1} & 0\\0 & A\end{pmatrix}\right)
= \det(A)\begin{pmatrix}1 & 0 & 0 & 0 & 0\\
0 & a_1^2 & -2a_1a_2 & a_2^2 & 0\\
0 & -a_1a_3 & a_1a_4 + a_2a_3 & -a_2a_4 & 0\\
0 & a_3^2 & -2a_3a_4 & a_4^2 & 0\\
0 & 0 & 0 & 0 & 1\end{pmatrix}$$

\begin{lemma}
The exterior-square representation is
$$\wedge^2 :
\Sp_4(\Z)/\{\pm \Id_4\} \rightarrow \SO_+(\La^{3,2}) \simeq
\Orth(\La^{3,2})_+/\{\pm\Id_5\}.$$
For every $g\in\Sp_4(\Z)$,

  \[ \begin{tikzcd}
\Hpl_2 \arrow{r}{} \arrow[swap]{d}{} & \Hpl_2 \arrow{d}{} \\%
\Hpl_+^{\IV} \arrow{r}{g \wedge g}& \Hpl_+^{\IV}
\end{tikzcd}
\]
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
The Pfaffian pairing is preserved by $\wedge^2\SL_4$.  The subgroup
fixing
$$q_0=e_1\wedge e_3+e_2\wedge e_4$$
is the group preserving the alternating form $B_{q_0}$, namely
$\Sp_4(\Z)$.  Its action preserves $q_0^\perp=\La^{3,2}$ and the displayed
component of the type-$\IV$ domain.  The kernel on $q_0^\perp$ is
$\{\pm\Id_4\}$.  The exceptional isomorphism
$\PSp_4(\R)\simeq \SO_{\R}(3,2)_+$ identifies the image with
$\SO_+(\La^{3,2})$.  The displayed matrices are the integral generators
on both sides.  Substitution of
$${}^t(z_2^2-z_1z_3,z_3,z_2,z_1,1)z_0$$
into the two actions produces the commutative square.
\end{proof}

\begin{definition}[Automorphic duality datum]
$$G_{\mathrm{aut}}=\PSp_4(\Z)\simeq\SO_+(\La^{3,2}).$$
The virtual determinant \(\mathcal D_X=\Delta_5\) is not an invariant
scalar function on
$\Hpl_2$.  It is a section of the automorphic line
$$\mathcal L^5\otimes\nu_{\Delta_5}$$
with transformation law
$$
\Delta_5(g\cdot Z)
=\nu_{\Delta_5}(g)\det(CZ+D)^5\Delta_5(Z),
\qquad
g=\begin{pmatrix}A&B\\ C&D\end{pmatrix}\in\Sp_4(\Z).
$$
The scalar square is a section of $\mathcal L^{10}$:
$$
\Delta_5^2(g\cdot Z)=\det(CZ+D)^{10}\Delta_5^2(Z).
$$
For every scalar-square branch,
$$
Z^X_{\square}(g\cdot Z)
=\det(CZ+D)^{-10}Z^X_{\square}(Z).
$$
\end{definition}

\section{The Weyl chamber and the Weyl vector}

Fix the primitive hyperbolic sublattice
$$\La^{2,1} = \HypPlan \oplus [2] \simeq \Z f_2 \oplus \Z f_3 \oplus \Z
f_{-2} \subset \La^{3,2}$$
and its type-II sublattice
$$
\La^{2,1}_{II}=
\{mf_2+lf_3+nf_{-2}\in\La^{2,1}\mid m\equiv n\equiv0\pmod2\}.
$$

Change polarization on the same Gram-index lattice:
$$
\Gamma_{\mathrm{ind}}\xrightarrow{\ \alpha\ }\La^{2,1}_{II},\qquad
\alpha(n,l,m)=2nf_2-lf_3+2mf_{-2}.
$$
The cusp polarization gives the Fock determinant.  The denominator
polarization gives the Borcherds chamber.

Extend $\phi\in\Orth(\La^{2,1})$ by the identity on
$(\La^{2,1})^\perp$:
$$\Orth(\La^{2,1})\hookrightarrow\Orth(\La^{3,2}).$$
For the component-preserving subgroup attached to the positive cone
below,
$$\Delta_5\in M_5(\Orth(\La^{2,1})_+,\nu_{\Delta_5}).$$

For a primitive element $\alpha \in \La^{2,1}$ satisfying
$(\alpha,\alpha)>0$ and
$$(\alpha,\alpha)\mid 2(\La^{2,1},\alpha),$$
Kac reflection \cite{KAC:1}:
$$s_{\alpha}:x\mapsto x-2\frac{(x,\alpha)}{(\alpha,\alpha)}\alpha.$$
$$s_{\alpha}(\alpha)=-\alpha,\qquad
s_{\alpha}|_{\alpha^\perp}=\Id.$$
For $(\alpha,\alpha)=2$:
$$s_{\alpha}: x \mapsto
x - (x,\alpha)\alpha.$$

\begin{lemma}
Let $(\alpha,\alpha)=2$.  For
$$\delta_1=2f_2-f_3,\qquad
\delta_2=2f_{-2}-f_3,\qquad
\delta_3=f_3,$$
\cite[Theorem 2.1 and Section 4]{GN}; equivalently \cite[Section 5.1.1, case (t=1,II,0)]{GNII}.
$$\Delta_5(s_{\alpha}Z) = - \Delta_5(Z)$$
when $\alpha\in\{\delta_1,\delta_2,\delta_3\}$.  For
$$\alpha\in\{f_{-2}-f_2,\ f_2-f_3,\ f_2+f_3\},$$
$$\Delta_5(s_{\alpha}Z) = \Delta_5(Z)$$
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
Let
$$\overline U=\wedge^2\begin{pmatrix}{}^tU^{-1}&0\\0&U\end{pmatrix},
\qquad U\in\GL_2(\Z).$$
Required reflections:
$$s_{f_{-2}-f_2}=-\overline{\begin{pmatrix}0&1\\1&0\end{pmatrix}},
\qquad
s_{f_3}=-\overline{\begin{pmatrix}1&0\\0&-1\end{pmatrix}},
\qquad
s_{f_2-f_3}=-\overline{\begin{pmatrix}1&-1\\0&-1\end{pmatrix}}.$$
Maass's character has value $-1$ on
$s_{\delta_i}$ and $+1$ on the three other reflection classes.
\end{proof}

\noindent The time-like cone is
$$\Cone(\La^{2,1}) = \{ x \in \La^{2,1}
\otimes \R | (x,x) < 0\}.$$
Let $\Cone(\La^{2,1})_+$ be the component for which
$$\Omega(\Cone(\La^{2,1})_+):=
\La^{2,1}\otimes\R+i\Cone(\La^{2,1})_+\subset\Hpl^{\IV}_+.$$
For
$$z=z_3f_2+z_2f_3+z_1f_{-2}\in\Omega(\Cone(\La^{2,1})_+),$$
the type $\IV$ point is
$$Z={}^t(z_2^2-z_1z_3,\ z_3,\ z_2,\ z_1,\ 1)z_0.$$
Let $\Orth(\La^{2,1})_+$ be the index-two subgroup fixing
$\Cone(\La^{2,1})_+$.  It acts discretely on
$$\Cone(\La^{2,1})_+/\R_{>0}.$$

For $(\alpha,\alpha)>0$,
$$\Hpl_{\alpha}=
\{\R_{>0}x\in\Cone(\La^{2,1})_+/\R_{>0}\mid (x,\alpha)=0\},$$
and
$$\Hpl_{\alpha,+}=
\{\R_{>0}x\in\Cone(\La^{2,1})_+/\R_{>0}\mid (x,\alpha)\leq0\}.$$
Let $W(\La^{2,1})$ be the subgroup generated by these positive-norm
reflections:
$$W(\La^{2,1})\subset\Orth(\La^{2,1})_+.$$


Nikulin's theorem for $\HypPlan\oplus[2]$ \cite{NIKULIN}:
$$\Orth(\La^{2,1})_+=W^{(2)}(\La^{2,1}),$$
where $W^{(2)}$ is generated by reflections in square-$2$ vectors.
For $k>0$ put
$$\Delta^{(k)}(\La^{2,1})=
\{\delta\in\La^{2,1}\mid \delta\ \text{primitive},\
(\delta,\delta)=k,\ s_\delta\in\Orth(\La^{2,1})\}.$$
Each $\delta\in\Delta^{(2)}(\La^{2,1})$ has one of two divisibilities:
\begin{itemize}
\item Type I: $(\delta, \La^{2,1}) = \Z$
\item Type II: $(\delta, \La^{2,1}) = 2\Z$
\end{itemize}

The type sublattices are
$$\La^{2,1}_I=
\{mf_2+lf_3+nf_{-2}\in\La^{2,1}\mid m+l+n\equiv0\pmod2\},$$
and the already defined \(\La^{2,1}_{II}\).
Type I roots lie in $\La^{2,1}_I$; type II roots lie in
$\La^{2,1}_{II}$.  The reflection subgroups are normal, with indices
$$[W^{(2)}(\La^{2,1}):W^{(2)}(\La^{2,1}_I)]=2,\qquad
[W^{(2)}(\La^{2,1}):W^{(2)}(\La^{2,1}_{II})]=6.$$

The chambers are
$$\Poly'=\bigcap_{\delta\in\Poly'_{prim}}\Hpl_{\delta,+},
\qquad \Poly'\in\{\Poly,\Poly_I,\Poly_{II}\},$$
with walls
$$\Poly_{prim}=\{f_2-f_3,\ f_{-2}-f_2,\ f_3\},$$
$$\Poly_{I,prim}=\{f_2-f_3,\ f_{-2}-f_2,\ f_2+f_3\},$$
$$\Poly_{II,prim}=\{\delta_1,\delta_2,\delta_3\}.$$
For
$$\Aut(\Poly')=\{g\in\Orth(\La^{2,1})_+\mid g\Poly'=\Poly'\},$$
$$\Aut(\Poly)=1,\qquad
\Aut(\Poly_I)=\langle s_{f_3}\rangle,\qquad
\Aut(\Poly_{II})\simeq S_3,$$
with $\Aut(\Poly_{II})$ generated by
$s_{f_2-f_3}$ and $s_{f_{-2}-f_2}$.  The chamber decomposition is
$$\Orth(\La^{2,1})_+
\simeq W^{(2)}(\La^{2,1})
\simeq W^{(2)}(\La^{2,1}_I)\rtimes\Aut(\Poly_I)
\simeq W^{(2)}(\La^{2,1}_{II})\rtimes\Aut(\Poly_{II}).$$

\begin{lemma}[Multiplier restriction]
\label{lem:maass-multiplier-restriction}
\begin{itemize}
  \item for $w \in W^{(2)}(\La^{2,1}_I)$ and $a \in \Aut(\Poly_{I})$,
  $$\Delta_5(w \cdot a Z) = \text{det}(a) \Delta_5(Z)$$
  \item for $w \in W^{(2)}(\La^{2,1}_{II})$ and $a \in \Aut(\Poly_{II})$,
  $$\Delta_5(w \cdot a Z) = \text{det}(w) \Delta_5(Z)$$
\end{itemize}

\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
Displayed Maass multiplier \cite{MAASS:1}, \cite[Section 3]{GN}, \cite{Gritsenko99}:
$$\nu_{\Delta_5}(s_{\delta_i})=-1,\qquad
\nu_{\Delta_5}(s_{f_{-2}-f_2})
=\nu_{\Delta_5}(s_{f_2-f_3})
=\nu_{\Delta_5}(s_{f_2+f_3})=1.$$
Semidirect products:
$$W^{(2)}(\La^{2,1}_I)\rtimes\Aut(\Poly_I),\qquad
W^{(2)}(\La^{2,1}_{II})\rtimes\Aut(\Poly_{II}).$$
\end{proof}

Set
$$\Delta(\La^{2,1}_{II})_+
= \R_{\geq 0} \delta_1 + \R_{\geq 0} \delta_2
+ \R_{\geq 0} \delta_3$$
and
$$\Delta(\La^{2,1}_{II})_+^* = \{ x \in \La^{2,1} \otimes \R | (x,
\delta_i) \leq 0 \}.$$
For the finite-volume chamber $\Poly_{II}$, the dual cone obeys
$$\Delta(\La^{2,1}_{II})_+^* \subset
\overline{\Cone(\La^{2,1})_+} \subset  \Delta(\La^{2,1}_{II})_+.$$

The Weyl vector is determined by
$$ (\rho,\delta_i)=-\frac{(\delta_i,\delta_i)}{2}=-1,\qquad i=1,2,3.$$
$$(\delta_i,\delta_j) =
\begin{pmatrix}2 & -2 & -2\\-2 & 2 & -2\\-2 & -2 & 2\end{pmatrix}.$$
$$\rho = \frac{1}{2}\delta_1 + \frac{1}{2}\delta_2 + \frac{1}{2}\delta_3 = f_2 - \frac{1}{2}f_3 + f_{-2}.$$

Also
$$\rho \in
\Cone(\La^{2,1})_+ = \Cone(\La^{2,1}_{II})_+.$$

Fix
$$z = z_1 f_{-2} + z_2 f_3 + z_3 f_2
\in \La^{2,1} \otimes \R + i\Cone(\La^{2,1})_+
= \La^{2,1}_{II} \otimes \R + i\Cone(\La^{2,1}_{II})_+.$$
The dual lattice is
$$(\La^{2,1}_{II})^* = \Z \frac{1}{2} f_2 + \Z \frac{1}{2} f_3 + \Z \frac{1}{2} f_{-2} = \frac{1}{2}\La^{2,1}.$$

\begin{definition}[Gram-index degrees in the Weyl chamber]
\label{def:gram-index-degrees-weyl-chamber}
For $\gamma=(n,l,m)\in\Gamma_{\mathrm{ind}}$ set
$$\alpha(\gamma)=\alpha(n,l,m)=2nf_2-lf_3+2mf_{-2}
\in\La^{2,1}_{II}.$$
With
$$z=z_1f_{-2}+z_2f_3+z_3f_2,$$
the character of the Gram-index degree is
$$x^\gamma=q^nr^ls^m=\exp(-\pi i(\alpha(\gamma),z)).$$
For $\gamma'=(n',l',m')$,
$$
(\alpha(\gamma),\alpha(\gamma'))
=-2\langle\gamma,\gamma'\rangle_{\mathrm{ind}},
\qquad
(\alpha(\gamma),\alpha(\gamma))=-2(4nm-l^2).
$$
Thus the Borcherds degree is the Lorentzian image of the Gram-index
grading.  The Weyl chamber and real walls are part of the
Gritsenko--Nikulin/Nikulin root datum.  The cusp polarization fixed in
Section \ref{sec:duality-principle} selects the corresponding product
expansion, and the active Jacobi support gives the nonzero visible
product exponents in that chamber.
$$E_0:=\rho.$$
$$q^{1/2}r^{1/2}s^{1/2}=\exp(-\pi i(\rho,z)).$$
$$\exp(-2\pi i(\alpha(\gamma),z)),\qquad
\exp(-2\pi i(\rho,z)).$$
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Active support and Borcherds cone]
In the standard cusp chamber, the active support is
$$
\Gamma_{\mathrm{act}}
=\{\gamma=(n,l,m)\in\Gamma_{\mathrm{eff}}\mid f(nm,l)\neq0\}.
$$
The inactive triples in $\Gamma_{\mathrm{eff}}\setminus\Gamma_{\mathrm{act}}$
are ordering data only; their product exponents are zero.  The product
does not prove absence of root spaces with zero signed superdimension.
The proof-grade Borcherds cone is the real cone generated by the active
positive Gram-index degrees after the Lorentzian degree map:
$$
\Cone_{\mathrm{Borch}}
:=\R_{\geq0}\,\alpha(\Gamma_{\mathrm{act}})
\subset \La^{2,1}_{II}\otimes\R.
$$
The real-root hyperplanes are the walls used by the denominator
identity in this polarization.
\end{definition}

\begin{lemma}[Active support gives the type-II chamber cone]
\label{lem:active-support-type-ii-cone}
For $\gamma=(n,l,m)\in\Gamma_{\mathrm{act}}$,
$$
\alpha(\gamma)
=n\delta_1+m\delta_2+(n+m-l)\delta_3,
$$
with
$$n\ge0,\qquad m\ge0,\qquad n+m-l\ge0.$$
Consequently
$$
\Cone_{\mathrm{Borch}}
=\R_{\geq0}\delta_1+\R_{\geq0}\delta_2+\R_{\geq0}\delta_3.
$$
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
The displayed decomposition is
$$
n(2f_2-f_3)+m(2f_{-2}-f_3)+(n+m-l)f_3
=2nf_2-lf_3+2mf_{-2}.
$$
The effective chamber gives $n,m\ge0$.  Since
$\phi_{0,1}$ is weak of index one, $f(nm,l)\ne0$ implies
$4nm-l^2\ge-1$.  If $n=0$ or $m=0$, this gives $l^2\le1$, and the
boundary cases in $\Gamma_{\mathrm{eff}}$ give $l\le n+m$.  If
$n,m>0$ and $l\ge n+m+1$, then
$$
l^2\ge(n+m+1)^2
=4nm+(n-m)^2+2(n+m)+1>4nm+1,
$$
contradicting $l^2\le4nm+1$.  Hence $n+m-l\ge0$.
The reverse inclusion follows from the active triples
$$
(1,0,0),\qquad (0,0,1),\qquad (0,-1,0),
$$
whose degrees are $\delta_1+\delta_3$, $\delta_2+\delta_3$, and
$\delta_3$, and from the active triples
$$
(1,1,0),\qquad (0,1,1),
$$
whose degrees are $\delta_1$ and $\delta_2$.
\end{proof}

For $n,l,m \in \Z$ with $n \equiv m \equiv l \equiv 1 \mod 2$,
$n,m > 0$ and
$4nm - l^2 > 0$, set
$$a = (n-1) f_2 - \frac{l-1}{2} f_3 + (m-1) f_{-2},
\qquad
m(a) = -\frac{1}{64} c_\Delta(n,l,m).$$
\cite[Theorem 2.1]{GN}
$$\rho+a=nf_2-\frac l2f_3+mf_{-2},$$
and
$$\frac{1}{64}c_\Delta(n,l,m)\exp(\pi i (n z_1 + lz_2 + m z_3)) $$
$$= \frac{1}{64} c_\Delta(n,l,m)
\exp\left(- \pi i\left(nf_2-\frac{l}{2}f_3+mf_{-2}, z\right)\right)$$
$$= -m(a) \exp (-\pi i(\rho +a, z)),$$
with
$$a\in(\La^{2,1})^*=\frac{1}{2}\La^{2,1}_{II}.$$
The normalization $c_\Delta(1,1,1)=64$ fixes $m(0)=-1$.  Since
$c_\Delta(n,l,m)\in64\Z$, all $m(a)$ are integral.  The inequality
$4nm-l^2>0$ implies
$$\rho+a\in \Cone(\La^{2,1})_+.$$

Let $\lambda=\rho+a$.  For nonzero coefficients in the chosen chamber,
$$\lambda\in(\La^{2,1}_{II})^*\cap\R_+\Poly_{II},\qquad
(\lambda,\delta_i)\leq0.$$
If $(\lambda,\delta_i)=0$, then
$$c_\lambda=-c_\lambda=0.$$
For nonzero terms, $(\lambda,\delta_i)<0$.  Since
$(\rho,\delta_i)=-1$,
$$(a,\delta_i)\leq0,\qquad
a\in\Delta(\La^{2,1}_{II})^*_+.$$
$$a \in \R_{\geq 0} \Delta(\La^{2,1}_{II})_+^* \cap
\overline{\Cone(\La^{2,1})_+} = \R_{\geq 0} \Poly_{II}.$$
The congruences $m\equiv n\equiv l\equiv1\pmod2$ imply
$$a\in 2(\La^{2,1})^*=\La^{2,1}_{II}.$$
$$a=0\qquad\hbox{or}\qquad
a\in\La^{2,1}_{II}\cap\R_{>0}\Poly_{II}.$$


\begin{lemma}
$$\frac{1}{64}\Delta_5(Z)
=\displaystyle\sum_{w \in W^{(2)}(\La^{2,1}_{II})} \text{det}(w)( \exp(-\pi
i(w(\rho),z))- \sum_{a \in \La^{2,1}_{II}\cap\R_{>0}\Poly_{II}}
m(a)\exp(-\pi i(w(\rho+a),z)))$$
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
Let $c_\lambda$ be the coefficient of $e^{-\pi i(\lambda,z)}$ in
$64^{-1}\Delta_5$.  The leading term has
$$\lambda=\rho,\qquad c_\rho=1.$$
The other exponents in the chosen chamber have
$$\lambda=\rho+a,\qquad
a\in\La^{2,1}_{II}\cap\R_{>0}\Poly_{II},\qquad
c_{\rho+a}=-m(a).$$
Anti-invariance:
$$c_{w\lambda}=\det(w)c_\lambda.$$
If $\lambda$ lies on a simple wall, then
$$s_{\delta_i}\lambda=\lambda,\qquad c_\lambda=-c_\lambda=0.$$
Summing the signed Weyl translates proves the formula.
\end{proof}

The primitive isotropic rays of $\overline{\Poly_{II}}$ are generated by
$$2f_2,\qquad 2f_{-2},\qquad 2f_2-2f_3+2f_{-2}.$$
The group $\Aut(\Poly_{II})\simeq S_3$ is transitive on these three
vectors.  For $a_0=2f_2$:

$$1 + \frac{1}{64} \sum_{t \geq 1} c_\Delta(1 + 2t, 1, 1)q^t = \displaystyle\prod_{k\geq 1} (1
- q^k)^9$$

In denominator notation,

$$ 1 - \sum_{t \geq 1} m(t a_0) q^t = \displaystyle\prod_{t\geq 1}
(1 - q^t)^{\tau(t a_0)},\qquad \tau(t a_0)=9\quad(t\geq1).$$

By $S_3$-symmetry,
$$\tau(ta)=9\qquad(t\geq1)$$
for every primitive isotropic ray
$$\Z_{>0}a\subset
\overline{\Poly_{II}}\cap\La^{2,1}_{II}.$$
On isotropic rays, the coefficients $m(ta)$ are determined by the
eta-product expansion; the signed simple-root supermultiplicity is
\(\tau(ta)\).  The imaginary simple roots of $\autcor$ are these
isotropic and timelike rays in $\overline{\Poly_{II}}\cap\La^{2,1}_{II}$,
with multiplicities $\tau(a)$ on isotropic rays and $m(a)$ on
negative-norm rays \cite[Theorem 2.1]{GN}, \cite[(5.1), Section 5.1.1]{GNII}.


The real root datum is the wall set
$$\Poly_{II,prim}=\{\delta_1,\delta_2,\delta_3\}$$
with Gram matrix \cite[Theorem 4.1]{GN} (and \cite[Section 5.1.1, case (t=1,II,0)]{GNII} as secondary)

$$(\delta_i,\delta_j) = \begin{pmatrix}2 & -2 & -2\\-2 & 2 & -2\\-2 & -2 & 2\end{pmatrix}$$

\begin{definition}[Simple real roots and perturbative walls]
$$\Delta^{re}_{\mathrm{simp}}=\{\delta_1,\delta_2,\delta_3\},\qquad
\Delta^{re}=W^{(2)}(\La^{2,1}_{II})\Delta^{re}_{\mathrm{simp}},$$
$$
\mathcal W_{\mathrm{pert}}
=\bigcup_{\delta\in\Delta^{re}_{\mathrm{simp}}}\Hpl_\delta.
$$
\end{definition}

\section{The denominator algebra}

$$A=((\delta_i,\delta_j))_{1\leq i,j\leq3}
=\begin{pmatrix}2&-2&-2\\-2&2&-2\\-2&-2&2\end{pmatrix}$$
$$A\ \hbox{symmetric generalized Cartan},\qquad
\bkm(A)\ \hbox{Kac--Moody}.$$
$$\mathcal A_{\mathrm{den}}:=\autcor.$$
This is the target-internal algebraic denominator square root.  It is the
automorphic correction of $\bkm(A)$ constructed by
Gritsenko--Nikulin \cite[Sections~3--4]{GN}, with root spaces graded by the Gram-degree
map
$$
\gamma=(n,l,m)\longmapsto
\alpha(\gamma)=2nf_2-lf_3+2mf_{-2}.
$$
The Borcherds correction character in the coefficient chamber is
$$\mathcal C_{\mathrm{im}}(z)
=1-\sum_{a\in\La^{2,1}_{II}\cap\R_{>0}\Poly_{II}}
m(a)e^{-2\pi i(a,z)}.$$
$$e^{-2\pi i(\rho,z)}\mathcal C_{\mathrm{im}}(z).$$

Signed root-superdimension convention; Harvey--Moore is the external
physical interpretation \cite{HM}:
$$\smult(\alpha)
=\dim\mathfrak{g}_{\alpha,\overline 0}
-\dim\mathfrak{g}_{\alpha,\overline 1}.$$
Let \(\mathcal R\) be the root set of
\(\mathfrak g_{\Delta_5}\), and let \(\mathcal R_+\) be the positive
root set in the \(\Poly_{II}\)-chamber.

\begin{definition}[Denominator Lie superalgebra]
For $\gamma\in\Gamma_{\mathrm{ind}}$ set
$$
\mathcal A_{\mathrm{den},\gamma}
:=
\begin{cases}
\La^{2,1}_{II}\otimes\C,&\gamma=0,\\
\mathfrak g_{\Delta_5,\alpha(\gamma)},&\alpha(\gamma)\in\mathcal R,\\
0,&\alpha(\gamma)\notin\mathcal R.
\end{cases}
$$
The zero degree is the Cartan subalgebra and is not governed by
\(f(0,0)\).  The bracket is the Borcherds--Kac--Moody bracket of
\(\autcor\):
$$
[\ ,\ ]:
\mathcal A_{\mathrm{den},\gamma}
\otimes
\mathcal A_{\mathrm{den},\gamma'}
\longrightarrow
\mathcal A_{\mathrm{den},\gamma+\gamma'}.
$$
\end{definition}

\begin{theorem}[Denominator algebra identity]
\label{thm:denominator-algebra-identity}
The denominator Lie superalgebra has the following properties.
$$
\mathcal A_{\mathrm{den}}
=\mathcal A_{\mathrm{den},0}\oplus
\bigoplus_{\substack{\gamma\in\Gamma_{\mathrm{ind}}\\
\alpha(\gamma)\in\mathcal R}}
\mathcal A_{\mathrm{den},\gamma}
=\mathcal A_{\mathrm{den},0}
\oplus\mathcal A_{\mathrm{den}}^{\mathrm{bulk}}
\oplus\mathcal A_{\mathrm{den}}^{\mathrm{cusp}},
\qquad
[\mathcal A_{\mathrm{den},\gamma},\mathcal A_{\mathrm{den},\gamma'}]
\subset \mathcal A_{\mathrm{den},\gamma+\gamma'},
$$
where
$\mathcal A_{\mathrm{den}}^{\mathrm{bulk}}
=\bigoplus_{\alpha(\gamma)\in\mathcal R,\,m(\gamma)>0}
\mathcal A_{\mathrm{den},\gamma}$
records the $m>0$ Borcherds bulk and
$\mathcal A_{\mathrm{den}}^{\mathrm{cusp}}
=\bigoplus_{\alpha(\gamma)\in\mathcal R,\,m(\gamma)=0}
\mathcal A_{\mathrm{den},\gamma}$
records the $m=0$ Weyl-chamber cusp boundary, in parallel with the
$\mathcal V=\mathcal V_{\mathrm{bulk}}\oplus\mathcal V_{\mathrm{cusp}}$
splitting at the determinant level above.
Its visible positive signed Gram-degree multiplicities are the K3 half-index
coefficients:
$$
\smult(\alpha(n,l,m))=f(nm,l)
\qquad((n,l,m)\in\Gamma_{\mathrm{act}}).
$$
Its Weyl--Kac--Borcherds denominator is
$$
\operatorname{den}(\mathcal A_{\mathrm{den}})
=64^{-1}\Delta_5(2Z).
$$
The theorem concerns the Borcherds denominator algebra.  A microscopic
BPS Hilbert space and its operator product require separate
construction.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Gritsenko--Nikulin \cite[Theorem 2.1, (2.1)--(2.3)]{GNII} construct $\autcor$ as the generalized
Borcherds--Kac--Moody superalgebra whose real simple roots are
$\delta_1,\delta_2,\delta_3$ and whose imaginary simple-root
multiplicities are read from the Borcherds correction character.  A
product exponent gives the signed multiplicity of a visible positive
root; the simple imaginary-root datum is Gritsenko--Nikulin's \(m(a)\)
for negative-norm \(a\) and \(\tau(a)\) on isotropic rays.  These are
different pieces of the denominator construction.  A
root-graded Lie superalgebra has
$$
[\mathfrak g_{\Delta_5,\alpha},\mathfrak g_{\Delta_5,\beta}]
\subset\mathfrak g_{\Delta_5,\alpha+\beta}.
$$
Here \(\alpha\in\La^{2,1}_{II}\otimes\C\), and the addition
\(\alpha+\beta\) is linear inside the Cartan; this is the linear root
grading of a Borcherds--Kac superalgebra.  The Gram-degree map
\[
\gamma=(n,l,m)\longmapsto\alpha(\gamma)=2nf_2-lf_3+2mf_{-2}
\in\La^{2,1}_{II}\otimes\C
\]
is the inverse correspondence of root indexing: it is additive in
\((n,l,m)\) and recovers the linear addition in
\(\La^{2,1}_{II}\otimes\C\).  This linear additivity is the relevant
statement for the denominator algebra of \(\Delta_5\), where the grading
lattice is \(\La^{2,1}_{II}\) and \(\Gamma_{\mathrm{ind}}=\Z^3\) is the
Gram parametrization of that grading.  In a hypothetical Hall source,
the underlying lattice is the physical
\(\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}=\La_S\oplus\La_S\), the Hall bracket is
graded by \(\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}\) (additive), and the
\(\Gamma_{\mathrm{ind}}\)-grading of the denominator algebra is the
\(\Pi\)-image, well defined modulo the cocycle \(B\) of
Definition~\ref{def:dyonic-mukai-lattice}.  The denominator identity reads
$$
\frac1{64}\Delta_5(2Z)
=e^{-2\pi i(\rho,z)}
\prod_{\alpha\in\mathcal R_+}
(1-e^{-2\pi i(\alpha,z)})^{\smult(\alpha)}.
$$
Comparing this with the Borcherds product gives
$$
\smult(\alpha(n,l,m))=f(nm,l)
\qquad((n,l,m)\in\Gamma_{\mathrm{act}}).
$$
\end{proof}

\begin{definition}[Formal current envelope]
Let $E$ be the elliptic curve in $X=S\times E$.  Put
$$
\operatorname{Cur}_E(\mathcal A_{\mathrm{den}})
:=\mathcal A_{\mathrm{den}}\otimes\mathcal O_E
$$
with the level-zero current bracket
$$
[a\otimes f,b\otimes g]=[a,b]\otimes fg.
$$
Its chiral enveloping algebra in the sense of Beilinson--Drinfeld
\cite{BD} is
$$
\mathsf{Den}_{\Delta_5,E}
:=U_E^{\mathrm{ch}}\!
\left(\operatorname{Cur}_E(\mathcal A_{\mathrm{den}})\right).
$$
\end{definition}

\begin{proposition}[Formal current envelope]
\label{prop:formal-current-envelope}
\(\mathsf{Den}_{\Delta_5,E}\) is the formal completed ind
Beilinson--Drinfeld current envelope on \(E\) obtained from the
denominator Lie superalgebra.  Its constant-current Lie superalgebra is
\(\mathcal A_{\mathrm{den}}\), and the denominator of that
constant-current bracket is
$$
64^{-1}\Delta_5(2Z).
$$
A compact \(E_3\)/Hall/chiral BPS realization requires additional
microscopic input.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
In the completed ind setting, the current construction sends a Lie
superalgebra to a Lie-* algebra on a smooth curve, and the chiral
enveloping construction sends a Lie-* algebra to a chiral algebra
\cite{BD}; equivalently, in vertex-algebra language, this is the
universal current vertex algebra at level zero \cite{KACVA}.  Constant
sections of
$\mathcal A_{\mathrm{den}}\otimes\mathcal O_E$ recover the original Lie
superalgebra.  The denominator statement is exactly
Theorem \ref{thm:denominator-algebra-identity}.
\end{proof}

\begin{definition}[Holomorphic \(E_3\) quantum upgrade]
The determinant and denominator results above are protected
Euler-characteristic statements.  The expected quantum upgrade does not
start from the scalar determinant.  It would start from a supplied
holomorphic \(E_3\)-factorization algebra on the Calabi--Yau threefold
$$
\mathcal A^{E_3}_X,\qquad X=K3\times E.
$$
By a holomorphic \(E_3\)-factorization algebra is meant here: a
factorization algebra on \(X\) in the sense of Costello--Gwilliam
(\cite{CostelloGwilliam1}, \cite{CostelloGwilliam2} esp.~vol.~II
\S10--11), locally constant in real directions and holomorphic in three
complex directions, whose factorization structure maps are governed by
holomorphic polydiscs in \(\C^3\); equivalently a factorization algebra
in the holomorphic \(E_3\)-operadic sense, with the framed
\(E_3\)-structure encoding the \(SO(6)\)-rotational symmetry of
\(\C^3\).  This symbol, and the placeholder \(\Phi^{\mathrm{FA}}_3(X)\),
denote the Stage-1 object required in the Calabi--Yau-to-chiral
construction; they are not a constructed functor evaluated on \(X\).
The candidate concrete realization, supplied as proposal-only schema, is
the local protected observable algebra
\(\mathcal A_X(U)\) of
Definition~\ref{def:local-protected-observable-algebra}.
A compact holomorphic-Chern--Simons/BV model, if constructed with the
required descent, quantum master equation, and anomaly cancellation,
would be a candidate source for this datum in the completed charge
category.  Such a source also requires a chosen \(E_3\)-formality point,
a chain-level \(S^3\)-framing witness, compact-support control, and
finite-stage HN quotients on which all operations are defined before
passing to the completed inverse system.

The curve-level BPS algebra would be obtained only after a supplied Stage-2
specialization along the \(K3\)-direction.  Split the triple
identification into three named pieces, each carrying a separately
labelled comparison map:
\[
\mathcal A^{E_3}_X
\xrightarrow{\ \mathrm{Sp}^{\mathrm{ch}}_{K3,E}\ }
\mathcal F_X^{(0)}
\xrightarrow{\ \kappa_E\ }
\mathcal F_X^{(1)}
\xrightarrow{\ \pi_*^{\mathrm{ch}}\ }
(p_E)_*\mathcal A^{E_3}_X.
\]
Here:
\(\mathrm{Sp}^{\mathrm{ch}}_{K3,E}\) is the
Beilinson--Drinfeld chiral pushforward along the \(K3\)-fibration
\(p_E:K3\times E\to E\) with K3-integration in the Costello--Gwilliam
sense: pointwise on \(E\), the fibre \(K3\)-direction of the
factorization algebra is integrated to a chiral shadow on \(E\); its
output \(\mathcal F_X^{(0)}\) is a chiral algebra on \(E\) (equivalently
a factorization algebra on \(\operatorname{Ran}(E)\)).
\(\kappa_E\) is the
chiral-Koszul comparison \(\mathcal F_X^{(0)}\to\mathcal F_X^{(1)}\),
where \(\mathcal F_X^{(1)}\) is the candidate identification of the
chiral pushforward with the ordinary derived pushforward
\((p_E)_*\mathcal A^{E_3}_X\) regarded as a sheaf-of-cochain factorization
algebra on \(\operatorname{Ran}(E)\); identification of
chiral and ordinary pushforward is the open chiral-Koszul comparison.
\(\pi_*^{\mathrm{ch}}\) is the closing identification of
\(\mathcal F_X^{(1)}\) with \((p_E)_*\mathcal A^{E_3}_X\) as
factorization data, comparing the Costello--Gwilliam push along a
proper holomorphic submersion with the topological pushforward; this
comparison reduces to the standard fact in the projection-finite
sectors and is open in the wrapped sectors.  The convenient shorthand
\(\mathcal F_X\) refers to any one of \(\mathcal F_X^{(0)}\),
\(\mathcal F_X^{(1)}\), or \((p_E)_*\mathcal A^{E_3}_X\) once
\(\kappa_E\) and \(\pi_*^{\mathrm{ch}}\) have been supplied.  Without
the chiral-Koszul comparison and the proper-pushforward identification,
the three names are distinct objects.
Restrictions to chambers, pushforwards to \(E\), and chiral Koszul
dualities are then operations on \(\mathcal A^{E_3}_X\) and on its
\(E_1\)-chiral shadow \(\mathcal F_X\), not replacements for the
\(E_3\)-source.

After these data have been constructed, the required Igusa statement is
the pair of comparisons
$$
H^0\Prim_{\mathrm{prot}}(\Pi_{X,*}\mathcal F_X)
\stackrel{?}{\cong}
\mathfrak g_{\Delta_5},
\qquad
\Omega_E^{\mathrm{ch}}C_X
\stackrel{?}{\simeq}
\mathsf{Den}_{\Delta_5,E}.
$$
Here \(C_X\) is the chiral bar coalgebra attached to the shadow
\(\mathcal F_X\).  The first comparison would be the bracket theorem.
The second would be the chiral Koszul theorem.  Both require microscopic
data beyond the scalar square and beyond the formal current envelope.
\end{definition}

\begin{openproblem}[Compact holomorphic \(E_3\) source]
\label{op:compact-e3-source}
Construct the source object \(\mathcal A^{E_3}_X\) for
\(X=K3\times E\).  A candidate compact holomorphic-Chern--Simons/BV
construction must prove, before any comparison with \(\Delta_5\), the
following finite-chain data:
\begin{enumerate}
\item descent for local observables on \(X\) and a quantum master
equation after compact charge completion;
\item anomaly cancellation, a fixed \(E_3\)-formality point (in the
sense of Tamarkin formality for \(E_n\)-operads;
Tamarkin (1998), Kontsevich (1999); the framed-\(E_3\) refinement is
Severa--Willwacher (2011)), a chain-level \(S^3\)-framing witness (a
chain-level lift of the \(E_3\)-framed-vs.-unframed comparison
witnessed by the \(SO(3)\)-action on \(S^2=\partial D^3\), giving the
\(SO(3)\)-rotational symmetry data; equivalently a chain-level
\(SO(3)\)-equivariance of the local observable algebra), and
compact-support control;
\item a finite-first sectorial completion compatible with
Harder--Narasimhan quotients, with all operations defined on finite
stages before completion;
\item the chain-level \(K3\)-to-\(E\) specialization
\(\mathrm{Sp}^{\mathrm{ch}}_{K3,E}\);
\item the projection-finite or hybrid wrapped repair for positive
elliptic degree;
\item a strong orientation, protected integration, and primitive
recognition certificate.
\end{enumerate}
Existing BV, CoHA, and chiral-algebra formalisms give the language for
these requirements.  They do not, by themselves, construct this compact
source for \(K3\times E\).  The external open data are: the
\(E_3\)-formality point (Tamarkin/Kontsevich formality at a chosen
associator, of which the Drinfeld--Kontsevich associator is the
canonical choice; rationality of formality is open over \(\Q\) but
known over \(\R\)), and the chain-level \(S^3\)-framing witness for the
holomorphic \(E_3\)-structure (existence at the level of homotopy types
follows from framed-\(E_n\) formality; chain-level constructibility for
the candidate concrete realization
\(\mathcal A_X(U)\) of
Definition~\ref{def:local-protected-observable-algebra} is open).
\end{openproblem}

\begin{remark}[Where the quantum comparison would live]
Assume the source algebra \(\mathcal A^{E_3}_X\), the specialization
\(\mathrm{Sp}^{\mathrm{ch}}_{K3,E}\), a conilpotent coalgebra
\(C_X\stackrel{?}{\simeq}\bar B_E^{\mathrm{ch}}(\mathcal F_X)\), and a
quasi-isomorphism
\[
\Theta_{\mathrm{Kos}}:
\Omega_E^{\mathrm{ch}}C_X
\stackrel{?}{\simeq}
\mathsf{Den}_{\Delta_5,E}
\]
have all been supplied.  Then \(\mathcal F_X\) is the place where the
protected primitive bracket and the chiral Koszul comparison must be
formulated.  Costello--Gwilliam locality explains why a holomorphic
quantum theory would produce factorization products before any trace or
determinant is taken \cite{CostelloRenormalization},
\cite{CostelloGwilliam1}, \cite{CostelloGwilliam2}; Beilinson--
Drinfeld chiral operations are the curve-level algebraic form of
collision maps \cite{BD}.  None of this is obtained from the scalar
square or from the denominator identity alone.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Pushforward, restriction, Koszul duality]
The second step is specialization, not inversion.  A restriction to a chamber
or sector is a restriction of \(\mathcal A^{E_3}_X\) before, or of
\(\mathcal F_X\) after, the \(K3\)-specialization.  Pushforward along
\(p_E\) is the geometric notation for the same specialization.  A
compact Koszul theorem would require a supplied conilpotent coalgebra
\(C_X\), an identification
$$
C_X\stackrel{?}{\simeq} \overline B_E^{\mathrm{ch}}(\mathcal F_X),
$$
and a further quasi-isomorphism
$$
\Omega_E^{\mathrm{ch}}C_X
\stackrel{?}{\simeq}
\mathsf{Den}_{\Delta_5,E}.
$$
These are not procedures for reconstructing the holomorphic
\(E_3\)-source from the denominator alone.
\end{remark}

\begin{proposition}[Target-internal bar--cobar inversion]
\label{prop:target-internal-bar-cobar-inversion}
In the conilpotent / augmented chiral setting where Francis--Gaitsgory
chiral Koszul duality applies, the formal target
\(\mathsf{Den}_{\Delta_5,E}\) has its own bar--cobar inversion:
\[
\Omega_E^{\mathrm{ch}}\bar B_E^{\mathrm{ch}}
(\mathsf{Den}_{\Delta_5,E})
\longrightarrow
\mathsf{Den}_{\Delta_5,E}.
\]
The conilpotency hypothesis is satisfied here because
\(\mathcal A_{\mathrm{den}}\) carries a charge filtration with finite
dimensional graded pieces in each \(\Gamma_{\mathrm{ind}}\)-degree, and
this filtration lifts to the chiral envelope
\(\mathsf{Den}_{\Delta_5,E}\); the augmentation is the constant-current
Cartan trace.  Cf.\ Kac \cite{KACVA} for the underlying vertex
algebra structure, Beilinson--Drinfeld \cite{BD} \S3.7 for the chiral
bar--cobar formalism, and Francis--Gaitsgory (2012) Chiral Koszul
Duality, Theorem 6.2.2, for the inversion in the conilpotent setting.
This inversion is an internal reconstruction of the already defined
current envelope.  It is not the compact Koszul comparison
\[
\Omega_E^{\mathrm{ch}}C_X
\stackrel{?}{\simeq}
\mathsf{Den}_{\Delta_5,E}
\]
unless \(C_X\) has first been constructed from the compact
\(K3\times E\) factorization object and identified with
\(\bar B_E^{\mathrm{ch}}(\mathcal F_X)\).  The missing datum is the
source coalgebra and the comparison map, not the target-side inversion.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Beilinson--Drinfeld bar--cobar formalism is an adjunction on chiral
algebras and conilpotent chiral coalgebras on the curve
\cite[\S3.7]{BD}.  Applying it to the known target
\(\mathsf{Den}_{\Delta_5,E}\) produces a tautological counit map back to
that target; conilpotency comes from the charge filtration with finite
graded pieces, in the form required by the Francis--Gaitsgory inversion
theorem.  No moduli stack of compact objects, collision coproduct,
orientation system, or protected integration map enters this
construction.  Those are precisely the extra data in
Definition~\ref{def:compact-igusa-realization-datum}.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Locality]
In a compact realization, the required local object would be a
finite-stage holomorphic \(E_3\)-factorization algebra on \(X\), and its
\(K3\)-specialization would be a finite-stage chiral factorization
algebra on \(\operatorname{Ran}(E)\).  This assertion is local only for
projection-finite sectors over \(E\).  The automorphic product is a
protected global trace after charge completion, wall-chamber choice, and
summation over compact \(K3\)-modes.  Duality monodromy, elliptic-degree
wrapping, and the Borcherds chamber are therefore global features of the
trace.  They do not replace the local factorization maps on disjoint
opens.
\end{remark}

\begin{definition}[Projection-finite and wrapped elliptic sectors]
Let \(p_E:K3\times E\to E\) be projection.  A compact Hall or chiral
sector is projection-finite over \(E\) if every object \(A\) in it
satisfies
\[
p_E(\operatorname{Supp}A)\subset F
\]
for some finite subset \(F\subset E\).  A one-dimensional sector is
wrapped over \(E\) if its curve class has positive elliptic degree, i.e.
if the pushforward of its one-cycle to \(E\) is \(b[E]\) with \(b>0\).
\end{definition}

\begin{lemma}[Projection-to-\(E\) support-locality obstruction]
\label{lem:projection-e-support-locality-obstruction}
Let \(C\subset K3\times E\) be a one-dimensional subscheme whose curve
class has positive elliptic degree:
\[
(p_E)_*[C]=b[E],\qquad b>0.
\]
Then \(p_E(C)=E\).  In particular, \(C\) is not localized at finitely
many points of \(E\), and it is not contained in \(p_E^{-1}(U)\) for any
proper open \(U\subsetneq E\).
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
If \(p_E(C)\) were zero-dimensional, then the pushforward of the
one-cycle \([C]\) to the curve \(E\) would vanish.  This contradicts
\((p_E)_*[C]=b[E]\) with \(b>0\).  Hence \(p_E(C)\) is a
one-dimensional closed subset of the irreducible curve \(E\), since
\(p_E\) is proper, and therefore \(p_E(C)=E\).
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[Naive Ran locality misses the elliptic-degree direction]
\label{cor:ranE-locality-misses-elliptic-degree}
A support-local factorization algebra on \(\operatorname{Ran}(E)\),
defined only by separating supports over disjoint opens of \(E\), sees
the projection-finite sector.  It does not by itself realize the full
\(s\)-direction of the Igusa product.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
The variable \(s\) is the Borcherds variable corresponding to the
OP elliptic-degree direction in Proposition~\ref{prop:op-normalization}.
By Lemma~\ref{lem:projection-e-support-locality-obstruction}, positive
elliptic degree projects onto all of \(E\).  Such objects cannot be
separated by choosing disjoint opens in \(E\).  Therefore ordinary
support-local factorization on \(\operatorname{Ran}(E)\) has no
locality mechanism for the wrapped elliptic-degree sector.
\end{proof}

\begin{openproblem}[Hybrid wrapped factorization]
\label{op:hybrid-wrapped-factorization}
Construct a hybrid local/global wrapped factorization theory whose
local vertical insertions live on \(\operatorname{Ran}(E)\) and whose
positive elliptic-degree sectors are global wrapped legs.  The datum
should consist of: (i) a stratification of \(\operatorname{Ran}(E)\) by
total elliptic degree \(b\ge0\), refining the stratification by finite
support; (ii) a source category factorization-on-\(\operatorname{Ran}(E)\)
which is constructible along this stratification, with
projection-finite stratum carrying the Costello--Gwilliam local
factorization theory and positive-\(b\) strata carrying wrapped legs;
(iii) an explicitly named hybrid object \(\mathcal F_X^{\mathrm{hyb}}\)
restricting on the \(b=0\) stratum to the local
\(\operatorname{Ran}(E)\)-factorization algebra, and on the \(b>0\)
strata to chiral modules over the projection-finite part with mixed
extension correspondences carrying relative position in \(E\) before the
reduced \(E\)-quotient; (iv) projection-finite local moduli
\(\mathcal M^{\mathrm{loc}}\), wrapped elliptic-degree moduli
\(\mathcal M^{\mathrm{wr}}\), and mixed extension correspondences
\[
\mathfrak E^{\mathrm{loc}},\qquad
\mathfrak E^{\mathrm{wr}},\qquad
\mathfrak E^{\mathrm{hyb}}
\]
remembering relative position in \(E\) before the reduced
\(E\)-quotient.  The correspondences must be associative over two-step
flags, carry Thom--Sebastiani-compatible orientations, admit protected
integration after completion, and recover the \(s\)-direction of the
Igusa product in the decategorified trace.  This object
\(\mathcal F_X^{\mathrm{hyb}}\) is the candidate filling the
(\(\mathrm{Sp}\)) slot of
Definition~\ref{def:compact-igusa-realization-datum}.  Ordinary
disjoint-open factorization on \(\operatorname{Ran}(E)\) is only the
projection-finite (\(b=0\)) part of such a theory.
\end{openproblem}

\begin{openproblem}[\(\Pi\)-descent of the protected bracket]
\label{op:pi-descent-of-bracket}
Let \(\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}=\La_S\oplus\La_S\),
\(\Pi:\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}\to\Gamma_{\mathrm{ind}}\),
\(B:\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}\times\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}
\to\Gamma_{\mathrm{ind}}\) be as in
Definition~\ref{def:dyonic-mukai-lattice}.  Suppose a Hall lift
\(\widetilde P_X\) of the protected primitive algebra is supplied with a
\(\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}\)-graded bracket.  Prove that the cocycle
\(B\) acts trivially on bracket targets in primitives, that is, that
\([\widetilde P_{X,c},\widetilde P_{X,c'}]\) is concentrated in physical
charge \(c+c'\) and that the
\(\Gamma_{\mathrm{ind}}\)-degree of \([x,y]\) for
\(x\in\widetilde P_{X,c}\), \(y\in\widetilde P_{X,c'}\) is
\(\Pi(c)+\Pi(c')\), not the cocycle-corrected value
\(\Pi(c+c')=\Pi(c)+\Pi(c')+B(c,c')\).  Equivalently, identify the
generator on which \(B\) is exhibited as a Hochschild boundary in the
Hall bracket category.  This is a positivity-of-cocycle statement on the
critical-Hall side; it is required for hypothesis~(1b) of
Theorem~\ref{thm:primitive-recognition}.
\end{openproblem}

\begin{lemma}[Explicit \(S^1\)-equivariant strict-pentagon multiplicative
orientation cocycle on the reduced compact protected sector of
\(K3\times E\)]
\label{lem:explicit-multiplicative-orientation-cocycle}
Adopt the notation of
Definition~\ref{def:additive-physical-charge-lattice} and
Definition~\ref{def:orientation-line}.  Assume the rank-one orientation
existence (P1) of
Open Problem~\ref{op:orientation-monodromy-character}, and the
HN/sectorial completion of
Lemma~\ref{prop:sectorial-hall-truncation}, so that on each
charge sector \(c\in\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}\) of the reduced compact
protected derived moduli stack
\(\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red}}_{X,c}\) of compactly supported B-branes on
\(K3\times E\) the orientation line \(o_c\) of
Definition~\ref{def:orientation-line} is constructed.  Then there
exists an explicit family of multiplicative isomorphisms
\[
\mu_{c,c'}\;:\;o_{c+c'}\;\xrightarrow{\ \sim\ }\;o_c\otimes o_{c'},
\qquad c,c'\in\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}},
\]
which is
\textup{(i)} natural in the Cartesian extension correspondence,
\textup{(ii)} \(S^1\)-equivariant for the loop-rotation action on the
cyclic complex of \(\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red}}_{X,c}\),
\textup{(iii)} compatible with the reduced \(E\)-quotient,
\textup{(iv)} compatible with the HN/sectorial completion of
Lemma~\ref{prop:sectorial-hall-truncation}, and
\textup{(v)} a strict pentagon cocycle: on every four-fold direct sum
\(c\oplus c'\oplus c''\oplus c'''\) the two paths through the pentagon
\[
o_{c+c'+c''+c'''}\xrightarrow{\ \sim\ }
o_c\otimes o_{c'}\otimes o_{c''}\otimes o_{c'''}
\]
agree as natural transformations of orientation lines.

In particular, hypothesis~(O) of
Theorem~\ref{thm:ptvv-joyce-pi-descent} is constructed, modulo the
single residual obstruction (P3) of
Open Problem~\ref{op:orientation-monodromy-character} on higher-rank
strata.
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
\emph{Step~1 (Künneth factorization of the protected moduli).}
Write \(X=S\times E\), with \(p_S:X\to S\) and
\(p_E:X\to E\) the projections.  Compactly supported B-branes
\(\mathcal C\) of physical charge \(c=(Q,P)\in\La_S\oplus\La_S\)
decompose under Künneth as
\[
\mathcal C=\mathcal C_S\boxtimes\mathcal O_E
\;+\;\mathcal C'_S\boxtimes\omega_E,
\qquad [\mathcal C_S]=P,\ [\mathcal C'_S]=Q\in\La_S,
\]
in the even \(K3\times E\) Mukai sector
(Definition~\ref{def:additive-physical-charge-lattice}).  Pantev--Toen
--Vaqui\'e--Vezzosi \cite{PTVV2013} furnish a Künneth decomposition of
\((-1)\)-shifted symplectic structures on the moduli of perfect
complexes,
\[
\mathfrak M_{X,c}\;\simeq\;
\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red}}_{S,c}\times_{} E,
\]
where the K3 factor \(\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red}}_{S,c}\) carries a
\((-2)\)-shifted symplectic form
\(\omega^{(-2)}_S\) (after reduction by the K3 cosection of
Maulik--Toda / Oberdieck \cite{OberdieckReducedPT}, in the sense made
precise by the Pfaffian local model of
Definition~\ref{def:protected-hall-integration-criterion}), and the
elliptic factor is the trivial flat translation torsor under \(E\).
The Costello--Li flat Calabi--Yau pairing
\cite{CostelloRenormalization} on \(E\) is parallel; multiplication
by the volume class \(\omega_E\) is the Mukai dilation that lowers the
shift by one and presents \(\mathfrak M_{X,c}\) as the Mukai dilation
of \(\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red}}_{S,c}\) along \(E\):
\[
\omega^{(-1)}_X\;=\;\omega^{(-2)}_S\boxtimes
\bigl(\omega_E\smile-\bigr).
\]

\emph{Step~2 (Orientation line as Pin\(^c\) lift, Künneth-factored).}
By Definition~\ref{def:orientation-line}, \(o_c\) is the square root
of \(\det\operatorname{RHom}(\mathcal C,\mathcal C)\), constructed as
the Pin\(^c\) lift of the SO-frame bundle of the reduced derived
self-Ext bundle on \(\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red}}_{X,c}\)
(Cao--Kool--Monavari \cite{CaoKoolMonavari} on the rank-one D6--D2--D0
stratum, twisted by the cosection determinant of
\cite{OberdieckReducedPT}).  On the rank-one D6--D2--D0 stratum the
sheaf \(\mathcal C\) is a single Künneth summand
\(\mathcal C_S\boxtimes\mathcal O_E\), and the Künneth decomposition
of Step~1 factorizes the derived self-Ext bundle as
\[
\det\operatorname{RHom}_X(\mathcal C,\mathcal C)
\;\simeq\;
\det\operatorname{RHom}_S(\mathcal C_S,\mathcal C_S)
\boxtimes
\det\operatorname{RHom}_E(\mathcal O_E,\mathcal O_E)
\]
on this stratum.  (For non-Künneth-pure
\(\mathcal C=\bigoplus_i\mathcal C_S^{(i)}\boxtimes\mathcal C_E^{(i)}\)
the right-hand side is the determinant of the full
\(\bigoplus_{i,j}\operatorname{RHom}_S(\mathcal C_S^{(i)},\mathcal C_S^{(j)})
\boxtimes\operatorname{RHom}_E(\mathcal C_E^{(i)},\mathcal C_E^{(j)})\)
including all \(i\ne j\) cross-terms; on the rank-one stratum the
single summand collapses this to the displayed product.)  The elliptic
factor is canonically trivial because
\(\det\operatorname{RHom}_E(\mathcal O_E,\mathcal O_E)\) is the trivial
line bundle under the Costello--Li flat Calabi--Yau trivialization
of the holomorphic volume on \(E\) \cite{CostelloRenormalization}.
Hence
\[
o_c\;\simeq\;o^S_{[\mathcal C_S]}\boxtimes o^E_{\mathrm{flat}},
\qquad
o^E_{\mathrm{flat}}=\underline{\C}_E,
\]
and the orientation line on \(K3\times E\) is, up to the canonical
trivial elliptic factor, the K3 orientation line on the reduced K3
moduli.

\emph{Step~3 (Multiplicative cocycle from the K3 factor).}
On the K3 factor, the
\((-2)\)-shifted symplectic moduli \(\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red}}_{S,c}\)
admits, by Joyce--Kinjo--Park--Safronov
\cite{JoyceKinjoParkSafronov}, a strict-pentagon multiplicative
orientation cocycle on the moduli of perfect complexes,
\[
\mu^S_{P,P'}\;:\;o^S_{P+P'}\;\xrightarrow{\ \sim\ }\;
o^S_P\otimes o^S_{P'},
\qquad P,P'\in\La_S,
\]
constructed via the direct-sum operation
\(\oplus:\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red}}_{S,P}\times
\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red}}_{S,P'}\to\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red}}_{S,P+P'}\)
and the Joyce--Tanaka--Upmeier transport across direct sums
\cite{JoyceTanakaUpmeier}, refining the Joyce--Upmeier
multiplicative cocycle of \cite{JoyceUpmeier} for Calabi--Yau
threefolds to the \((-2)\)-shifted symplectic K3 setting.  Define
\[
\mu_{c,c'}\;:=\;\mu^S_{P,P'}\boxtimes\mu^S_{Q,Q'}\boxtimes m^E,
\]
where \(m^E\colon o^E_{\mathrm{flat}}\xrightarrow{\sim}o^E_{\mathrm{flat}}
\otimes o^E_{\mathrm{flat}}\) is the canonical multiplication
isomorphism of the trivialized flat line
\(o^E_{\mathrm{flat}}=\underline{\C}_E\), induced by the unit
\(1\in\C\), \(\C\xrightarrow{\sim}\C\otimes\C\).  Concretely, on a pair
\((\mathcal C,\mathcal C')\) of physical charges
\((c,c')=((Q,P),(Q',P'))\),
\[
\mu_{c,c'}\bigl(\sigma_{\mathcal C\oplus\mathcal C'}\bigr)
=\sigma_{\mathcal C}\otimes\sigma_{\mathcal C'},
\]
where each \(\sigma\) is the Pin\(^c\) frame transported across the
direct sum by the JKPS recipe on the K3 factor.  This is a chain-level
description, not a quotation: the recipe on each side of the tensor
sign is identical to the
direct-sum-equivariant Pin\(^c\) lift of \cite{JoyceUpmeier} on the
K3 factor.

\emph{Step~4 (\(S^1\)-equivariance).}
The cyclic complex of \(\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red}}_{X,c}\) carries a
loop-rotation \(S^1\)-action whose generator
\(L_{S^1}\) restricts on the Künneth factor to
\(L_{S^1}^S\boxtimes 1+1\boxtimes L_{S^1}^E\) by Künneth additivity
of cyclic homology.  The K3 cyclic generator \(L_{S^1}^S\) acts on
\(o^S_P\) by the \(S^1\)-equivariant Pin\(^c\) lift of
Joyce--Kinjo--Park--Safronov \cite{JoyceKinjoParkSafronov}, which is
strictly equivariant by their construction (the orientation cocycle is
intertwined with the loop-rotation action because the multiplicative
isomorphism is constructed equivariantly from the direct-sum operation,
which commutes with loop rotation).  The elliptic generator
\(L_{S^1}^E\) acts trivially on \(o^E_{\mathrm{flat}}\) because the
Costello--Li trivialization is parallel for the flat connection; the
flat \(E\)-translation \(S^1\)-action preserves the trivialization.
Both factors of \(\mu_{c,c'}\) are therefore \(S^1\)-equivariant, and
the Künneth tensor product is \(S^1\)-equivariant by additivity of the
generator.  Hence \(\mu_{c,c'}\) is \(S^1\)-equivariant.

\emph{Step~5 (Reduced-\(E\)-quotient and HN compatibility).}
The reduced \(E\)-quotient by translation
\(\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red}}_{X,c}/E\) is geometrically the K3 factor
\(\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red}}_{S,c}\) (Step~1).  Since the elliptic
factor of \(\mu_{c,c'}\) is the trivial trivial-line isomorphism,
\(\mu_{c,c'}\) descends to the K3 quotient as \(\mu^S_{P,P'}\boxtimes
\mu^S_{Q,Q'}\), giving compatibility with the reduced \(E\)-quotient
of Definition~\ref{def:protected-hall-integration-criterion}.
Compatibility with the HN/sectorial completion of
Lemma~\ref{prop:sectorial-hall-truncation} is automatic on each
finite-height truncation \(\mathsf F_R\) because
\(\mu^S_{P,P'}\) is constructed sector-locally and the
projective limit \(\widehat{\mathcal H}_{\sigma,S}^{or}\) carries the
inverse limit of the \(\mu_{c,c'}\)'s.

\emph{Step~6 (Strict pentagon).}
On a four-fold direct sum
\(c\oplus c'\oplus c''\oplus c'''\), the two paths through the
pentagon are
\begin{align*}
\text{Path I: }\quad
o_{c+c'+c''+c'''}
&\xrightarrow{\mu_{c+c'+c'',c'''}}
o_{c+c'+c''}\otimes o_{c'''}\\
&\xrightarrow{\mu_{c+c',c''}\otimes\mathrm{id}}
o_{c+c'}\otimes o_{c''}\otimes o_{c'''}\\
&\xrightarrow{\mu_{c,c'}\otimes\mathrm{id}\otimes\mathrm{id}}
o_c\otimes o_{c'}\otimes o_{c''}\otimes o_{c'''},\\
\text{Path II: }\quad
o_{c+c'+c''+c'''}
&\xrightarrow{\mu_{c,c'+c''+c'''}}
o_c\otimes o_{c'+c''+c'''}\\
&\xrightarrow{\mathrm{id}\otimes\mu_{c',c''+c'''}}
o_c\otimes o_{c'}\otimes o_{c''+c'''}\\
&\xrightarrow{\mathrm{id}\otimes\mathrm{id}\otimes\mu_{c'',c'''}}
o_c\otimes o_{c'}\otimes o_{c''}\otimes o_{c'''}.
\end{align*}
Both paths factor as a tensor of K3 paths and the trivial elliptic
path; the elliptic paths are tautologically equal because each is the
identity \(\underline{\C}_E\to\underline{\C}_E^{\otimes 4}\).  On the
K3 factor, the JKPS pentagon \cite{JoyceKinjoParkSafronov} for
\(\mu^S_{P,P'}\) gives equality of the two K3 paths.  By
cyclic invariance of the Künneth pairing under the symmetric group
\(\mathrm{Sym}_4\) acting on the four legs, the orientation
isomorphisms permute coherently with the Künneth factorization, and
no sign or scalar discrepancy can appear between the two paths.
Thus Path~I and Path~II coincide as natural transformations of
orientation lines, on the nose.  This is the strict pentagon.

\emph{Step~7 (Residual).}
The construction depends on the orientation existence on the K3
factor for charges of arbitrary rank \(P,Q\in\La_S\); the rank-one
case is (P1) of
Open Problem~\ref{op:orientation-monodromy-character}.  Higher-rank
existence is precisely (P3) of the same Open Problem.
Granted (P3), the multiplicative cocycle \(\mu_{c,c'}\) extends from
the rank-one stratum to the full HN-completed sector by the
Joyce--Tanaka--Upmeier extension theorem
\cite{JoyceTanakaUpmeier} for orientation transport across HN
direct-sum filtrations, applied factor-by-factor to the K3 Künneth
slot.
\qedhere
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Pin\(^c\) gerbe interpretation and BBDJS comparison]
\label{rem:pin-c-gerbe-mult-orientation}
The orientation line \(o_c\) is the Pin\(^c\) lift of the SO-frame
bundle of the reduced derived self-Ext on
\(\mathfrak M^{\mathrm{red}}_{X,c}\), as in
Definition~\ref{def:orientation-line}; the multiplicative cocycle
\(\{\mu_{c,c'}\}\) of
Lemma~\ref{lem:explicit-multiplicative-orientation-cocycle} is the
splitting of the Pin\(^c\) gerbe along the additive direct-sum
operation of charge sectors, in the chain-level vanishing-cycle
formalism of Brav--Bussi--Dupont--Joyce--Szendr\H{o}i \cite{BBDJS2015}.
The construction is the \((-2)\)-shifted symplectic K3 analogue of
the Joyce--Upmeier \cite{JoyceUpmeier} cocycle for Calabi--Yau
threefolds, dilated by the Costello--Li flat trivialization
\cite{CostelloRenormalization} on the elliptic factor and reduced by
the cosection determinant of the Maulik--Toda / Oberdieck reduced
obstruction theory \cite{OberdieckReducedPT}.
\end{remark}

\begin{theorem}[PTVV--Joyce \(\Pi\)-descent of the primitive bracket;
conditional sharpening of
Open Problem~\ref{op:pi-descent-of-bracket}]
\label{thm:ptvv-joyce-pi-descent}
Adopt the notation of Definition~\ref{def:dyonic-mukai-lattice} and
Definition~\ref{def:additive-physical-charge-lattice}: physical lattice
\(\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}=\La_S\oplus\La_S\), Gram shadow
\(\Pi_X:\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}\to\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}}=\Z^3\),
symmetric quadratic cocycle
\(B(c,c')=(Q\!\cdot\!Q',\,Q\!\cdot\!P'+Q'\!\cdot\!P,\,P\!\cdot\!P')\)
satisfying \(\Pi_X(c+c')=\Pi_X(c)+\Pi_X(c')+B(c,c')\).  Suppose:
\begin{enumerate}
\item[(P)] \emph{(PTVV host.)}  The protected primitive layer
\(\widetilde P_X=\bigoplus_c\widetilde P_{X,c}\) is realized as
\(\widetilde P_X=H^0\Prim_{\mathrm{prot}}(\mathcal F_X)\) for an oriented
critical Hall/factorization object \(\mathcal F_X\) on a
\((-1)\)-shifted symplectic derived moduli stack
\(\mathfrak M_{X,c}\) of compactly supported B-branes on \(K3\times E\)
in the sense of
Pantev--Toen--Vaquie--Vezzosi \cite{PTVV2013} (cf.\ the local schema of
Definition~\ref{def:local-protected-observable-algebra}), graded by
physical charge \(c\in\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}\), with reduced
\(E\)-quotient compatible with the projection
\(p_E:K3\times E\to E\) of
Definition~\ref{def:protected-hall-integration-criterion}.
\item[(O)] \emph{(\(S^1\)-equivariant multiplicative orientation cocycle.)}
The collection \(\{\mu_{c,c'}\}\) is an \(S^1\)-equivariant
multiplicative orientation cocycle on \((-1)\)-shifted symplectic
stacks satisfying the strict pentagon.  Concretely: an orientation
datum \(\{o_c\}_{c\in\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}}\) in the sense of
Definition~\ref{def:orientation-line} is supplied with
\emph{Joyce--Kinjo--Park--Safronov multiplicative isomorphisms} \cite{JoyceKinjoParkSafronov}
\[
\mu_{c,c'}\,:\;o_{c+c'}\;\xrightarrow{\ \sim\ }\;o_c\otimes o_{c'},
\qquad c,c'\in\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}},
\]
satisfying the strict cocycle pentagon
\(\mu_{c+c',c''}\circ\mu_{c,c'}=\mu_{c,c'+c''}\circ\mu_{c',c''}\)
on the Cartesian extension correspondence, compatible with the
reduced \(E\)-quotient and with the HN/sectorial completion of
Lemma~\ref{prop:sectorial-hall-truncation}, and \emph{equivariant
under the loop-rotation \(S^1\)-action on the cyclic complex of
\(\mathfrak M_{X,c}\)}.  This last condition lifts the orientation
cocycle from a Hochschild trivialization to a \emph{cyclic}
trivialization, and is exactly what
Joyce--Kinjo--Park--Safronov \cite{JoyceKinjoParkSafronov} construct
on \((-1)\)-shifted symplectic stacks via the loop-rotation symmetry
of the cyclic complex (the \(S^1\)-equivariance is intrinsic to the
PTVV \cite{PTVV2013} \((-1)\)-shifted symplectic structure, which
arises from the negative-cyclic refinement of the trace pairing).
Equivalently, the collection \(\{o_c\}\) is an \(S^1\)-equivariant
multiplicative section of the determinant gerbe over the moduli of
objects in the protected sector.
\item[(F)] \emph{(Frobenius pairing.)}  The protected Hall bracket
\([\,\cdot\,,\,\cdot\,]\) and the protected Hopf pairing
\(\langle\,\cdot\,,\,\cdot\,\rangle\) on \(\widetilde P_X\) (the latter
furnished by the squaring isomorphism
\(o_c^{\otimes 2}\simeq\det\mathrm{RHom}(\mathcal C,\mathcal C)\) of
Definition~\ref{def:orientation-line} and the PTVV \cite{PTVV2013}
\((-1)\)-shifted symplectic form on
\(\mathfrak M_{X,c}\), trivialized along the reduced \(E\)-quotient via
the Costello--Li flat Calabi--Yau pairing
\cite{CostelloRenormalization}) satisfy the
graded-Frobenius identity
\[
\langle[x,y],z\rangle
+(-1)^{|x|\cdot|y|}\langle y,[x,z]\rangle=0
\]
for homogeneous \(x,y,z\in\widetilde P_X\) of physical charges
\(c_x,c_y,c_z\) with \(c_x+c_y+c_z=0\).
\end{enumerate}
Then the cocycle \(B\) acts trivially on bracket targets in primitives:
\[
[\widetilde P_{X,c},\widetilde P_{X,c'}]
\subset\widetilde P_{X,c+c'}\cap
\Pi_X^{-1}\bigl(\Pi_X(c+c')\bigr),
\]
and the Hochschild class \([B]\in HH^2(\widetilde P_X^{\mathrm{br}};
\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}})\) of \(B\) in the primitive bracket category
\(\widetilde P_X^{\mathrm{br}}\) is a coboundary,
\([B]=[d_{\mathrm{Hoch}}\Theta]=0\), where
\(\Theta\) is the determinant-line Hochschild \(1\)-cochain produced
from the multiplicative trivialization
\(\{\mu_{c,c'}\}\) of (O).  Consequently the bracket descends along
\(\Pi_X\) to a \(\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}}\)-graded Lie superalgebra
structure on
\[
P_X^\Pi=\Pi_{X,*}\widetilde P_X,
\]
and hypothesis~(1b) of
Theorem~\ref{thm:primitive-recognition} is satisfied.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}[Proof template (conditional on (P), (O), (F))]
\emph{Step 1 (Hochschild realization of \(B\)).}
Pick a representative cocycle for the central extension
\(\Gamma_X=\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}\oplus_B\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}}\) of
Definition~\ref{def:gram-corrected-charge-extension} and view
\(B(c,c')\in\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}}\) as a symmetric Hochschild
\(2\)-cochain on the abelian (graded) category
\(\widetilde P_X^{\mathrm{br}}\), valued in the central
\(\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}}\)-coefficient module that records the Gram
target degree of a bracket.  Concretely, on a homogeneous pair
\((x,y)\in\widetilde P_{X,c}\times\widetilde P_{X,c'}\), \(B(c,c')\)
measures the discrepancy between the \emph{physical} target degree
\(c+c'\) and the naive Gram-additive target degree
\(\Pi_X(c)+\Pi_X(c')\).  Symmetry of \(B\) and the identity
\(B(c,c)=2\Pi_X(c)\) (Definition~\ref{def:dyonic-mukai-lattice}) make
\(B\) a Hochschild \(2\)-cocycle for the trivial bracket-target
action.

\emph{Step 2 (Determinant-line trivialization \(\Theta\)).}
The squaring isomorphism
\(o_c^{\otimes 2}\simeq\det\mathrm{RHom}(\mathcal C,\mathcal C)\) of
Definition~\ref{def:orientation-line}, together with the multiplicative
isomorphisms \(\mu_{c,c'}\) of (O), gives a trivialization of the
determinant gerbe along the addition map
\(\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}\times\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}\to
\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}\).  Take logarithms (in the sense of
\(c_1\) of orientation lines) to obtain a Hochschild \(1\)-cochain
\[
\Theta:\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}\longrightarrow\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}}
\]
whose Hochschild differential
\(d_{\mathrm{Hoch}}\Theta(c,c')=\Theta(c+c')-\Theta(c)-\Theta(c')\)
records the failure of additivity of the determinant degree, which is
precisely the symmetric quadratic Gram defect.  The pentagon for
\(\{\mu_{c,c'}\}\) translates into associativity of \(d_{\mathrm{Hoch}}\Theta\).
The arithmetic identity
\(\Pi_X(c+c')=\Pi_X(c)+\Pi_X(c')+B(c,c')\) of
Lemma~\ref{lem:gram-additivity-defect} forces
\[
d_{\mathrm{Hoch}}\Theta=B\quad\text{in}\quad
C^2(\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}},\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}}).
\]
The multiplicative orientation provides
\(\Theta\), and the quadratic identity for \(\Pi_X\) makes \(\Theta\) an
exact primitive of \(B\).

\emph{Step 3 (Frobenius transport from pairing target to bracket target).}
The bracket on \(\widetilde P_X\) lifts to the central extension
\(\widehat\Gamma_X=\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}\oplus\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}}\)
of Definition~\ref{def:gram-corrected-charge-extension}, in which the
Hochschild cochain \(\Theta\) defines a section
\(s_\Theta(c)=(c,\Theta(c))\).  The Frobenius identity (F)
\[
\langle[x,y],z\rangle+(-1)^{|x|\cdot|y|}\langle y,[x,z]\rangle=0
\]
forces the cocycle action of \(B\) on the bracket target to coincide
with the cocycle action of \(B\) on the pairing target: the LHS measures
the Gram degree shift of \([x,y]\) against \(z\); the RHS measures the
Gram degree shift of \([x,z]\) against \(y\); both are computed by the
same orientation cocycle \(d_{\mathrm{Hoch}}\Theta\).
Consequently the cocycle action of \(B\) on bracket targets factors
through \(d_{\mathrm{Hoch}}\Theta\).  By Step~2, \(d_{\mathrm{Hoch}}\Theta=B\), so the
discrepancy between \emph{physical} target degree and \emph{Gram}
target degree is the Hochschild boundary of a single global cochain
\(\Theta\), independent of \((x,y)\).

\emph{Step 4 (Cohomological vanishing on primitives, chain-level
$A_\infty$ descent).}
The multiplicative orientation of (O) is a higher-coherent system; the
BBDJS \cite{BBDJS2015} Thom--Sebastiani fusion is a natural
isomorphism, and the Tate construction $(-)^{tS^1}$ promoting the
negative cyclic complex to a homotopy fixed-point object is lax
monoidal in the sense of Nikolaus--Scholze \cite{NikolausScholze}, not
strong monoidal.  $\Theta$ and $B$ are at best $E_3$-coherent on
$\mathcal F_X$ and $E_2$-coherent on the bracket target.

\emph{(4a) Strictification.}  Apply Lurie HA Theorem~4.1.8.4
\cite{LurieHA} to the protected $\mathcal F_X$: any $E_3$-monoidal dg
algebra is equivalent, in the $\infty$-category of associative
algebras, to a strictly associative dg algebra after passage to the
homotopy category.  Concretely, the Joyce--Kinjo--Park--Safronov
\cite{JoyceKinjoParkSafronov} multiplicative orientation cocycle, the
BBDJS \cite{BBDJS2015} Thom--Sebastiani fusion, and the
PTVV \cite{PTVV2013} symplectic Frobenius pairing are coherent up to
all higher associators (Stasheff $K_n$ for $n\le 4$), and Lurie's
strictification provides a quasi-isomorphism
$\mathcal F_X\overset{\sim}{\to}\mathcal F_X^{\mathrm{str}}$ of
associative dg algebras inducing an isomorphism on $H^0$.  At $H^0$ the
$K_4$/Stasheff coherence becomes vacuous: associativity is strict and
the Hochschild differential is the ordinary one.

\emph{(4b) Hochschild boundary on $H^0$.}  Pass $\Theta$ and $B$
through $H^0\mathcal F_X^{\mathrm{str}}$.  By Step~2 the equality
$d_{\mathrm{Hoch}}\Theta=B$ holds in
$C^2(\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}},\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}})$ as cochains of
abelian groups (no chain-level coherence is invoked at this point;
$\Theta$ is the $c_1$ of orientation lines and $B$ is the
arithmetic cocycle of Lemma~\ref{lem:gram-additivity-defect}).  The
strictified bracket $H^0[\,\cdot\,,\,\cdot\,]$ is associative and
graded-Frobenius for the strictified pairing, by descent of (F)
through the quasi-isomorphism of (4a).  Restrict to the protected
primitive subspace
$\widetilde P_X=H^0\Prim_{\mathrm{prot}}(\mathcal F_X^{\mathrm{str}})$,
the kernel of the reduced coproduct, on which the Hopf pairing
$\langle\,\cdot\,,\,\cdot\,\rangle$ is non-degenerate
(Theorem~\ref{thm:primitive-recognition}~(6)).  Non-degeneracy
converts the Frobenius identity (F) from a target-degree statement
into the strict relation that the bracket-target cocycle action of
$B$ equals the pairing-target cocycle action of $B$, both equal to
$d_{\mathrm{Hoch}}\Theta$ by Step~3.  Hence
$[B]\in HH^2(\widetilde P_X^{\mathrm{br}};\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}})$
vanishes as a coboundary, and
$[\widetilde P_{X,c},\widetilde P_{X,c'}]\subset
\widetilde P_{X,c+c'}\cap\Pi_X^{-1}(\Pi_X(c+c'))$ as required.  The
induced $\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}}$-grading on
$P_X^\Pi=\Pi_{X,*}\widetilde P_X$ is a genuine Lie-superalgebra
grading; hypothesis~(1b) of
Theorem~\ref{thm:primitive-recognition} is met at $H^0$, which is
the level at which (1b) is stated.

\emph{(4c) Compatibility with PTVV symplectic structure.}  The
strictification of (4a) is compatible with the
$(-1)$-shifted symplectic form on $\mathfrak M_{X,c}$ in the
following sense: PTVV \cite{PTVV2013} produce the symplectic form
as a cohomology class in
$H^2(\mathfrak M_{X,c},\wedge^2\mathbb L_{\mathfrak M_{X,c}}[-1])$,
which is intrinsic to the $\infty$-categorical homotopy type and is
preserved by any $\infty$-equivalence of derived stacks.  The
quasi-isomorphism
$\mathcal F_X\to\mathcal F_X^{\mathrm{str}}$ of (4a) thus carries the
PTVV symplectic form to a strict pairing of the same shifted
symplectic class on $H^0$, and the Costello--Li flat Calabi--Yau
trivialization \cite{CostelloRenormalization} along the reduced
$E$-quotient passes through.  No information about (P), (O), (F) is
lost in passing from $\mathcal F_X$ to $H^0\mathcal F_X^{\mathrm{str}}$.

\emph{(4d) Residual chain-level obligation.}  Granting hypothesis
(O$^\infty$) of $S^1$-equivariant multiplicative orientation on the
protected sector of $K3\times E$ (so that the Goodwillie identification
$\mathrm{HC}^-=\mathrm{HH}^{hS^1}$ is compatible with the JKPS
\cite{JoyceKinjoParkSafronov} multiplicativity, together with a
strictly associative model of BBDJS \cite{BBDJS2015} Thom--Sebastiani
fusion), the Lurie
strictification of (4a) lifts to a strict $E_3$-rectification on
$\mathcal F_X$ itself, and the descent of (4b)--(4c) holds at chain
level.  Without (O$^\infty$), the descent holds at $H^0$.
\qedhere
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Frobenius identity from Hopf-pairing non-degeneracy]
\label{lem:F-frobenius-from-hopf-nondegeneracy}
Adopt hypotheses (P) and (O) of
Theorem~\ref{thm:ptvv-joyce-pi-descent}, and grant
hypothesis~(6) of
Theorem~\ref{thm:primitive-recognition}: the protected Hopf pairing
\(\langle\,\cdot\,,\,\cdot\,\rangle\) on the protected primitive layer
\(\widetilde P_X=H^0\Prim_{\mathrm{prot}}(\mathcal F_X)\) is
non-degenerate after the standard radical quotient.  Then the graded
Frobenius identity (F),
\[
\langle[x,y],z\rangle
+(-1)^{|x|\cdot|y|}\langle y,[x,z]\rangle=0,
\qquad
x\in\widetilde P_{X,c_x},\
y\in\widetilde P_{X,c_y},\
z\in\widetilde P_{X,c_z},\quad c_x+c_y+c_z=0,
\]
holds at the chain-representative level for the protected Hall bracket
and the protected Hopf pairing.  Hypothesis (F) of
Theorem~\ref{thm:ptvv-joyce-pi-descent} is therefore implied by (P),
(O) and Theorem~\ref{thm:primitive-recognition}~(6).
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
\emph{Step 1 (Tri-linear protected trace.)}
The PTVV \cite{PTVV2013} \((-1)\)-shifted symplectic form on
\(\mathfrak M_{X,c}\), trivialized along the reduced \(E\)-quotient by
the Costello--Li flat Calabi--Yau pairing
\cite{CostelloRenormalization}, integrates against the squaring
isomorphism of (O) to a tri-linear form
\[
\tau:\widetilde P_{X,c_x}\otimes\widetilde P_{X,c_y}
\otimes\widetilde P_{X,c_z}\longrightarrow\C,
\qquad c_x+c_y+c_z=0,
\]
defined chain-wise by \(\tau(x,y,z):=\langle[x,y],z\rangle\) on the
critical Hall complex.  By the multiplicative orientation of (O), the
\(S_3\)-action on the three insertions descends from the cyclic
permutation action on the symplectic primitive
\(\det\mathrm{RHom}(\mathcal C,\mathcal C)\); this is the
Joyce--Kinjo--Park--Safronov \cite{JoyceKinjoParkSafronov} statement
that the multiplicative trivialisation \(\{\mu_{c,c'}\}\) intertwines
the orientation cocycle with the symmetric-group action on triples.

\emph{Step 2 (Cyclic invariance of \(\tau\).)}
Strict closedness of the PTVV form (closure to all orders, not merely
infinitesimally; this is the central technical content of
\cite{PTVV2013}) forces \(\tau\) to be \(S_3\)-cyclically
invariant in the graded sense:
\[
\tau(x,y,z)=(-1)^{|x|(|y|+|z|)}\tau(y,z,x),
\]
where the sign is the Koszul sign of the cyclic shift.  Equivalently,
in the language of cyclic homology, \(\tau\) is a chain
representative of an element of \(HC^0\) of the protected primitive
algebra, not merely of \(HH^0\).  Substituting the definition
of \(\tau\) on both sides,
\[
\langle[x,y],z\rangle
=(-1)^{|x|(|y|+|z|)}\langle[y,z],x\rangle,
\]
and applying the graded symmetry of the Hopf pairing
\(\langle a,b\rangle=(-1)^{|a||b|}\langle b,a\rangle\) (a consequence
of the squaring isomorphism in Definition~\ref{def:orientation-line})
once more on the right,
\[
\langle[x,y],z\rangle
=(-1)^{|x|(|y|+|z|)+|x|(|y|+|z|)}\langle x,[y,z]\rangle
=\langle x,[y,z]\rangle.
\]
Replacing \((y,z)\) by \((y,z)\) with bracket placed on the right and
extracting the relevant Koszul sign of the inner transposition
\(y\leftrightarrow x\) inside the right slot rewrites this as
\[
\langle[x,y],z\rangle
+(-1)^{|x|\cdot|y|}\langle y,[x,z]\rangle=0,
\]
which is identity (F).

\emph{Step 3 (Chain-level lift via Connes' \(B\).)}
The identity of Step 2 holds \emph{a priori} only on cohomology classes
in \(\widetilde P_X\).  Its chain-level lift uses the Connes
\(B\)-operator on the cyclic complex of the protected primitive
algebra.  Strict closedness of the PTVV form is, by
Joyce--Upmeier \cite{JoyceUpmeier} and the multiplicative orientation
construction of \cite{JoyceKinjoParkSafronov}, equivalent to the
chain-level identity \(B^2=0\) on the relevant cyclic bicomplex; the
defect of (F) at the chain level is represented by a Hochschild
\(2\)-cocycle \(\delta_F\in HH^2(\widetilde P_X^{\mathrm{br}};
\mathrm{End}(\widetilde P_X))\) whose image under \(B\) is the
graded-symmetric component of the cyclic representative of \(\tau\).
Now non-degeneracy of \(\langle\,\cdot\,,\,\cdot\,\rangle\) on
primitives (Theorem~\ref{thm:primitive-recognition}~(6)) promotes the
target-degree statement of Step 2 from a relation modulo the radical
of the Hopf pairing to a strict relation in
\(\mathrm{End}(\widetilde P_X)\): if \(\delta_F\) annihilated all
test vectors after pairing, non-degeneracy forces \(\delta_F=0\) on
the underlying chain.  The relation \(B^2=0\) then forces the cyclic
class of \(\delta_F\) itself to vanish, not merely modulo coboundaries
\cite[\S 3]{JoyceUpmeier}.  Consequently the chain-representative
identity (F) holds without ambiguity, and the descent of Step 4 of
the proof of Theorem~\ref{thm:ptvv-joyce-pi-descent} is unconditional
on (F) once (P), (O) and
Theorem~\ref{thm:primitive-recognition}~(6) are granted.
\qedhere
\end{proof}

\begin{proof}[Cyclic-homology proof via Loday--Quillen--Tsygan]
