Granted (P) alone, transport the cocycle to the cyclic complex
of the protected Hall sector and use strict cyclic invariance of the
Connes trace.

\smallskip\emph{Step 1\(^\prime\) (Bar resolution and cyclic complex).}
Write \(A_X^{\mathrm{prot}}\) for the chain-level dg associative algebra
underlying the protected Hall sector \(\widetilde P_X\) of (P);
concretely, on a derived chart \(\Spec R\) of \(\mathfrak M_{X,c}\),
\(A_X^{\mathrm{prot}}\) is the commutative dg algebra of homotopical
endomorphisms produced by the \((-1)\)-shifted symplectic structure.
Form the bar resolution \(\operatorname{Bar}_*(A_X^{\mathrm{prot}})\) and the
mixed complex \((C_*(A_X^{\mathrm{prot}}),b,B_{\mathrm{C}})\) of Connes; here
\(b\) is the Hochschild boundary and \(B_{\mathrm{C}}\) is the Connes
\(B\)-operator with \(B_{\mathrm{C}}^2=0\) and
\([b,B_{\mathrm{C}}]+B_{\mathrm{C}}\,b=0\) on the nose
\cite{ConnesNCG}, \cite{LodayCyclicHomology}.  (The subscript
\({\mathrm{C}}\) distinguishes the Connes operator from the
gerbe-class cocycle \(B\colon\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}\times\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}
\to\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}}\) of
Definition~\ref{def:dyonic-mukai-lattice}.)  Cyclic homology is
\(HC_*(A_X^{\mathrm{prot}})=H_*(C_*(A_X^{\mathrm{prot}}),b+u B)\) with
\(u\) of degree \(-2\); the periodic completion is
\(HP_*(A_X^{\mathrm{prot}})\).  The \((-1)\)-shifted symplectic form
of (P) is recorded in this language as a cyclic class
\(\varpi_X\in HC_2(A_X^{\mathrm{prot}})\), the Calabi--Yau volume of
PTVV \cite{PTVV2013}; this is the strict chain-level avatar of the
Costello--Li flat CY pairing in the Frobenius hypothesis (F) of the
first proof.  (The notation \(\varpi_X\) is reserved for this cyclic
class to avoid collision with the Weyl vector
\(\rho\in\La^{2,1}_{II}\otimes\Q\) of the denominator algebra section.)

\smallskip\emph{Step 2\(^\prime\) (Chain-level cocycle \(B_{\mathrm{ch}}\)).}
On homogeneous classes \(c,c'\in\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}\), define the
chain-level cocycle
\[
B_{\mathrm{ch}}(c,c')\;:=\;\operatorname{tr}_{HC}\!\bigl(c\cdot c'\cdot\varpi_X\;-\;
c'\cdot c\cdot\varpi_X\bigr)\;\in\;HC_2(A_X^{\mathrm{prot}}),
\]
where \(\operatorname{tr}_{HC}\) is the Connes cyclic trace and the products are the
Hall convolution on \(\widetilde P_X\) lifted to \(C_*\).  Cyclic
invariance of \(\operatorname{tr}_{HC}\) is strict on \(C_*\): the symbol
\(c\cdot c'\cdot\varpi_X\) and its cyclic permutation
\(\varpi_X\cdot c\cdot c'\) coincide as elements of the cyclic complex
because Connes' \(B\)-operator is strictly squared-zero \cite[\S2.5]{LodayCyclicHomology}.
Two consequences are immediate:
\begin{enumerate}
\item[(\(\alpha\))] symmetry, \(B_{\mathrm{ch}}(c,c')=B_{\mathrm{ch}}(c',c)\),
holds on the nose by interchanging the two terms;
\item[(\(\beta\))] strict closedness, \((b+uB_{\mathrm{C}}) B_{\mathrm{ch}}=0\),
follows from cyclic invariance and the Calabi--Yau identity
\(b\varpi_X=0=B_{\mathrm{C}}\varpi_X\) which characterises a class in \(HC_2\).
\end{enumerate}
The image of \(B_{\mathrm{ch}}\) in
\(HC^2_{\mathrm{strict}}(A_X^{\mathrm{prot}};\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}})\)
is the strict, chain-level lift of the Hochschild class \([B]\) of
the first proof; the comparison map
\(HC^2_{\mathrm{strict}}\to HH^2\) of Loday--Quillen--Tsygan
\cite{LodayQuillen1984}, \cite{Tsygan1983} sends
\([B_{\mathrm{ch}}]\) to \([B]\).

\smallskip\emph{Step 3\(^\prime\) (Strict associativity from cyclic
invariance).}  Equip \(\operatorname{Bar}_*(\widehat\Gamma_X)\) with the canonical
A\(_\infty\) structure transferred from the bar resolution of
\(A_X^{\mathrm{prot}}\) along the augmentation
\(A_X^{\mathrm{prot}}\twoheadrightarrow\widehat\Gamma_X\) of
Definition~\ref{def:gram-corrected-charge-extension}.  The Stasheff
obstruction class \(K_4\in C^4_{\mathrm{Hoch}}(\widehat\Gamma_X)\) for
collapse of the A\(_\infty\) structure to a strict associative dg
algebra is computed as the homotopy of the Hochschild cocycle identity
for \(B_{\mathrm{ch}}\); cyclic invariance (\(\alpha\)) and strict
closedness (\(\beta\)) of Step~2\(^\prime\) reduce \(K_4\) to a
quadrilinear expression in \(B_{\mathrm{C}}\) applied to
\(\varpi_X\), which vanishes by \(B^2=0\).  Hence
\(\operatorname{Bar}_*(\widehat\Gamma_X)\) collapses to a strictly associative dg
monoid in the cyclic-homology category, equivalently \(\widehat\Gamma_X\)
is strictly associative on the nose.  Restricted to primitives, the
class
\([B_{\mathrm{ch}}]\in HC^2_{\mathrm{strict}}\!\bigl(\widetilde
P_X^{\mathrm{br}};\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}}\bigr)\) is then a strict
coboundary of the Connes contraction
\(\iota_{\varpi_X}:HC_*\to HC_{*-2}\) applied to \(\Pi_X\): explicitly,
\(\iota_{\varpi_X}\Pi_X\) is the chain-level avatar of the Hochschild
\(1\)-cochain \(\Theta\) of the first proof, and
\((b+uB_{\mathrm{C}})(\iota_{\varpi_X}\Pi_X)=B_{\mathrm{ch}}\) on the nose.

\smallskip\emph{Step 4\(^\prime\) (Compatibility with PTVV--Joyce).}
The two routes give the same group \(\Gamma_X\): the comparison
\(HC^2_{\mathrm{strict}}\to HH^2\) sends
\([B_{\mathrm{ch}}]\mapsto[B]\) and \(\iota_{\varpi_X}\Pi_X\mapsto\Theta\),
and the Joyce--Kinjo--Park--Safronov multiplicative isomorphism
\(\mu_{c,c'}\) of (O) is, in this language, the cyclic-homology lift
to the determinant gerbe of the chain-level identity
\((b+uB_{\mathrm{C}})(\iota_{\varpi_X}\Pi_X)=B_{\mathrm{ch}}\).  Equivalently, the
Kapustin--Rozansky / Kontsevich--Soibelman correspondence between
shifted symplectic geometry and cyclic homology
\cite{KSCoHA}, refined by Davison--Meinhardt
\cite{DavisonMeinhardtCoHA} and the modern Joyce--Kinjo--Park--Safronov
formulation \cite{JoyceKinjoParkSafronov}, identifies the cyclic
pairing \(\varpi_X\) with the PTVV symplectic form and the Connes trace
with the integrated Frobenius pairing of (F).  Step~4 of the first
proof and Step~3\(^\prime\) here certify the same vanishing
\([B]=0\) on primitives; the descended bracket on
\(P_X^\Pi=\Pi_{X,*}\widetilde P_X\) is independent of the route, and
hypothesis~(1b) of Theorem~\ref{thm:primitive-recognition} holds.
\qedhere
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Comparison of the two proofs]
\label{rem:cyclic-vs-orientation-step4}
\([B]=[B_{\mathrm{ch}}]\) under the Loday--Quillen--Tsygan comparison
\(HC^*_{\mathrm{strict}}\to HH^*\) of \cite{LodayQuillen1984},
\cite{Tsygan1983}, \cite[\S2]{LodayCyclicHomology}, with witnessing
cochains \(\Theta\) (PTVV--Joyce) and
\(\iota_{\varpi_X}\Pi_X\) (cyclic-homology).
\end{remark}

The residual content of Theorem~\ref{thm:ptvv-joyce-pi-descent}
reduces to construction of the PTVV host (P) on the reduced compact
protected sector of \(K3\times E\) together with closure of the
rank-extension (P3) of
Open Problem~\ref{op:orientation-monodromy-character}; (F) is derived
from (P)+(O) by
Lemma~\ref{lem:F-frobenius-from-hopf-nondegeneracy}, and (O) is
constructed by
Lemma~\ref{lem:explicit-multiplicative-orientation-cocycle}.


\begin{lemma}[Graded Frobenius identity from CY-3 Serre functor]
\label{lem:F-frobenius-from-cy-serre}
Suppose that the protected observable algebra
\(\mathcal A_X\) of
Definition~\ref{def:local-protected-observable-algebra}, after the
reduced \(E\)-quotient and the Costello--Li flat trivialization
\cite{CostelloRenormalization} along the elliptic factor, is realized
as a Calabi--Yau \(A_\infty\)-category of dimension \(d=3\),
i.e.~it carries a Serre functor \(S\simeq[3]\) and a
non-degenerate cyclically invariant pairing
\[
\langle\,\cdot\,,\,\cdot\,\rangle_S
:\Hom_{\mathcal A_X}(X,Y)\otimes
\Hom_{\mathcal A_X}(Y,X[3])\longrightarrow k,
\]
in the sense of Kontsevich--Soibelman \cite{KSCoHA} (cyclic
\(A_\infty\)-structure) and PTVV
\cite{PTVV2013}/BBDJS \cite{BBDJS2015} (orientation data realising the
shift \([3]\) on the moduli of objects of \(\mathcal A_X\)).  Let
\(\widetilde P_X\subset H_*(\mathcal A_X)\) be the protected primitive
subspace, equipped with the Hall bracket \([\,\cdot\,,\,\cdot\,]\) and
the Hopf pairing \(\langle\,\cdot\,,\,\cdot\,\rangle\) of
Theorem~\ref{thm:primitive-recognition}.  Then the graded Frobenius
identity holds:
\[
\langle[x,y],z\rangle
+(-1)^{|x|\cdot|y|}\langle y,[x,z]\rangle=0,
\qquad x,y,z\in\widetilde P_X\ \mathrm{homogeneous},
\]
i.e.~hypothesis (F) of Theorem~\ref{thm:ptvv-joyce-pi-descent} is met.
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
\emph{Step 1 (Serre pairing and cyclic trace).}
A CY-\(d\) \(A_\infty\)-category \(\mathcal A_X\) is, by
\cite{KSCoHA} (\S~10), an \(A_\infty\)-category equipped with a
quasi-isomorphism \(S\xrightarrow{\sim}[d]\) of bimodules and a
non-degenerate cyclically symmetric pairing
\(\langle\,\cdot\,,\,\cdot\,\rangle_S\) on
\(\Hom_{\mathcal A_X}(-,-)\), of total degree \(-d\).  Equivalently,
there is a chain-level cyclic trace
\(\tr_S:\Hom_{\mathcal A_X}(X,X)\to k[-d]\) satisfying
\(\tr_S(f\circ g)=(-1)^{|f|\cdot|g|}\tr_S(g\circ f)\) for composable
homogeneous \(f,g\) (loc.~cit., Lemma~10.2.4).  PTVV
\cite{PTVV2013} produce the underlying \((-d)\)-shifted symplectic
form on \(\mathfrak M_{X,c}\); BBDJS \cite{BBDJS2015} extend the
orientation/d-critical datum that realises \(S\simeq[d]\) at chain
level on the perfect-complex moduli.  Costello--Li
\cite{CostelloRenormalization} flat trivialization along the elliptic
factor reduces \(d=4\) to \(d=3\), so the discussion takes \(d=3\) and the
identification \(\langle x,y\rangle=\tr_S(x\cdot y)\), where
\(\cdot\) is the cup product on the protected primitive subspace.

\emph{Step 2 (Frobenius from cyclic invariance).}
Specialise to homogeneous primitives \(x,y,z\in\widetilde P_X\) and
expand the Hall bracket as the graded commutator
\([x,y]=x\cdot y-(-1)^{|x|\cdot|y|}y\cdot x\) (the bracket on
primitives in a connected graded Hopf algebra is the antisymmetrised
product, by Theorem~\ref{thm:primitive-recognition}~(5)).  Then
\begin{align*}
\langle[x,y],z\rangle
&=\tr_S\bigl((x\cdot y-(-1)^{|x|\cdot|y|}y\cdot x)\cdot z\bigr)\\
&=\tr_S(x\cdot y\cdot z)-(-1)^{|x|\cdot|y|}\tr_S(y\cdot x\cdot z).
\end{align*}
Cyclic invariance of \(\tr_S\) applied to the second term gives
\(\tr_S(y\cdot x\cdot z)=(-1)^{|y|\cdot(|x|+|z|)}\tr_S(x\cdot z\cdot y)\),
and applied to the first gives
\(\tr_S(x\cdot y\cdot z)=(-1)^{|x|\cdot(|y|+|z|)}\tr_S(y\cdot z\cdot x)\).
Substituting and re-collecting,
\[
\langle[x,y],z\rangle=
-(-1)^{|x|\cdot|y|}\tr_S\bigl(y\cdot(x\cdot z-(-1)^{|x|\cdot|z|}z\cdot x)\bigr)
=-(-1)^{|x|\cdot|y|}\langle y,[x,z]\rangle,
\]
which is (F).

\emph{Step 3 (Chain-level lift).}
The cyclic trace \(\tr_S\) is a strict invariant on the
\(A_\infty\)-homotopy category by \cite{KSCoHA}, \S~10.2; on
\(d\)-critical thickenings it lifts to perfect-complex chain level by
\cite{BBDJS2015} (the cyclic structure on the vanishing-cycle dg
algebra) and PTVV \cite{PTVV2013} (the shifted symplectic form
descends to the cotangent complex of \(\mathfrak M_{X,c}\)).  The
identity of Step~2 therefore holds at chain level, hence on the
protected primitive subspace \(\widetilde P_X\).
\qedhere
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}
Lemma~\ref{lem:F-frobenius-from-cy-serre} derives (F) from the
CY-\(3\) Serre functor of \(\mathcal A_X\), parallel to the derivation
through the squaring isomorphism
\(o_c^{\otimes 2}\simeq\det\mathrm{RHom}(\mathcal C,\mathcal C)\) of
Definition~\ref{def:orientation-line} and the Hopf pairing of
Theorem~\ref{thm:primitive-recognition}~(6).  Both derivations meet at
\(\langle\,\cdot\,,\,\cdot\,\rangle=\tr_S(\,\cdot\,\cdot\,\cdot\,)\), the
BBDJS \cite{BBDJS2015} cyclic upgrade of the PTVV
\cite{PTVV2013} \((-1)\)-shifted symplectic form, and produce the same
sign convention \((-1)^{|x|\cdot|y|}\) on the Gram degree
\(c_x+c_y+c_z=0\).
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Unitarity]
This paper uses the protected index, the virtual determinant, and
the Borcherds denominator algebra.  A holomorphic \(E_3\)-factorization
algebra in cochains is part of the open compact realization datum, not a
positive Hilbert-space construction already in hand.  Negative
coefficients \(f(nm,l)\) record an odd excess in a protected supertrace
or in a \(K_0\)-representative; actual parity dimensions require an
additional Hilbert-space or denominator-algebra parity datum.  If the
untwisted compactification is unitary, the statement that survives the
twist is right-moving cohomology, protected integration, and the signed
index.  Reflection positivity is not a hypothesis of the Borcherds
denominator theorem.
\end{remark}

\begin{lemma}[Cyclotomic-spectrum construction of the multiplicative
orientation cocycle; alternative source for hypothesis (O) of
Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:ptvv-joyce-pi-descent}}]
\label{lem:cyclotomic-multiplicative-orientation}
Let \(\mathcal F_X\) be the protected observable algebra of
Definition~\textup{\ref{def:local-protected-observable-algebra}},
graded by physical charge \(c\in\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}\), and let
\(\{o_c\}_{c\in\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}}\) be the orientation lines of
Definition~\textup{\ref{def:orientation-line}}.  Suppose:
\begin{enumerate}
\item[\textup{(C1)}] \emph{(Cyclotomic host.)} Each charged sector
\(\mathcal F_{X,c}\) is realised as a connective cyclotomic spectrum
in the sense of Nikolaus--Scholze \cite{NikolausScholze}; the
\(p\)-typical cyclotomic structure map
\(\varphi_p:\mathcal F_{X,c}\to(\mathcal F_{X,c})^{tC_p}\) is the
Frobenius inherited from the chiral product on
\(\operatorname{Ran}(E)\).  Equivalently, the underlying spectrum
\(HH(\mathcal F_{X,c})\) carries the natural \(S^1\)-action by the
Connes operator \(B\) of Goodwillie \cite{Goodwillie1985}, with
genuine \(S^1\)-fixed points
\(HC^-(\mathcal F_{X,c}):=HH(\mathcal F_{X,c})^{hS^1}\).
\item[\textup{(C2)}] \emph{(Determinant track.)} The orientation line
\(o_c\) lifts to a unit
\(\widehat o_c\in\pi_0HC^-(\mathcal F_{X,c})\) representing the
graded determinant
\(\det\mathrm{RHom}(\mathcal C,\mathcal C)^{1/2}\) of
Definition~\textup{\ref{def:orientation-line}} in the \(S^1\)-equivariant
periodic Picard groupoid, in the sense of
Joyce--Kinjo--Park--Safronov \cite{JoyceKinjoParkSafronov}.
\item[\textup{(C3)}] \emph{(Strict tensor compatibility.)} The
external product on \(\{\mathcal F_{X,c}\}\) is symmetric monoidal as
a map of cyclotomic spectra,
\(\mathcal F_{X,c}\boxtimes\mathcal F_{X,c'}\to\mathcal F_{X,c+c'}\),
intertwining \(\varphi_p\) on each side.
\end{enumerate}
Then there exists a multiplicative orientation cocycle
\[
\mu_{c,c'}\,:\;o_{c+c'}\;\xrightarrow{\ \sim\ }\;o_c\otimes o_{c'},
\qquad c,c'\in\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}},
\]
with the following properties:
\begin{enumerate}
\item[\textup{(i)}] (Strict pentagon.)
\(\mu_{c+c',c''}\circ\mu_{c,c'}=\mu_{c,c'+c''}\circ\mu_{c',c''}\) as
maps of \(HC^-\)-modules, with no higher coherence remainder.
\item[\textup{(ii)}] (\(S^1\)-equivariance.) Each \(\mu_{c,c'}\) is
an \(S^1\)-equivariant map of cyclotomic spectra; the Connes operator
\(B\) intertwines source and target.
\item[\textup{(iii)}] (PTVV compatibility.) The Tate construction
\((-)^{tC_p}\) carries \(\mu_{c,c'}\) to a comparison of Frobenius
twists \(\mathcal F_{X,c}^{(p)}\otimes\mathcal F_{X,c'}^{(p)}\to
\mathcal F_{X,c+c'}^{(p)}\) compatible with the PTVV \cite{PTVV2013}
\((-1)\)-shifted symplectic form on \(\mathfrak M_{X,c}\), in the
sense that \(\mu_{c,c'}\) restricts on the underlying graded
determinants to the symplectic-Lagrangian comparison map of
\cite{JoyceKinjoParkSafronov}.
\end{enumerate}
In particular, hypothesis (O) of
Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:ptvv-joyce-pi-descent}} is satisfied, and the
construction of \(\{\mu_{c,c'}\}\) is independent of the Costello--Li
flat Calabi--Yau pairing and of any K\"unneth decomposition of
\(\mathcal F_X\) along \(K3\times E\).
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
\emph{Step 1 (Construction of \(\mu_{c,c'}\) in \(HC^-\)).}  Apply the
\(S^1\)-fixed-points functor \((-)^{hS^1}\) to the symmetric monoidal
external product of (C3): the resulting map
\[
HC^-(\mathcal F_{X,c})\otimes HC^-(\mathcal F_{X,c'})
\;\longrightarrow\;
HC^-(\mathcal F_{X,c+c'})
\]
is a strict map of \(\mathbb E_\infty\)-algebras in cyclotomic spectra
by Nikolaus--Scholze \cite[Cor.~II.1.7, Thm.~II.6.9]{NikolausScholze},
since \((-)^{hS^1}\) is lax symmetric monoidal and the cyclotomic
Frobenius \(\varphi_p\) is itself symmetric monoidal.  Take
\(\widehat o_c\) and \(\widehat o_{c'}\) as in (C2); their product
under this map lifts the right-hand side of the desired isomorphism
\(o_c\otimes o_{c'}\), and divides the lift \(\widehat o_{c+c'}\) of
\(o_{c+c'}\) to define
\(\mu_{c,c'}:=\widehat o_{c+c'}\cdot
(\widehat o_c\boxtimes\widehat o_{c'})^{-1}\).  The Connes operator
\(B\) acts trivially on units of \(\pi_0\), so \(\mu_{c,c'}\) is
\(S^1\)-equivariant on the nose.

\emph{Step 2 (Strict pentagon from \(\mathbb E_\infty\)-associativity).}
The pentagon
\(\mu_{c+c',c''}\circ\mu_{c,c'}=\mu_{c,c'+c''}\circ\mu_{c',c''}\) is
the \(\pi_0\)-shadow of the strict associator of the
\(\mathbb E_\infty\)-algebra structure on \(\bigoplus_c HC^-(\mathcal F_{X,c})\)
in cyclotomic spectra.  Strictness follows because Nikolaus--Scholze
\cite[Thm.~I.1.13]{NikolausScholze} present the cyclotomic
\(\infty\)-category as a strict \(\mathbb E_\infty\)-monoidal limit
along the Frobenius diagram; the homotopy-coherent pentagon
collapses to an on-the-nose identity at the level of
\(\pi_0\)-units.  No higher coherence datum is required, because
\(\pi_0HC^-\) is a discrete commutative monoid and units satisfy strict
associativity in any commutative monoid.

\emph{Step 3 (\(S^1\)-equivariance built in).}  By construction
\(HC^-=HH^{hS^1}\) is the genuine \(S^1\)-fixed-points spectrum, so
every map produced by Step~1 is \(S^1\)-equivariant.  The Connes
operator \(B\) is the generator of the \(S^1\)-action on \(HH\)
\cite{Goodwillie1985}, and \(B\) acts as a derivation on \(HC^-\);
it kills \(\pi_0\)-units, hence kills \(\mu_{c,c'}\) as a higher
homotopy.

\emph{Step 4 (Tate-construction comparison with PTVV).}  Apply
\((-)^{tC_p}\) to the equation defining \(\mu_{c,c'}\).  The
Frobenius \(\varphi_p\) intertwines source and target by (C1) and (C3),
so \(\mu_{c,c'}^{tC_p}\) is the comparison of Frobenius twists
\(\mathcal F_{X,c}^{(p)}\otimes\mathcal F_{X,c'}^{(p)}\to
\mathcal F_{X,c+c'}^{(p)}\).  Restrict to the underlying graded
determinants: the symplectic structure on
\(\mathfrak M_{X,c}\) of PTVV \cite{PTVV2013} is the
\((-1)\)-shifted symplectic form whose square root is \(o_c\)
\textup{\cite[Definition~\ref{def:orientation-line}]{}}; under
\((-)^{tC_p}\) this form is sent to the Tate-Frobenius pairing on
\(\det\mathrm{RHom}(\mathcal C,\mathcal C)^{(p)}\), which by
Joyce--Kinjo--Park--Safronov \cite[multiplicative orientation
construction]{JoyceKinjoParkSafronov} agrees with the
symplectic-Lagrangian comparison map.  Compatibility (iii) follows.

The data \(\{\mu_{c,c'}\}\) is a multiplicative
orientation cocycle satisfying (i)--(iii), so hypothesis (O) of
Theorem~\ref{thm:ptvv-joyce-pi-descent} holds.  The construction
factors through the cyclotomic-spectrum machinery of Nikolaus--Scholze
\cite{NikolausScholze} and the Connes-\(B\) calculus of
Goodwillie \cite{Goodwillie1985}; it does not invoke Costello--Li
chiral pairings, K\"unneth decompositions of \(\mathcal F_X\) along
\(K3\times E\), or any compactness datum beyond (C1)--(C3).  \qedhere
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}
Hypotheses (C1), (C2), (C3) are open for \(K3\times E\): (C1) asks
\(\mathcal F_{X,c}\) to carry a cyclotomic structure in the
Nikolaus--Scholze sense \cite{NikolausScholze}; (C2) asks orientation
lines to lift to \(\pi_0HC^-\) units, refining
Definition~\ref{def:orientation-line}; (C3) asks symmetric monoidality
of \(\{\mathcal F_{X,c}\}\) at the cyclotomic level.  The cocycle
\(\mu_{c,c'}\) is built from the Hochschild--cyclic machinery of
\(\mathcal F_X\) alone, supplying an alternative construction of
hypothesis (O) disjoint from the Costello--Li flat Calabi--Yau pairing
and from any K\"unneth decomposition.
\end{remark}

\begin{definition}[Sectorial Hall truncation]
Suppose an extension-closed compact Hall category graded by the additive
physical lattice \(\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}\) of
Definition~\ref{def:additive-physical-charge-lattice}, together with the
Gram map \(\Pi_X\), a stability/HN/support datum
\(\sigma=(Z_\sigma,\mathcal P_\sigma)\), and semistable stacks
\(\mathfrak M_{\sigma,S,c}^{ss}\) for \(c\in\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}\).
Fix a strict
sector \(S\subset\C^\times\) of angular width \(<\pi\), with no active
semistable ray on its boundary.  Choose \(\vartheta\) so that
$$
h_S(c):=\Re(e^{-i\vartheta}Z_\sigma(c))>0
$$
on every nonzero semistable class with central charge in \(S\).
For \(R>0\), set
$$
F_{\sigma,S}(R)
=\{c\mid \mathfrak M_{\sigma,S,c}^{ss}\ne\varnothing,\
0<h_S(c)\le R\},
$$
and
$$
\Gamma_{\sigma,S}^{HN}(R)
=\left\{c_1+\cdots+c_k\ \middle|\
c_i\in F_{\sigma,S}(R),\
\sum_i h_S(c_i)\le R\right\}.
$$
If an oriented critical Hall object
\(\mathcal H_{\sigma,S}^{or}\) has been constructed, put
$$
\mathcal H_{\sigma,S}^{>R}
=\prod_{h_S(c)>R}\mathcal H_{\sigma,S,c}^{or},
\qquad
\mathsf F_R\mathcal H_{\sigma,S}^{or}
=\mathcal H_{\sigma,S}^{or}/\mathcal H_{\sigma,S}^{>R}.
$$
\end{definition}

\begin{lemma}[Conditional finite Hall quotient]
\label{prop:sectorial-hall-truncation}
A nonzero additive heart cannot have finite nonzero charge support in
\(\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}\).  The pushed-forward active support
\(\Gamma_{\mathrm{act}}\subset\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}}\) is not additive.
The finite Hall object is therefore not a finite active-support heart.

Assume the support property, the
HN property, finite type of the
semistable stacks in bounded \(h_S\)-height, and the oriented critical
Hall correspondences.  Then \(F_{\sigma,S}(R)\) and
\(\Gamma_{\sigma,S}^{HN}(R)\) are finite,
\(\mathcal H_{\sigma,S}^{>R}\) is a two-sided Hall ideal, and
\(\mathsf F_R\mathcal H_{\sigma,S}^{or}\) is a finite Hall quotient.
The compact sectorial Hall object is the completed inverse system
$$
\widehat{\mathcal H}_{\sigma,S}^{or}
=\varprojlim_R\mathsf F_R\mathcal H_{\sigma,S}^{or}.
$$
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
If a heart contains an object of nonzero charge \(c\), it contains
all finite direct sums of that object, hence all charges \(kc\).
Since \(\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}\) is torsion-free, the charge support is
infinite.  Also \((0,-1,0)\in\Gamma_{\mathrm{act}}\), while
\((0,-2,0)\notin\Gamma_{\mathrm{act}}\), so active support is not
additive.

For semistable classes in \(S\), the strict-sector condition gives
\(h_S(c)\ge \kappa|Z_\sigma(c)|\) for some \(\kappa>0\).  The support
property and discreteness of the numerical lattice make
\(F_{\sigma,S}(R)\) finite.  The function \(h_S\) is positive and
additive on extensions in the sector; hence HN sums of total height
\(\le R\) form a finite set and the subspace of height \(>R\) is a
two-sided Hall ideal.  The inverse limit is the \(h_S\)-adic Hall
completion.
\end{proof}

\begin{definition}[Compact Igusa realization datum]
\label{def:compact-igusa-realization-datum}
A compact realization of the Igusa square root is a package
$$
\mathfrak K_X
=\left(\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}},\Pi_X,
\mathcal A^{E_3}_X,\mathrm{Sp}^{\mathrm{ch}}_{K3,E},
\mathcal F_X,\mathcal H_X,C_X,\Theta_{\mathrm{Kos}},
\Pi_{\mathrm{rec}}\right)
$$
with the following data.
\begin{enumerate}
\item[\((\Gamma)\)] The additive physical charge lattice
\(\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}\), the Gram map
\(\Pi_X:\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}\to\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}}\), and the
cocycle \(B\) of
Definition~\ref{def:additive-physical-charge-lattice} and
Lemma~\ref{lem:gram-additivity-defect}.  The Hall category is graded by
\(\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}\), not by \(\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}}\) itself.
\item[\((E_3)\)] A supplied charge-completed holomorphic
\(E_3\)-factorization algebra, denoted \(\mathcal A^{E_3}_X\), on
\(X=K3\times E\), finite-first after the sectorial HN quotients of
Proposition~\ref{prop:sectorial-hall-truncation}.  A compact
holomorphic-Chern--Simons/BV construction, if it satisfies descent, the
quantum master equation, and anomaly cancellation in the completed charge
category, is a candidate source for this datum.  The datum also includes
a fixed \(E_3\)-formality point, a chain-level \(S^3\)-framing witness,
compact-support control, and continuity of the \(E_3\) operations across
the finite HN inverse system.
\item[\((\mathrm{Sp})\)] A supplied chain-level \(K3\)-to-\(E\) specialization
\(\mathrm{Sp}^{\mathrm{ch}}_{K3,E}\) and named comparison maps
\(\kappa_E\) (chiral-Koszul) and \(\pi_*^{\mathrm{ch}}\)
(proper-pushforward identification), with the triple zigzag
$$
\mathcal A^{E_3}_X
\xrightarrow{\ \mathrm{Sp}^{\mathrm{ch}}_{K3,E}\ }
\mathcal F_X^{(0)}
\xrightarrow{\ \kappa_E\ }
\mathcal F_X^{(1)}
\xrightarrow{\ \pi_*^{\mathrm{ch}}\ }
(p_E)_*\mathcal A^{E_3}_X
$$
of equivalences in the projection-finite sectors.  In the wrapped
elliptic-degree sectors, the candidate filling is the hybrid object
\(\mathcal F_X^{\mathrm{hyb}}\) of
Open Problem~\ref{op:hybrid-wrapped-factorization}, namely a
charge-completed compact observable factorization object on
\(\operatorname{Ran}(E)\) constructible along the elliptic-degree
stratification.  A global Fock/Hecke sector is acceptable here only if
it acts through mixed local/wrapped Hall correspondences before the
reduced \(E\)-quotient.  These equivalences and wrapped-sector data are
part of the datum, not operations constructed from the determinant.
\item[\((\mathrm H)\)] An oriented compact Hall factorization object \(\mathcal H_X\)
graded by \(c\in\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}\), with finite-type sectorial
moduli stacks and extension correspondences
$$
\mathfrak M_c^\sigma\times\mathfrak M_{c'}^\sigma
\xleftarrow{\ p_{c,c'}\ }
\mathfrak E_{c,c'}^\sigma
\xrightarrow{\ q_{c,c'}\ }
\mathfrak M_{c+c'}^\sigma,
$$
perfect reduced obstruction theories or critical
\((-1)\)-shifted symplectic structures, vanishing-cycle coefficients,
orientation lines with chosen square roots, Thom--Sebastiani orientation
transport coherent for triple extensions, and protected integration maps
compatible with HN completion and wall crossing.  The Hall atlas must
include local-local, wrapped-wrapped, and mixed local/wrapped extension
correspondences before quotienting by the translation action of \(E\);
quotienting first forgets the relative \(E\)-position needed by mixed
convolution.  If a lifted action of
\(W^{(2)}(\La^{2,1}_{II})\) on the oriented completed Hall object is
supplied, its induced orientation character \(\epsilon_o\) is required to satisfy
\[
\epsilon_o|_{W^{(2)}(\La^{2,1}_{II})}
=\nu_{\Delta_5}|_{W^{(2)}(\La^{2,1}_{II})}.
\]
Constructing the domain of this comparison and the character
\(\epsilon_o\) is part of the datum.  The comparison is a geometric
orientation-monodromy condition on the Hall side; it requires computing
the determinant-line signs on the three type-II simple reflections and
checking the reflection relations.  It is not obtained by choosing the
scalar normalization of \(\Delta_5\).
\item[\((\Pi_*)\)] A Gram-pushforward or cocycle-corrected descent
datum
\[
\Pi_{X,*}\mathcal F_X
\]
whose protected primitives are \(\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}}\)-graded and
whose bracket is induced from the upstairs
\(\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}\)-graded Hall bracket.  Before this descent,
the protected primitives of \(\mathcal F_X\) are graded by the upstairs
additive charge \(c\), not by a Gram triple.  The comparison with
\(\mathfrak g_{\Delta_5,\alpha(n,l,m)}\) is made after passing to
\((n,l,m)=\Pi_X(c)\).
\item[\((\mathrm C)\)] A conilpotent chiral coalgebra \(C_X\) and a charge-preserving
quasi-isomorphism
$$
C_X\simeq \bar B_E^{\mathrm{ch}}(\mathcal F_X)
$$
in the completed chiral bar category.
\item[\((\Theta)\)] A chiral cobar quasi-isomorphism
$$
\Theta_{\mathrm{Kos}}:
\Omega_E^{\mathrm{ch}}C_X
\xrightarrow{\ \simeq\ }
\mathsf{Den}_{\Delta_5,E}.
$$
\item[\((\Pi)\)] A primitive recognition certificate
\(\Pi_{\mathrm{rec}}\) for
$$
P_X^\Pi:=H^0\Prim_{\mathrm{prot}}(\Pi_{X,*}\mathcal F_X).
$$
This certificate is not a determinant datum.  It consists of the
Gram-descended Lie superalgebra structure on \(P_X^\Pi\), the parity split of
each homogeneous primitive piece, simple primitive representatives for
the Gritsenko--Nikulin real and imaginary simple roots, verification of
the Borcherds--Kac defining relations in the protected bracket, the
completed Hopf pairing, generation by the simple primitives and the
Cartan, a no-extra-relations theorem, completed PBW compatibility, and
the same radical quotient as the Gritsenko--Nikulin automorphic
correction.
\end{enumerate}
\end{definition}

\begin{theorem}[Primitive recognition certificate]
\label{prop:compact-igusa-realization-criterion}
\label{thm:primitive-recognition}
Let \(\mathscr B_{\Delta_5}\) be the Borcherds--Cartan superdatum used by
Gritsenko--Nikulin for the automorphic correction: Cartan
\(\La^{2,1}_{II}\otimes\C\), real simple roots
\(\delta_1,\delta_2,\delta_3\), imaginary simple-root fibres with the
Gritsenko--Nikulin parity split, and bilinear form
\((\alpha_i,\alpha_j)\).  Let \(G(\mathscr B_{\Delta_5})\) denote the
corresponding Borcherds--Kac Lie superalgebra modulo the standard radical
of the completed invariant pairing; this is
\(\mathcal A_{\mathrm{den}}=\mathfrak g_{\Delta_5}\).

Suppose a compact Hall/factorization construction supplies the
Gram-descended primitive algebra
$$
P_X^\Pi=H^0\Prim_{\mathrm{prot}}(\Pi_{X,*}\mathcal F_X)
$$
after its completed Hopf-pairing radical quotient, with the following
data.
\begin{enumerate}
\item[(1a)] A \(\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}\)-graded Lie superalgebra
structure on a Hall lift \(\widetilde P_X\) with
\(P_X^\Pi=\Pi_{X,*}\widetilde P_X\), where \(\Pi_{X,*}\) is the descent
along \(\Pi_X:\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}\to\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}}\) of
Definition~\ref{def:dyonic-mukai-lattice}, finite dimensional in each
homogeneous parity piece, and a Cartan identification
$$P^\Pi_{X,0}\simeq\La^{2,1}_{II}\otimes\C.$$
\item[(1b)] \(\Pi_X\)-descent of the bracket: the cocycle
\(B(c,c')\in\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}}\) of
Definition~\ref{def:dyonic-mukai-lattice} acts trivially on bracket
targets in primitives, that is,
\[
[\widetilde P_{X,c},\widetilde P_{X,c'}]
\subset\widetilde P_{X,c+c'}\cap
\Pi_X^{-1}\bigl(\Pi_X(c)+\Pi_X(c')+B(c,c')\bigr)
\xrightarrow{\ \Pi_{X,*}\ }
P^\Pi_{X,\Pi_X(c)+\Pi_X(c')},
\]
so that the induced \(\Gamma_{\mathrm{gram}}\)-grading of
\(P_X^\Pi\) is a Lie-superalgebra grading; \(B\) lies in the Hochschild
kernel of the protected primitive bracket.  Granted (P) and (O),
Theorem~\ref{thm:ptvv-joyce-pi-descent} exhibits
\(B=d_{\mathrm{Hoch}}\Theta\) as a Hochschild boundary, with \(\Theta\)
the determinant-line cochain produced from the multiplicative
trivialisation \(\{\mu_{c,c'}\}\) of (O); the chain-level graded
Frobenius identity (F) is supplied by
Lemma~\ref{lem:F-frobenius-from-hopf-nondegeneracy} from (P), (O), and
item~(6) below.  Existence of (O) on the reduced compact protected
sector of \(K3\times E\) is Open
Problem~\ref{op:pi-descent-of-bracket}.
\item The degree map
\[
\alpha(n,l,m)=2nf_2-lf_3+2mf_{-2}
\]
identifies the Gram-descended grading with the Gritsenko--Nikulin root
grading.  The upstairs Hall bracket is graded by
\(\Gamma_X^{\mathrm{phys}}\); this item is a statement after the descent
datum \(\Pi_{X,*}\).
\item For every simple-root index \(i\) of
\(\mathscr B_{\Delta_5}\), primitive representatives
\[
e_i^X\in P^\Pi_{X,\alpha_i},\qquad
f_i^X\in P^\Pi_{X,-\alpha_i},\qquad
h_i^X\in P^\Pi_{X,0}
\]
are supplied, preserving the real/imaginary distinction, multiplicity
fibres, and parity map.
\item In the protected Hall/factorization bracket these representatives
satisfy the Borcherds--Kac defining relations for
\(\mathscr B_{\Delta_5}\): Cartan and Chevalley relations, real Serre
relations for the even real simple roots, the imaginary-root
orthogonality relations \((\alpha_i,\alpha_j)=0\Rightarrow
[e_i^X,e_j^X]=[f_i^X,f_j^X]=0\), and the super sign rule.
\item The completed Hopf pairing on the positive and negative primitive
halves has the same radical quotient as the Gritsenko--Nikulin/Kac
construction of \(G(\mathscr B_{\Delta_5})\).
\item The Hall primitive algebra satisfies a no-extra-relations theorem:
after the standard radical quotient, the kernel of the map from the
Borcherds--Kac presentation is exactly the Borcherds--Serre ideal and no
additional completed relation survives.
\item \(P_X^\Pi\) is generated by \(P^\Pi_{X,0}\) and the simple primitive
representatives \(e_i^X,f_i^X\).
\item A completed PBW theorem holds for \(P_X^\Pi\), and its PBW filtration
is transported to the PBW filtration on
\(U(\mathfrak g_{\Delta_5})\) under the comparison map.
\item The full root-space parity dimensions in \(P_X^\Pi\) agree with those
of \(G(\mathscr B_{\Delta_5})\).  Consequently, on active positive
Gram degrees,
$$
\sdim P^\Pi_{X,(n,l,m)}=f(nm,l).
$$
\end{enumerate}
Then
$$
H^0\Prim_{\mathrm{prot}}(\Pi_{X,*}\mathcal F_X)
\cong
\mathcal A_{\mathrm{den}}
=\mathfrak g_{\Delta_5}
$$
as Gram-graded Lie superalgebras, and its Weyl--Kac--Borcherds
denominator is \(64^{-1}\Delta_5(2Z)\).  If in addition
\(\Theta_{\mathrm{Kos}}\) is supplied, then
$$
\Omega_E^{\mathrm{ch}}C_X\simeq\mathsf{Den}_{\Delta_5,E}.
$$
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The simple primitive representatives and the displayed relations give a
homomorphism
$$
G(\mathscr B_{\Delta_5})\longrightarrow P_X^\Pi
$$
from the universal Borcherds--Kac presentation.  Generation gives
surjectivity.  The no-extra-relations hypothesis identifies the kernel
with the standard Borcherds--Serre ideal after the completed radical
quotient; the completed PBW compatibility promotes the finite-stage
identification to the inverse limit.  The full parity dimensions rule out
additional zero-superdimension root spaces.  Hence the homomorphism is an
isomorphism of Gram-graded Lie superalgebras.  The denominator statement
is Theorem~\ref{thm:denominator-algebra-identity}.  The chiral statement
is exactly the quasi-isomorphism \(\Theta_{\mathrm{Kos}}\).
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Low-degree bracket information]
\label{prop:low-degree-denominator-brackets}
The denominator algebra determines the following low-degree data.  With
$$
\alpha(n,l,m)=n\delta_1+m\delta_2+(n+m-l)\delta_3,
$$
the active rows through height three are
$$
\begin{array}{c|c|c|c}
\beta & \gamma & (\beta,\beta) & \smult(\beta)\\ \hline
\delta_i & (1,1,0),(0,1,1),(0,-1,0) & 2 & 1\\
\delta_i+\delta_j\ (i<j) & (1,2,1),(1,0,0),(0,0,1) & 0 & 10\\
2\delta_i+\delta_j\ (i\ne j) & \hbox{six real rows} & 2 & 1\\
\delta_1+\delta_2+\delta_3 & (1,1,1) & -6 & -64 .
\end{array}
$$
After choosing even Chevalley generators \(e_i,f_i,h_i\) for the real
simple roots,
$$
[h_i,e_j]=(\delta_i,\delta_j)e_j,\qquad
[e_i,f_j]=\delta_{ij}h_i,\qquad
(\operatorname{ad}e_i)^3e_j=0\quad(i\ne j).
$$
For \(E_{ij}:=[e_i,e_j]\),
$$
[f_i,E_{ij}]=2e_j,\qquad [f_j,E_{ij}]=-2e_i.
$$
These are denominator-algebra constants.  They are not compact Hall
constants.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The table is obtained by writing
\(\beta=c_1\delta_1+c_2\delta_2+c_3\delta_3\) and solving
$$
\gamma(\beta)=(c_1,c_1+c_2-c_3,c_2).
$$
Then \((\beta,\beta)=-2(4nm-l^2)\), and
\(\smult(\beta)=f(nm,l)\) follows from
Theorem~\ref{thm:denominator-algebra-identity}.  The displayed bracket
constants are the normalized Chevalley, Jacobi and Serre constants for
the symmetric Cartan matrix \(A=((\delta_i,\delta_j))\).
\end{proof}

\begin{openproblem}[Compact \(E_3\), Hall, and chiral Koszul realization]
\label{op:compact-igusa-realization}
Construct the datum
\(\mathfrak K_X\) of Definition~\ref{def:compact-igusa-realization-datum}.
Equivalently, construct the holomorphic \(E_3\)-factorization algebra
on \(K3\times E\), its chain-level \(K3\)-to-\(E\) specialization, the
compact observable chiral shadow on \(\operatorname{Ran}(E)\), the
oriented HN-completed Hall object, protected integration, the
conilpotent chiral bar coalgebra, the chiral cobar quasi-isomorphism to
\(\mathsf{Den}_{\Delta_5,E}\), and the primitive recognition certificate
of Theorem~\ref{thm:primitive-recognition}.  In particular one must
construct the compact Hall bracket constants, the full compact parity
dimensions, the simple primitive representatives, and the
Borcherds--Kac relation verification.  The scalar square and the
denominator algebra are inputs to this problem.  They are not its
solution.
\end{openproblem}

\begin{definition}[Imaginary simple roots]
For $a\in \La^{2,1}_{II}\cap\R_{>0}\Poly_{II}$ set
$$
\mu_{\overline 0}(a)=
\begin{cases}
m(a),& (a,a)<0\ \text{and}\ m(a)>0,\\
\tau(a),& (a,a)=0\ \text{and}\ \tau(a)>0,\\
0,&\text{otherwise},
\end{cases}
$$
and
$$
\mu_{\overline 1}(a)=
\begin{cases}
-m(a),& (a,a)<0\ \text{and}\ m(a)<0,\\
-\tau(a),& (a,a)=0\ \text{and}\ \tau(a)<0,\\
0,&\text{otherwise}.
\end{cases}
$$
This sign split is the Gritsenko--Nikulin BKM parity datum.  The
product statement alone fixes only a Grothendieck representative for the
signed exponent.  Define multisets by
multiplicity:
$$a\in\Delta_{\overline0}^{im}\quad\hbox{with multiplicity }
\mu_{\overline0}(a),$$
$$a\in\Delta_{\overline1}^{im}\quad\hbox{with multiplicity }
\mu_{\overline1}(a).$$
Put
$$\Delta^{im}=\Delta_{\overline0}^{im}\cup\Delta_{\overline1}^{im}.$$
$$\mathcal O_{\mathrm{den}}^{im}
=\bigoplus_{a\in\Delta^{im}}
\left(\mathfrak g_{a,\overline0}\ominus\mathfrak g_{a,\overline1}\right).$$
This is notation inside the denominator algebra; it is not a BPS state
space.
\end{definition}
The real simple roots are
$$\Delta_{\overline0}^{re,\mathrm{simp}}
=\Delta^{re}_{\mathrm{simp}}=\Poly_{II,prim}
=\{\delta_1,\delta_2,\delta_3\},\qquad
\Delta_{\overline1}^{re,\mathrm{simp}}=\varnothing.$$
Put
$$\Delta_{\overline p}=\Delta_{\overline p}^{re,\mathrm{simp}}\cup
\Delta_{\overline p}^{im}\qquad(p=0,1),\qquad
\Delta=\Delta_{\overline0}\cup\Delta_{\overline1}.$$
The Cartan data satisfy $(\alpha,\alpha)>0$ for
$\alpha \in \Delta^{re}$, $(\alpha,\alpha)\leq 0$ for
$\alpha \in \Delta^{im}$, and
$(\alpha,\alpha')\leq 0$ for all distinct $\alpha,\alpha'\in\Delta$.
If $(\alpha,\alpha)>0$, then
$$2\frac{(\alpha,\alpha')}{(\alpha,\alpha)} \in \Z,$$
since $(\alpha,\alpha)=2$ and
$\La^{2,1}_{II}=\Z\delta_1+\Z\delta_2+\Z\delta_3$.
\begin{definition}[Generators and relations]
Let $I$ be an index set equipped with a parity map $p:I\to\Z/2\Z$ and a
root map $i\mapsto\alpha_i\in\Delta$, with fibres over an imaginary root
of cardinality $\mu_{\overline p}(a)$ in parity $p$.  If
$i\neq j$ and $\alpha_i=\alpha_j$, the two indices are distinct simple
roots.
$$\operatorname{ch}:I\rightarrow\La^{2,1}_{II},\qquad
i\mapsto\alpha_i.$$
The superalgebra $\autcor$ is generated by
$$h_i,\ e_i,\ f_i,\qquad i\in I.$$
The Cartan subalgebra is identified with $\La^{2,1}_{II}\otimes\C$ by
$h_i\mapsto\alpha_i$.  Relations:

\begin{itemize}
\item $[h_i,e_j]=(\alpha_i,\alpha_j)e_j$ and
$[h_i,f_j]=-(\alpha_i,\alpha_j)f_j$
\item $[e_i,f_j]=\delta_{ij}h_i$
\item if $\alpha_i \in \Delta^{re}_{\mathrm{simp}}$ and $i\neq j$, then
$$
(\operatorname{ad} e_i)^{1-2(\alpha_i,\alpha_j)/(\alpha_i,\alpha_i)}
e_j=
(\operatorname{ad} f_i)^{1-2(\alpha_i,\alpha_j)/(\alpha_i,\alpha_i)}
f_j=0
$$
\item if $(\alpha_i,\alpha_j)=0$, then $[e_i,e_j]=[f_i,f_j]=0$
\end{itemize}
\end{definition}

The grading is by $\La^{2,1}_{II}$.  Put
$$Q_+=\sum_{\alpha\in\Delta}\Z_{\geq0}\alpha
\subset\La^{2,1}_{II}.$$
The triangular decomposition is
$$\autcor =
\left(\bigoplus_{\alpha \in Q_+\setminus\{0\}}
\mathfrak{g}_{\alpha}\right)
\oplus(\La^{2,1}_{II}\otimes\C)
\oplus
\left(\bigoplus_{\alpha \in Q_+\setminus\{0\}}
\mathfrak{g}_{-\alpha}\right).$$
For $i\in I$,
$$\deg e_i=\alpha_i,\qquad \deg f_i=-\alpha_i,\qquad \deg h_i=0.$$
$$[\mathfrak g_\alpha,\mathfrak g_\beta]\subset
\mathfrak g_{\alpha+\beta}.$$
$$\mathfrak{g}_0=\La^{2,1}_{II}\otimes\C.$$
The positive and negative roots are
$$\mathcal R_+=\{\alpha\in Q_+\setminus\{0\}\mid
\mathfrak{g}_{\alpha}\neq0\},\qquad
\mathcal R_-=-\mathcal R_+.$$
For every root $\alpha$, set
$$\rootmult_{\overline{0}}(\alpha)
=\dim\mathfrak{g}_{\alpha,\overline{0}},\qquad
\rootmult_{\overline{1}}(\alpha)
=\dim\mathfrak{g}_{\alpha,\overline{1}}.$$
The signed root superdimension is
$$\smult(\alpha)=\rootmult_{\overline{0}}(\alpha)
-\rootmult_{\overline{1}}(\alpha).$$
The Weyl--Kac--Borcherds denominator is
$$
\begin{aligned}
\Phi_{\Delta_5}(z)
&=\sum_{w\in W^{(2)}(\La^{2,1}_{II})}\det(w)
\left(
e^{-2\pi i(w(\rho),z)}
-\sum_{a\in\La^{2,1}_{II}\cap\R_{>0}\Poly_{II}}
m(a)e^{-2\pi i(w(\rho+a),z)}
\right)\\
&=e^{-2\pi i(\rho,z)}
\prod_{\alpha\in\mathcal R_+}
\left(1-e^{-2\pi i(\alpha,z)}\right)^{\smult(\alpha)}.
\end{aligned}
$$
$$\Omega(\La^{2,1}_{II})
=\La^{2,1}_{II}\otimes\R+i\Cone(\La^{2,1}_{II})_+.$$

\begin{theorem}[Denominator identity]
$$\frac{1}{64}\Delta_5(2Z)=\Phi_{\Delta_5}(z).$$
$$\operatorname{den}(\autcor)=\frac1{64}\Delta_5(2Z).$$
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
$$\frac1{64}\Delta_5(Z)
=\sum_{w\in W^{(2)}(\La^{2,1}_{II})}\det(w)
\left(
e^{-\pi i(w(\rho),z)}
-\sum_{a\in\La^{2,1}_{II}\cap\R_{>0}\Poly_{II}}
m(a)e^{-\pi i(w(\rho+a),z)}
\right).$$
$$Z\mapsto2Z:\qquad
e^{-\pi i(w(\rho+a),z)}
\mapsto e^{-2\pi i(w(\rho+a),z)}.$$
Weyl--Kac--Borcherds:
$$e^{-2\pi i(\rho,z)}
\prod_{\alpha\in\mathcal R_+}
\left(1-e^{-2\pi i(\alpha,z)}\right)^{\smult(\alpha)}.$$
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Gram-index cone and denominator cone]
$$\alpha(\Gamma_{\mathrm{act}})
=\{\alpha(n,l,m)\mid(n,l,m)\in\Gamma_{\mathrm{eff}},\ f(nm,l)\neq0\}
\subset\La^{2,1}_{II}.$$
$$
\alpha(\Gamma_{\mathrm{act}})
\subset
\mathcal R_+^{\mathrm{vis}}
:=\{\alpha\in\mathcal R_+\mid \smult(\alpha)\neq0\}.
$$
$$\smult(\alpha(n,l,m))
=\dim\mathfrak{g}_{\alpha(n,l,m),\overline0}
-\dim\mathfrak{g}_{\alpha(n,l,m),\overline1}
=f(nm,l)\qquad((n,l,m)\in\Gamma_{\mathrm{act}}).$$
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
$$\alpha:\Gamma_{\mathrm{ind}}\to\La^{2,1}_{II},\qquad
(n,l,m)\mapsto2nf_2-lf_3+2mf_{-2}.$$
$$q^nr^ls^m=\exp(-\pi i(\alpha(n,l,m),z))$$
$$Z\mapsto2Z.$$
$$\frac1{64}\Delta_5(2Z)
=e^{-2\pi i(\rho,z)}
\prod_{\alpha\in\mathcal R_+}
\left(1-e^{-2\pi i(\alpha,z)}\right)^{\smult(\alpha)}.$$
$$\frac1{64}\mathcal D_X(2Z)
=e^{-2\pi i(\rho,z)}
\prod_{(n,l,m)\in\Gamma_{\mathrm{eff}}}
\left(1-e^{-2\pi i(\alpha(n,l,m),z)}\right)^{f(nm,l)}.$$
The triples in $\Gamma_{\mathrm{eff}}\setminus\Gamma_{\mathrm{act}}$
have exponent zero and do not contribute visible product factors.  The
denominator product alone does not prove absence of root spaces with
zero signed superdimension.
$$\mathcal D_X=\Delta_5\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\smult(\alpha(n,l,m))=f(nm,l)
\quad((n,l,m)\in\Gamma_{\mathrm{act}}).$$
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[What the denominator determines]
The identity
$$
\frac1{64}\Delta_5(2Z)
=e^{-2\pi i(\rho,z)}
\prod_{\alpha\in\mathcal R_+}
\left(1-e^{-2\pi i(\alpha,z)}\right)^{\smult(\alpha)}
$$
determines the signed integers \(\smult(\alpha)\), once the
Gritsenko--Nikulin root set and positive root monoid have been fixed.  It
does not determine invisible zero-superdimension root spaces, the two
parity dimensions
$$
\rootmult_{\overline0}(\alpha),\qquad
\rootmult_{\overline1}(\alpha),
$$
and it does not determine the structure constants
$$
[\mathfrak g_\alpha,\mathfrak g_\beta]\to
\mathfrak g_{\alpha+\beta}.
$$
Thus signed root multiplicity is necessary input for primitive
recognition, but it is not a recognition certificate.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Write \(X^\alpha=e^{-2\pi i(\alpha,z)}\).  In the completed positive
root monoid algebra,
$$
\log\prod_{\alpha\in\mathcal R_+}(1-X^\alpha)^{\smult(\alpha)}
=-\sum_{\alpha\in\mathcal R_+}\sum_{k\ge1}
\frac{\smult(\alpha)}{k}X^{k\alpha}.
$$
Thus a logarithmic coefficient mixes divisor terms \(k\alpha=\lambda\).
The exponents \(\smult(\alpha)\) are recovered recursively by height,
equivalently by Mobius inversion on each primitive ray.  The recovered
exponent is only
$$
\smult(\alpha)=
\rootmult_{\overline0}(\alpha)-\rootmult_{\overline1}(\alpha).
$$
The difference $a-b$ does not determine the pair $(a,b)$, and no
bilinear bracket appears in the product.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[What the determinant forgets]
\label{thm:protected-denominator-shadow}
Let
$$
\mathcal B=\bigoplus_{\gamma\in\Gamma_{\mathrm{eff}}}\mathcal B_\gamma
$$
be any charge-graded super vector space with finite-dimensional
homogeneous pieces and
$$\sdim\mathcal B_{(n,l,m)}=f(nm,l).$$
Then its Gram-graded Euler/Fock determinant is
$$
64q^{1/2}r^{1/2}s^{1/2}
\prod_{\gamma\in\Gamma_{\mathrm{eff}}}(1-x^\gamma)^{\sdim\mathcal B_\gamma}
=\Delta_5(Z).
$$
If $\mathcal B$ carries a bracket compatible with charge addition, a
parity split, simple-root representatives, or a Hopf pairing, the
determinant forgets those data and remembers the class of
$\mathcal B$ in
$$K_0(\Gamma_{\mathrm{eff}}\hbox{-graded finite super vector spaces}).$$
Thus the determinant of
$\mathcal A_{\mathrm{den}}=\mathfrak g_{\Delta_5}$ is
the Grothendieck shadow of its denominator bracket.  The Borcherds
denominator bracket exists inside \(\mathcal A_{\mathrm{den}}\) by the
Gritsenko--Nikulin construction, but the determinant sees only its
charge-graded Grothendieck class.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The Fock determinant lemma gives
$$
\sdet_{\mathcal B}(1-x)
=\prod_{\gamma\in\Gamma_{\mathrm{eff}}}(1-x^\gamma)^{\sdim\mathcal B_\gamma}.
$$
The hypothesis $\sdim\mathcal B_{(n,l,m)}=f(nm,l)$ identifies this
product with the Borcherds product for $64^{-1}\Delta_5$.  Multiplying
by the vacuum factor gives $\Delta_5$.  A bracket
$$[\mathcal B_\gamma,\mathcal B_{\gamma'}]\to
\mathcal B_{\gamma+\gamma'}$$
does not occur in the determinant formula.  Neither do simple primitive
representatives, parity dimensions, relation constants, or a Hopf-pairing
radical.  The determinant is therefore invariant under replacing
$\mathcal B$ by any other graded super vector space with the same
Grothendieck class.
\end{proof}

\section{Coefficient dictionary and main synthesis}
\label{sec:coefficient-dictionary-main-synthesis}

The coefficient convention is fixed once and for all by
Eichler--Zagier normalization:
$$
Z_{\mathrm{K3}}=2\phi_{0,1},\qquad
\phi_{0,1}(\tau,z)=\sum_{n\ge0,\ l\in\Z}f(n,l)q^nr^l.
$$
Equivalently, if \(\phi_{12,1}\) is the first Fourier--Jacobi
coefficient of Igusa's weight-\(12\) form \(F_{12}\), and if
$$
\delta_{12}(\tau)=q\prod_{n\ge1}(1-q^n)^{24},
$$
then
$$
\phi_{0,1}=\frac{\phi_{12,1}}{\delta_{12}}.
$$
The first terms are
$$
\phi_{0,1}
=(r^{-1}+10+r)
+q(10r^{-2}-64r^{-1}+108-64r+10r^2)
$$
$$
\qquad
+q^2(r^{-3}+108r^{-2}-513r^{-1}+808
-513r+108r^2+r^3)+O(q^3).
$$
Thus
$$
f(0,-1)=1,\qquad f(0,0)=10,\qquad
f(1,1)=-64,\qquad f(1,0)=108.
$$
The weak Jacobi support condition is
$$
f(n,l)=0\quad\hbox{unless}\quad n\ge0,\quad 4n-l^2\ge-1,
$$
and \(f(n,l)=f(n,-l)\).  These integers have three distinct readings in
the paper:
$$
\begin{array}{c|c}
\hbox{object} & \hbox{meaning of }f(nm,l) \\ \hline
\mathcal V_{(n,l,m)} & \hbox{virtual \(K_0\)-superdimension} \\
\mathcal D_X & \hbox{Borcherds product exponent} \\
\mathfrak g_{\Delta_5,\alpha(n,l,m)} &
\hbox{signed root supermultiplicity on active support}
\end{array}
$$
The first reading is a protected Euler characteristic.  The second and
third readings are automorphic and denominator-algebra incarnations of
the same integer.  This is not an equality of Hilbert spaces, brackets,
or Hall structure constants.

The synthesis is the following spine:
\[
\begin{gathered}
\hbox{virtual determinant}
\longrightarrow
\hbox{denominator algebra}
\longrightarrow
\hbox{reduced scalar square}
\\
\longrightarrow
\hbox{compact realization problem}
\longrightarrow
\hbox{eight-row certificate extension}.
\end{gathered}
\]
\begin{theorem}[Coefficient dictionary and synthesis theorem]
\label{thm:protected-igusa-determinant}
Let \(X=K3\times E\).  Let
\[
\mathbb U_{n,l}\in K_0(\mathrm{sVect}_{\mathrm{fd}}),\qquad
\sdim\mathbb U_{n,l}=f(n,l),
\]
and define the virtual \(K_0\)-determinant object in the cusp chamber by
\[
\mathcal V_{(n,l,m)}=\mathbb U_{nm,l},\qquad
(n,l,m)\in\Gamma_{\mathrm{eff}}.
\]

First, the virtual determinant is the theta-normalized Igusa square root:
\[
\mathcal D_X(Z)
=64q^{1/2}r^{1/2}s^{1/2}
\prod_{(n,l,m)\in\Gamma_{\mathrm{eff}}}
(1-q^nr^ls^m)^{f(nm,l)}
=\Delta_5(Z).
\]
The numerical factor \(64\) is the theta-constant leading coefficient
\([q^{1/2}r^{1/2}s^{1/2}]\Delta_5\); the monic Borcherds product is
\[
D_5=64^{-1}\Delta_5.
\]

Second, under the Lorentzian degree map
\[
\alpha(n,l,m)=2nf_2-lf_3+2mf_{-2},
\qquad
q^nr^ls^m=\exp(-\pi i(\alpha(n,l,m),z)),
\]
the same active coefficients are the visible signed root
supermultiplicities of the Gritsenko--Nikulin denominator algebra:
\[
\smult\mathfrak g_{\Delta_5,\alpha(n,l,m)}
=f(nm,l)
\qquad ((n,l,m)\in\Gamma_{\mathrm{act}}),
\]
and
\[
\operatorname{den}(\mathfrak g_{\Delta_5})
=64^{-1}\Delta_5(2Z).
\]
This is the Gritsenko--Nikulin denominator theorem.  It determines the
signed root supermultiplicities in the fixed Borcherds datum; it does
not determine compact Hall constants or microscopic brackets.

Third, for the reduced Hilbert-scheme DT/PT/OP scalar branch,
\[
Z^X_{\mathrm{DT}}(T,Q,P)=Z^X_{\mathrm{OP}}(P,Q,T)
=-4096\,\Delta_5(Z)^{-2}.
\]
Here
\[
\chi_{10}^{\mathrm{OP}}=D_5^2=(64^{-1}\Delta_5)^2
=4096^{-1}\Delta_5^2,
\qquad
Z^X_{\mathrm{OP}}=-(\chi_{10}^{\mathrm{OP}})^{-1};
\]
hence \(-4096=-(64)^2\) is the OP scalar sign together with the
theta-to-monic normalization.  It is not an orientation character.
Thus, with
\[
\mathcal Z_{\mathrm{Borch}}^{\mathrm{vir}}=\mathcal D_X^{-1},
\]
one has
\[
Z^X_{\mathrm{DT}}=Z^X_{\mathrm{OP}}
=-4096\,(\mathcal Z_{\mathrm{Borch}}^{\mathrm{vir}})^2.
\]

Fourth, the stronger microscopic comparison
\[
H^0\Prim_{\mathrm{prot}}(\Pi_{X,*}\mathcal F_X)
\cong
\mathfrak g_{\Delta_5}
\]
is open unless the compact datum of
Definition~\ref{def:compact-igusa-realization-datum} is constructed.
If such a datum is constructed, Theorem~\ref{thm:primitive-recognition}
identifies its primitive denominator with \(64^{-1}\Delta_5(2Z)\).

Fifth, any claimed compact realization must also satisfy three
consequences.
\begin{enumerate}
\item A naive support-local factorization object on
\(\operatorname{Ran}(E)\) sees only projection-finite sectors.  If a
one-dimensional subscheme of \(K3\times E\) has positive elliptic
degree, its projection to \(E\) is all of \(E\).  Thus the full
\(s\)-direction of the Igusa product requires a hybrid local/global
wrapped factorization theory.  A separate global Fock/Hecke mode is
only determinant-level unless it is coupled to the local sector by mixed
Hall actions before the reduced \(E\)-quotient.
\item The automorphic character \(\nu_{\Delta_5}\) is theorem-level
data of \(\Delta_5\), and \(\Delta_5^2\) forgets it.  A compact Hall
orientation must construct a strong orientation character
\(\epsilon_o\) and prove
\[
\epsilon_o|_{W^{(2)}(\Lambda^{2,1}_{II})}
=\nu_{\Delta_5}|_{W^{(2)}(\Lambda^{2,1}_{II})}.
\]
The constants \(64\), \(4096\), and the OP minus sign do not solve this
orientation-monodromy problem.  The Hall-side proof must compute the
three simple type-II determinant-line signs and check the reflection
relations.
\item A primitive comparison with \(\mathfrak g_{\Delta_5}\) is a
presentation-level recognition certificate, not a consequence of signed
dimensions.  One must supply primitive representatives for the real and
imaginary simple roots, their parities, the Chevalley, real Serre and
orthogonality relations, generation, the completed Hopf pairing and the
same radical quotient, a no-extra-relations theorem, and completed PBW
compatibility.  Under these hypotheses the Borcherds--Kac universal
presentation gives the isomorphism with
\(\mathfrak g_{\Delta_5}\); without them the determinant fixes only a
Grothendieck class.
\end{enumerate}

Finally, the diagonal-divisor rows extend this same logic.  A row is
promoted beyond its automorphic product only by a row certificate fixing
the modular group or cover, character, divisor, Jacobi seed, product
lattice, Weyl chamber, reflection character, scalar theorem if one is
claimed, orientation data, one-particle index, and primitive algebra
comparison.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The Fock trace calculation gives
\[
\mathcal D_X
=64q^{1/2}r^{1/2}s^{1/2}\sdet_{\mathcal V}(1-x).
\]
The Borcherds--Gritsenko--Nikulin product formula for the input
\(\phi_{0,1}\) identifies this product with \(\Delta_5\), as recorded in
Proposition~\ref{prop:bgn-identification}.  The leading coefficient
\(64\) is fixed in the theta-normalized Fourier expansion of
\(\Delta_5\), hence \(D_5=64^{-1}\Delta_5\) is the monic product.

The Lorentzian monomial identity and pairing computation are in
Section~\ref{sec:duality-principle} and the Weyl-chamber section.  The
root-supermultiplicity and denominator identity are
Theorem~\ref{thm:denominator-algebra-identity}; the argument \(2Z\)
comes from passing from
\(\exp(-\pi i(\alpha,z))\) to the usual denominator character
\(\exp(-2\pi i(\alpha,z))\).

The reduced scalar identity is Theorem~\ref{thm:op-square}, with the
normalization conversion of Proposition~\ref{prop:op-normalization}.
Since Oberdieck--Pixton use
\(\chi_{10}^{\mathrm{OP}}=D_5^2\) and prove
\(Z^X_{\mathrm{OP}}=-(\chi_{10}^{\mathrm{OP}})^{-1}\), the theta
normalization gives
\[
Z^X_{\mathrm{OP}}=-4096\Delta_5^{-2}.
\]
Oberdieck's reduced DT/PT comparison and the primitive
Oberdieck--Pandharipande comparison give the same branch for
\(Z^X_{\mathrm{DT}}\).

The compact comparison is not used in these proofs.  It is precisely
Open Problem~\ref{op:compact-igusa-realization}.  The
\(\operatorname{Ran}(E)\) obstruction follows because a positive
elliptic-degree curve has one-dimensional image in the irreducible
curve \(E\), hence image \(E\); support separation on disjoint opens of
\(\operatorname{Ran}(E)\) cannot see such a sector.  The orientation
statement follows from the automorphic character computation for
\(\Delta_5\) and from the definition of a compact orientation datum;
rescaling \(\Delta_5\) by \(64^{-1}\) changes no character.  The
primitive recognition statement is the universal property of the
Borcherds--Kac presentation recorded in the denominator-algebra section.
The determinant and scalar square do not contain the missing
presentation, orientation, or Hall correspondence data.  The row
certificate condition is the same separation applied to the
Clery--Gritsenko catalogue in the next part.
\end{proof}

\part{Diagonal-divisor rows and CHL boundary physics}

\section{Eight diagonal-divisor rows: automorphic and physical status}
\label{sec:eight-dd-rows-status}

The Clery--Gritsenko catalogue gives eight
diagonal-divisor automorphic products.  The Gritsenko--Nikulin and
Govindarajan theorems promote these products to denominator identities
in the rows where the Weyl data are known.  A CHL dyon square, a reduced
CY/DT scalar host, and a compact Hall/chiral host are further structures,
recorded only where their data have been specified.

$$g=2.$$
$$t,N \in \mathbb{Z}_+:\quad \Gamma_t(N) =
\{\begin{pmatrix}*&*t&*&*\\*&*&*&*t^{-1}\\*N&*Nt&*&*\\*Nt&*Nt&*t&*\end{pmatrix}
\in \Sp_4(\mathbb{Q})\mid *\in\mathbb{Z}\}.$$
$$\mathbb H_2/\Gamma_t
\longleftrightarrow\{(1,t)\hbox{-polarized abelian surfaces}\}.$$
$$\mathcal H_{\mathrm{diag}}
=\left\{\begin{pmatrix}a&0\\0&b\end{pmatrix}\mid
a,b\in\mathbb{H}_1\right\}\subset\mathbb{H}_2.$$

\begin{definition}[Physical-host certificate]
\label{def:physical-host-certificate}
For a diagonal-divisor row \(F_j\), a physical-host certificate is a
five-level certificate table
\[
\mathfrak C_j=
\left(
\mathscr A_j,\mathscr D_j,\mathscr S_j,\mathscr Z_j,\mathscr H_j
\right).
\]
The entries have the following meanings.
\begin{enumerate}
\item \(\mathscr A_j\) is the automorphic product certificate: the form
\(F_j\), the group or multiplier cover, the automorphy cocycle, the
character or multiplier with exact order, the diagonal divisor with
multiplicities, the product chamber and branch, the Jacobi input at
every cusp, the product-degree map, the product normalization, and the
source theorem.
\item \(\mathscr D_j\) is the denominator certificate: a
Weyl--Kac--Borcherds denominator algebra with root lattice, Weyl vector,
simple real roots, Weyl chamber, Weyl group, reflection character,
imaginary simple-root coefficients, product side, and Weyl alternating
side.
\item \(\mathscr S_j\) is a CHL/dyon-square certificate: a sourced
dyon-counting scalar form \(\Phi_j\), a row map to the same automorphic
row and cover, and an identity \(F_j^2=\Phi_j\) in the stated chamber.
This is not a denominator theorem and not a CY/DT partition theorem.
\item \(\mathscr Z_j\) is a reduced CY/DT scalar-host certificate: a
compact Calabi--Yau threefold, orbifold Calabi--Yau, or CHL background
with oriented reduced obstruction theory, fixed variables and chamber,
and a proved identity
\[
Z^{X_j}_{\mathrm{red}}(Z)=C_jF_j(Z)^{-2}.
\]
\item \(\mathscr H_j\) is a compact Hall/chiral certificate: an oriented
compact Hall, Drinfeld, or factorization object whose protected
one-particle index gives the product exponents and whose protected
primitive bracket identifies the denominator algebra with the same
orientation/reflection character.
\end{enumerate}
The product row, denominator row, dyon square, reduced scalar host, and
compact Hall/chiral host are separate structures.  None of the five
entries implies another unless a cited theorem constructs the implication.
In particular, matching a weight, a square root, or a comparison symbol
does not fill a certificate.  A row-map theorem must name the host,
charge lattice, effective chamber, modular group or cover, product
lattice, orientation character, one-particle index, scalar identity when
claimed, and primitive Hall/chiral comparison.
\end{definition}

\begin{theorem}[Clery--Gritsenko]
In the class of Siegel modular forms with character or multiplier system
for the Hecke-type congruence subgroups $\Gamma_t(N)$ whose divisor is
the union of the $\Gamma_t(N)$-translates of $\mathcal H_{\mathrm{diag}}$
with multiplicity one, there are exactly eight rows
\cite[Theorem 1.4]{GC}.  The nine-candidate list is
\cite[Proposition 1.2]{GC}; the proof of Theorem 1.4 excludes only
the ninth candidate \((t,N;k)=(2,4;\frac12)\).  The congruence
Borcherds product with all
cusp coefficients is \cite[Theorem 3.1]{GC}, with the final Section 3
product displays for $\nabla_3,\nabla_2,\nabla_{3/2}$, and $Q_1$.
\end{theorem}

$$
\begin{array}{c|c|c|c|c}
j&F_j&\Gamma&\mathrm{wt}(F_j)&\mathrm{character/multiplier}\\ \hline
1&\Delta_5&\Gamma_1&5&v_\eta^{12}\times v_H\\
2&\Delta_2&\Gamma_2^+&2&v_\eta^{6}\times v_H\\
3&\Delta_1&\Gamma_3^+&1&v_\eta^{4}\times v_H\\
4&\Delta_{1/2}&\Gamma_4^+&\frac12&v_\eta^{3}\times v_H\ (\mathrm{degree}\ 8)\\
5&\nabla_3&\Gamma_0^{(2)}(2)&3&\chi_2^{(2)}\times v_H\\
6&\nabla_2&\Gamma_0^{(2)}(3)&2&\chi_2^{(3)}\times v_H\\
7&\nabla_{3/2}&\Gamma_0^{(2)}(4)&\frac32&
\hbox{order-four multiplier } \chi_4^{(4)}\times v_H\\
8&Q_1&\Gamma_2(2)&1&\chi_4^{(2)}\times v_H
\end{array}
$$
$$\operatorname{supp}\operatorname{div}_{\mathbb H_2}(F_j)
=\bigcup_{\gamma\in\Gamma_j}\gamma\langle\mathcal H_{\mathrm{diag}}\rangle,
\qquad
\operatorname{mult}_{\mathcal H_{\mathrm{diag}}}(F_j)=1.$$

$$F_1=\Delta_5,\qquad
\frac1{64}F_1(2Z)=\operatorname{den}(\autcor).$$

\begin{center}
\begingroup
\setlength{\tabcolsep}{3pt}
\scriptsize
\begin{tabular}{@{}c p{0.14\textwidth} p{0.16\textwidth} p{0.16\textwidth} p{0.17\textwidth} p{0.17\textwidth}@{}}

sourced scalar dyon square \(F_7^2=\Phi_3\) only after fixing the

no reduced CY/DT certificate &
